Zakat — Almsgiving
beginner
6 min
Definition and Conditions of Zakat Obligation
Definition and conditions of zakat obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of zakat, identify the five conditions for its obligation, and explain why it is not obligatory on minors or the insane.

Core Idea
Zakat is a transfer of ownership to the poor, not mere permission; it is not obligatory on minors or the insane.

Zakat is a pillar of Islam and a financial worship. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq defines zakat precisely and lists the conditions for its obligation. A key point of contention among schools is whether zakat applies to the property of minors and the insane. The Hanafi school, relying on the hadith 'the pen is lifted,' holds that it does not, while Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees.

Guided Path
1
Dissect the definition
Break down the definition of zakat: 'tamlik al-mal bi-ghayr 'iwad min faqir muslim ghayr hashimi...' Identify each key term: tamlik, mal, 'iwad, faqir, muslim, ghayr hashimi.
Understand the legal implications of each qualifier.
2
Identify the conditions of obligation
From the text, find the five conditions (shurut al-wujub): sanity, puberty, freedom, possession of nisab, and passage of a lunar year. Note that the text explicitly mentions 'aql and bulugh as conditions, implying the other three are assumed.
These conditions determine who must pay zakat.
3
Analyze the dispute on minors and insane
The text presents the Shafi'i objection that zakat is a financial duty like maintenance. Follow the Hanafi response based on the hadith 'رفع القلم عن ثلاثة' and the distinction between 'ibada and financial obligations.
This is a classic example of inter-madhhab ikhtilaf rooted in usul.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in Hanafi practice, a guardian is not required to pay zakat from a minor's property; in Shafi'i, it is obligatory.
This affects actual fatwa and practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكاة
تعريف الزكاة
هي تمليك المال بغير عوض من فقير مسلم غير هاشمي ولا مولاه بشرط قطع المنفعة أي الزكاة
احترز به عن الغني المحترز به عن

بكسر اللام وهو الدافع

الثاني
كتاب الزكاة: ذكر الزكاة بعد الصلاة تأسياً بما ذكر الله في آي من القرآن، وبما جاء به من السنة؛ لقوله عليه: بني" الإسلام على خمس إلخ، وقدم الصلاة؛ لأنها تجب على جميع البالغين العاقلين بخلاف الزكاة. والزكاة فرضت في السنة الثانية من الهجرة كالصوم قبل ،فرضه وهي في اللغة النماء، يقال: زكا الزرع إذا نما وزاد، وسميت بها؛ لأنها سبب نماء المال بالخلف في الدنيا، والثواب في العقبى، وتعبر عن الطهارة أيضاً، قال الله تعالى: وَحَنَانَا مِنْ لَدُنَّا وَزَكَاةً (مرم: ۱۳) أي طهارة، سميت بها؛ لأنها تطهر المزكي عن الذنوب. (عيني، فتح) تمليك المال: أي جزء منه وخرج بالتمليك الإباحة وبالمال المنفعة فلو أطعم يتيما ناويا الزكاة أو أسكن فقيرا داره سنة لم تجز (ط). تمليك المال بغير عوض كان الواجب أن يقول تمليك المال على وجه لابد منه حتى لا ترد الكفارة إذا ملكت؛ لأن التمليك بغير عوض موجود فيها، حتى أنها تؤدى بالإباحة بخلاف الزكاة رمز الحقائق: ١١٦/١] (وعيني) والفرق بين التمليك والإباحة أن في التمليك يملك الفقير التصرف فيه بما شاء، وفي الإباحة لا يملك التصرف غير أن يأكل، وأيضاً في إباحة الطعام ليس مقدار الإطعام معيناً، سواء شبع بنصف صاع، أو أقل، بخلاف التمليك، فإنه لا يجوز بأقل من نصف صاع. (محشي)
من
من
فقير: قيد إيتاء الزكاة بالفقير؛ لأنه لا يجوز إيتاؤها للأغنياء، وقيد بالمسلم؛ لأنها لا يجوز إيتاؤها للفقير الكافر؛ لقوله عليها: "خذها أغنيائهم وردها إلى فقرائهم أي المسلمين وقيد بقوله : "غير" هاشمي"؛ لأن الصدقة محرمة على بني هاشم؛ لقوله عليه: "يا معشر بني هاشم، إن الله تعالى حرم عليكم غسالة الناس وأوساخهم، وعوضكم منها بخمس الخمس"، ولا يجوز إيتاؤها لمولى الهاشمي أيضاً؛ لأن مولى القوم منهم - كما ورد في الحديث. (مستخلص) غير هاشمي: أي منسوباً إلى بني هاشم وهم آل علي وآل عباس، وآل عقيل وآل جعفر، وآل حارث بن عبد المطلب رمز الحقائق: ۱۱٥/١] ولا مولاه أي مولا هاشم أي معتقه بفتح التاء. وجه احتراز عن الدفع إلى فروعه وإن سفلوا، وإلى أصوله وإن علوا، وعن دفع أحد الزوجين إلى الآخر؛ فإن المنفعة لا تنقطع عن الدافع بالكلية في هذه الصور. الله تعالى: [متعلق بقوله: "تمليك المال" أي يكون مع الإخلاص لله (ع)] إشارة إلى وجوب النية؛ لتصير خالصة الله تعالى وليقع التميز بين العبادة والعادة. (مستخلص) وجوبها: أي افتراضها؛ لأنها تثبت بدليل مقطوع به وهو الكتاب والسنة والشرائط خمسة. (ع) العقل والبلوغ هذان شرط عندنا، وقال الشافعي واجبة عليهما؛ لأنها حق مالي، فيجب في مالهما، كنفقة الزوجات والعشر والخراج ولنا قوله عليا: رفع القلم عن ثلاثة (الحديث)، وهما ليسا بمخاطبين بالعبادة، فلا تجب عليهما -
Book of Zakat: Definition of Zakat: It is the transfer of ownership of wealth without compensation from a poor Muslim, non-Hashimi nor his client, with the condition of complete severance of benefit from the transferor for the sake of Allah. Conditions of its obligation: sanity and puberty. ...
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling explaining the legal definition of zakat and the conditions for its obligation. The author defines zakat as transferring ownership of wealth (tamlik al-mal) without compensation to a specific recipient. He qualifies the recipient: a poor Muslim, not a Hashimi nor the client (mawla) of a Hashimi, with the condition that the benefit is completely cut off from the giver. The commentary elaborates on each part: 'tamlik' excludes mere permission (ibaha), and 'mal' excludes usufruct. It also explains that the recipient must be poor (faqir), Muslim, and non-Hashimi (including the descendants of Ali, Abbas, etc.) due to the hadith that sadaqa is forbidden to the Hashimis, who are compensated by khums. The conditions for obligation (shurut al-wujub) are sanity and puberty. The passage then records a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that zakat is obligatory on minors and the insane because it is a financial duty like maintenance. The Hanafi response is based on the hadith 'The pen is lifted from three' – minors and the insane are not addressed by worship obligations. Thus, zakat is not obligatory on them in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الزكاة (al-zakat): Transfer of ownership of wealth without compensation to a qualified recipient for the sake of Allah, purifying the giver.
تمليك المال (tamlik al-mal): Transfer of ownership of wealth; the giver must give the poor full ownership of a specific part of wealth, not just the benefit.
فقير (faqir): A poor person who does not own the nisab; the recipient of zakat must be poor.
هاشمي (Hashimi): A descendant of Hashim (the Prophet's clan), including Al 'Ali, Al 'Abbas, etc.; they cannot receive zakat.
شروط الوجوب (shurut al-wujub): Conditions for the obligation of zakat: sanity, puberty, freedom, nisab, and hawliyya (passage of one year).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a condition (shart) for the obligation of zakat?
A) Sanity
B) Puberty
C) Being a non-Hashimi recipient
D) Possession of nisab

Key Takeaway
Zakat is obligatory only on sane, adult, free Muslims who possess nisab for one year; the property of minors and the insane is not subject to zakat in the Hanafi school.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate

The Hanafi Legal Definition of Zakat
Defines zakat lexically and legally with conditions and exclusions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi legal definition of zakat and identify its conditions, exclusions, and practical implications.

Core Idea
Zakat is a compulsory transfer of ownership to specific recipients with complete severance of benefit.

This lesson examines the precise legal definition of zakat as formulated by the Hanafi school. The definition is not merely academic—each word carries a specific legal condition that determines validity. Understanding this definition is the foundation for correctly calculating and discharging your zakat obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic and legal definitions
Note that the passage begins with the literal meaning (growth) and then gives the legal meaning (transfer of ownership). The legal definition is the operative one for fiqh.
The shift from linguistic to legal is typical in Hanafi texts.
2
Break down the legal definition into components
The definition contains: tamlik (transfer of ownership), no compensation, recipient is needy Muslim non-Hashimi (and not his freed slave), and condition of complete severance of benefit (qaṭʿ al-manfaʿah).
Each component is a necessary condition.
3
Understand the exclusions (ihtirazāt)
The passage explicitly excludes the rich, the kafir, the Hashimi, the freed slave of a Hashimi, and one's own dependents (ascendants, descendants, spouse) because benefit is not completely severed.
These exclusions are derived from the definition's restrictions.
4
Appreciate the conditions of validity
Tamlik is required, not mere ibahah (permission). Complete severance of benefit means the donor must not retain any direct benefit from the given wealth.
This distinguishes zakat from other charitable acts.
5
Note the necessity of niyyah
The phrase 'for the sake of Allah' indicates that intention is required to make the act worship, not just a mundane transfer.
Niyyah is a pillar in Hanafi zakat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكاة. تعريف الزكاة: تمليك المال بغير عوض من فقير مسلم غير هاشمي ولا مولاه بشرط قطع المنفعة. الزكاة لغة: النماء. وشرعاً: تمليك المال بغير عوض من فقير مسلم غير هاشمي ولا مولاه بشرط قطع المنفعة. احترز به عن الغني، وعن الكافر، وعن الهاشمي ومولاه، وعن الدفع إلى الفروع والأصول والزوجين؛ فإن المنفعة لا تنقطع بالكلية. قيد التمليك احترازاً عن الإباحة؛ فإن الإباحة لا تجزي في الزكاة. وشرط قطع المنفعة احترازاً عن دفع الزكاة لمن تلزمه نفقته ونحوه. وقوله: الله تعالى إشارة إلى وجوب النية؛ لتصير خالصة لله.
Book of Zakat. Definition of Zakat: Transfer of ownership of wealth without compensation from a needy Muslim, non-Hashimi, and not the freed slave of a Hashimi, with the condition of complete severance of benefit. Literally, zakat means growth. Legally, it is the transfer of ownership of wealth without compensation from a needy Muslim, non-Hashimi, and not the freed slave of a Hashimi, with the condition of complete severance of benefit. This excludes the rich, the disbeliever, the Hashimi and his freed slave, and payment to one's descendants, ancestors, and spouses, because benefit is not completely severed. The condition of transfer of ownership excludes mere permission (ibahah), which is not sufficient for zakat. The condition of complete severance of benefit excludes payment to those for whom he is obliged to provide maintenance and the like. The phrase 'for the sake of Allah' indicates the necessity of intention (niyyah) to make the act purely for Allah.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage defines zakat both linguistically and legally. Linguistically, 'zakat' means growth and increase. Legally, it is the transfer of ownership of a portion of one's wealth to a specific category of recipients, without compensation, for the sake of Allah. The definition includes several restrictions: the recipient must be needy (faqir), Muslim, and not a Hashimi (descendant of Hashim) or the freed slave of a Hashimi. Additionally, the donor must completely sever benefit from the wealth given; therefore, zakat cannot be given to one's own dependents or spouse, as benefit is shared. The definition excludes mere permission to use the wealth (ibahah), as zakat requires actual transfer of ownership. The phrase 'for the sake of Allah' emphasizes the necessity of intention (niyyah) to distinguish worship from habit. The Hanafi school stresses these conditions to ensure the zakat fulfills its purpose of purifying wealth.

Key Terms
تمليك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership, as opposed to mere permission (ibahah).
فقير (faqir): A needy person who does not possess the nisab or sufficient wealth to meet basic needs.
هاشمي (hashimi): A descendant of the Banu Hashim, including the families of Ali, Abbas, Aqil, Ja'far, and Harith ibn Abd al-Muttalib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for the recipient of zakat according to the definition?
A) Must be needy
B) Must be Muslim
C) Must be a Hashimi
D) Must not be the freed slave of a Hashimi

Key Takeaway
Zakat in Hanafi fiqh requires actual transfer of ownership to a qualified recipient with complete severance of benefit, and intention for Allah.

Conditions of Zakat: Sanity and Puberty (Hanafi vs. Shafi'i)
Establishes sanity and puberty as conditions for zakat obligation, with Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on zakat obligation for minors and the insane, and explain the key proof and rebuttal to the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Zakat is not obligatory on minors or the insane because they lack legal responsibility.

This lesson explores a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: whether zakat is obligatory on the wealth of minors and the insane. The Hanafi school holds that sanity and puberty are conditions for zakat, while the Shafi'i school disagrees. We will examine the proofs on both sides and understand the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: the Hanafi school requires sanity and puberty for zakat to be obligatory. The insane and minors are not obligated.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that zakat is obligatory on the wealth of minors and the insane, by analogy to nafaqah and ushr.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i analogical argument: zakat is a financial right like nafaqah, which is due on wealth regardless of the owner's capacity.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand why the Hanafis reject this analogy: zakat is an act of worship requiring intention (niyyah), unlike nafaqah which is a human right and does not require niyyah.
The hadith 'رفع القلم عن ثلاثة' is also cited as evidence that minors and insane are not addressed.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, a Hanafi mufti would rule that no zakat is due on a minor's wealth, whereas a Shafi'i mufti would require the guardian to pay.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشرط وجوبها: العقل والبلوغ. هذان شرط عندنا، وقال الشافعي واجبة عليهما؛ لأنها حق مالي، فيجب في مالهما، كنفقة الزوجات والعشر والخراج. ولنا قوله عليه السلام: «رفع القلم عن ثلاثة» الحديث، وهما ليسا بمخاطبين بالعبادة، فلا تجب عليهما. والنفقة ونحوها حقوق العباد، ولهذا تتأدى بدون النية، وكذا العشر؛ ولهذا يجب على المكاتب، وفي أرض الوقف. ولأن من شرطها النية، وهي لا تتحقق منهما، ولا تعتبر نية الولي؛ لأن العبادة لا تتأدى بنية الغير؛ ولأن ملكهما ناقص ولا يملكان التصرف فكيف ينمو مالهما، وهي لا تجب إلا في المال النامي.
And the conditions of its obligation are: sanity and puberty. These two are conditions according to us (Hanafis). Al-Shafi'i said it is obligatory upon them (the minor and insane) because it is a financial right, so it is obligatory upon their wealth, like the maintenance of wives, the tithe (ushr), and the land tax (kharaj). Our proof is his statement (peace be upon him): 'The pen is lifted from three' (the hadith), and they are not addressed for worship, so it is not obligatory upon them. Maintenance (nafaqah) and similar are rights of human beings, and therefore they are fulfilled without intention (niyyah); likewise the tithe, and therefore it is obligatory upon a mukatab and upon land of waqf. And because among its conditions is intention, which is not realized from them (the minor and insane), and the intention of the guardian is not considered, because worship is not fulfilled by the intention of another; and because their ownership is deficient and they do not have the right to dispose of property, so how can their wealth grow? And zakat is not obligatory except upon growing wealth.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage discusses the first two conditions for zakat obligation: sanity (`aql) and puberty (bulugh). The Hanafi school holds these as necessary because zakat is an act of worship, and the insane and minors are not legally responsible (mukallaf). Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that zakat is a financial obligation similar to nafaqah and ushr, which are due on the wealth of such individuals. The Hanafis respond with the hadith 'the pen is lifted from three' (the sleeping, the minor, and the insane), indicating they are not addressed by divine commands. Furthermore, nafaqah and ushr are rights of human beings, not purely acts of worship, and they do not require intention. Zakat requires intention (niyyah), which cannot be validly performed by an insane person or minor, and the guardian's intention does not substitute. Additionally, the ownership of such individuals is deficient; they cannot freely dispose of their property, so their wealth is not considered 'growing' in the required sense. Therefore, zakat is not obligatory on them.

Key Terms
العقل (al-'aql): Sanity, the mental capacity to understand and be addressed by divine commands.
البلوغ (al-bulugh): Puberty, the age of legal majority, when one becomes responsible for religious duties.
القلم مرفوع (al-qalam marfu'): A hadith meaning that the minor, insane, and sleeping are not held accountable for their actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Hanafi proof for not obligating zakat on minors and the insane?
A) Their wealth is not sufficient
B) The hadith 'رفع القلم عن ثلاثة'
C) They are not Muslims
D) Their guardians should pay instead

Key Takeaway
Sanity and puberty are conditions for zakat in the Hanafi school; this is based on the hadith 'رفع القلم' and the nature of zakat as worship requiring intention.

Conditions of Zakat: Islam and Freedom
Ruling with proof: two conditions of zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that Islam and freedom are conditions for zakat obligation and explain why a slave, including a mukatab, is exempt based on Hanafi proofs.

Core Idea
Zakat is only obligatory on a free Muslim; a slave's ownership is incomplete, so no zakat.

We continue with the conditions of zakat. Having covered time and the passing of a year, we now turn to two personal conditions of the payer: Islam and freedom. The passage establishes that a non-Muslim is not obligated because worship requires faith, and a slave is not obligated because his ownership is not full. Even a mukatab, though he may possess wealth, has incomplete ownership due to the risk of reversion. Let us examine the proofs and reasoning behind these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
List the conditions: Islam (third condition) and freedom (fourth condition). Understand that each is a prerequisite for the obligation of zakat.
Islam is a general condition for all acts of worship; freedom specifically affects ownership capacity.
2
Understand the ruling for each condition
For a non-Muslim: zakat is not obligatory because the act of worship is not valid without faith. For a slave: zakat is not obligatory because he does not fully own property.
The slave's lack of full ownership is key; his wealth belongs to the master.
3
Analyze the proof for the slave's exemption
The hadith 'لا صدقة إلا عن ظهر غنى' (no charity except from surplus wealth) is cited. Explain how a slave has no surplus because his property is not his own.
This hadith is ahad, so it gives zanni certainty, but it is sufficient for this ruling.
4
Extend the ruling to the mukatab
A mukatab (slave under contract of manumission) has some ownership, but it is incomplete because his wealth is shared: if he fails to pay, it goes to the master. Thus, he is also exempt.
The Hanafi school distinguishes this from the Shafi'i view, where the mukatab is considered owner and zakat might be due.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإسلام أي الثالث فلا تجب على الكافر؛ لأن الإسلام شرط لصحة العبادات كلها. والحرية أي الرابع فلا تجب على الرقيق؛ لعدم تحقق التمليك. فلا تجب على العبد؛ لعدم ملكه، وقد قال عليه السلام: «لا صدقة إلا عن ظهر غنى» ولا غنى للعبد، ولو مكاتباً؛ لأنه وإن ثبت له الملك إلا أنه ليس بكامل؛ لوجود المنافي، وهو الرق؛ ولأن المال الذي في يده دائر بينه وبين المولى، فإن أدى مال الكتابة سلم له، وإن عجز سلم للمولى، فكما لا يجب على المولى فيه شيء فكذلك لا يجب على المكاتب.
And Islam, i.e., the third condition, so it is not obligatory upon the disbeliever, because Islam is a condition for the validity of all acts of worship. And freedom, i.e., the fourth condition, so it is not obligatory upon the slave, because ownership is not fully realized. So it is not obligatory upon the slave, because he does not own property, and he (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no charity except from surplus of wealth,' and a slave has no surplus. Even if he is a mukatab (slave under contract of manumission), because even though he has ownership, it is incomplete due to the existence of the impediment, which is slavery; and because the wealth in his hand is shared between him and his master. If he pays the kitabah, it becomes his; if he fails, it goes to the master. So just as nothing is obligatory upon the master, likewise nothing is obligatory upon the mukatab.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage covers the third and fourth conditions for zakat: Islam and freedom. Zakat is an act of worship, and Islam is a prerequisite for the validity of all worship; hence, a non-Muslim is not obligated to pay zakat. As for freedom, a slave does not fully own property; his wealth belongs to his master. The hadith 'لا صدقة إلا عن ظهر غنى' indicates that zakat is only due from surplus wealth, and a slave has no surplus because his master owns everything. Even a mukatab (a slave who has contracted to buy his freedom) has incomplete ownership; his earnings are shared with his master until the contract is fulfilled. Therefore, zakat is not obligatory upon any slave, including a mukatab.

Key Terms
الحرية (al-hurriyah): Freedom; being a free person, not a slave.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has a written contract to purchase his freedom by paying installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is zakat not obligatory upon a mukatab according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because he is not a Muslim
B) Because his ownership is incomplete and shared with his master
C) Because he does not possess the nisab
D) Because the master pays on his behalf

Key Takeaway
Islam and freedom are essential conditions for zakat; a slave, including a mukatab, is exempt because his ownership is not fully realized.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
10 min
Condition of Zakat: Debt Prevents Obligation
Defines nisab, hawl, and the debt condition, with Shafi'i dispute on debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for zakat obligation and explain why the Hanafi school considers debt as a preventer, distinguishing it from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Zakat is only due on surplus wealth; debt cancels the nisab in Hanafi fiqh.

Zakat is a pillar of Islam, but its obligation depends on precise conditions. The Hanafi school adds a critical condition: the wealth must be free from debt. This lesson unpacks the nisab and hawl conditions, then focuses on the debt dispute with the Shafi'i school, revealing a fundamental difference in how surplus wealth is defined.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi conditions for zakat
List the three conditions discussed in the passage: ownership of nisab, passage of a lunar year (hawl), and freedom from debt.
Note that hawl applies to most wealth but not to crops.
2
Examine the Shafi'i objection
Understand that al-Shafi'i argues debt does not prevent zakat because the cause (nisab and growth) is present.
The Shafi'i position is that zakat is due on owned wealth regardless of liability.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Review the Hanafi dalil: zakat is on surplus wealth; debt makes wealth effectively non-existent. Supported by Companions' consensus and qiyas with a mukatab.
The analogy to mukatab highlights deficient ownership.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Apply both views to a concrete scenario: a person has 200 dirhams cash and 200 dirhams debt. Hanafi: no zakat. Shafi'i: zakat due.
This practical difference affects millions of Muslims annually.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Recognize that the Hanafi position is mufta bihi due to the strength of the Companions' practice and logical consistency.
The tarjih is based on ijma' and qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وملك نصاب: أي شرط وجوبها نصاب مملوك. والنصاب ما عينه الشارع سبباً للزكاة كمائتي درهم في الفضة، وعشرين مثقالاً في الذهب، وخمسة في الإبل، وثلاثين في البقرة، ولا تجب في أقل من النصاب. وقوله: حولي: اشتراط الحول مخصوص بما عدا زكاة الزرع والثمار. وإنما اشترط حولان الحول؛ لأن النماء شرط، وهو باطن، فأدير الحكم على زمان يتحقق فيه النمو، وهو الحول؛ لاشتماله على الفصول الأربع. حولي: صفة للنصاب أي حال عليه الحول؛ لقوله عليه السلام: «لا زكاة في مال حتى يحول عليه الحول». فارغ عن الدين: أي لو كان عليه دين يحيط بماله منع عن إيجاب الزكاة. كدين استهلاك، ومهر ولو مؤجلاً، وعشر، وخراج، ونفقة قريب وزوجة قضى بها، وكذا دين الزكاة بعد الوجوب. وقال الشافعي لا يمنع؛ لتحقق سبب الوجوب، وهو ملك نصاب نام. ولنا: أن الزكاة إنما تجب في المال الفاضل عن الحاجة، ومال المديون ليس كذلك. فاعتبر بقدر دينه معدوماً. وهو قول عثمان وابن عباس وابن عمر، وكان عثمان يقول: «هذا شهر زكاتكم، فمن كان عليه دين فليؤد دينه حتى تخلص أمواله فيؤدى منها الزكاة» وكان ذلك بمحضر من الصحابة من غير نكير، فكان إجماعاً. ولأن ملك المديون ناقص حيث كان للغريم أن يأخذ إذا ظفر بحبس حقه، فصار كمال المكاتب. وإن كان مالاً أكثر من دينه زكى الفاضل إذا بلغ نصاباً.
And ownership of nisab: meaning the condition of its obligation is ownership of a nisab. The nisab is what the Lawgiver has specified as a cause for zakat, like two hundred dirhams for silver, twenty mithqals for gold, five camels, thirty cows. And zakat is not obligatory for less than the nisab. And His saying: 'hawli' (yearly) – the condition of the passing of the year is specific to other than zakat of crops and fruits. The passing of the year is stipulated because growth is a condition, and it is hidden, so the ruling is attached to a time in which growth is realized, which is the year, because it includes the four seasons. 'Hawli' is an adjective for nisab, i.e., a year has passed over it, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'There is no zakat on wealth until a year passes over it.' Free from debt: meaning if he has a debt that encompasses his wealth, it prevents the obligation of zakat. Like a consumption debt, a dowry even if deferred, 'ushr, kharaj, and maintenance of a relative or wife that has been decreed, and likewise the debt of zakat after obligation. Al-Shafi'i said it does not prevent, because the cause of obligation is realized, which is ownership of a growing nisab. Our proof: zakat is only obligatory on wealth that is surplus to need, and the wealth of a debtor is not like that. So his wealth is considered non-existent to the extent of his debt. This is the statement of Uthman, Ibn Abbas, and Ibn Umar. Uthman used to say: 'This is the month of your zakat, so whoever has a debt should pay his debt until his wealth becomes clear, then pay zakat from it.' This was in the presence of Companions without any objection, so it was a consensus. And because the ownership of the debtor is deficient, since the creditor can seize his right when he finds it, so it becomes like the ownership of a mukatab. If his wealth exceeds his debt, he pays zakat on the surplus if it reaches a nisab.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage explains the fifth condition for zakat: ownership of a nisab that has passed a lunar year and is free from debt. The nisab is the minimum threshold set by Shariah: 200 dirhams of silver, 20 mithqals of gold, 5 camels, 30 cows, etc. The condition of a complete year (hawl) applies to livestock, gold, silver, and trade goods, but not to crops and fruits, which are zakatable at harvest. The year is required because growth is hidden and the four seasons allow for increase. The hadith 'لا زكاة في مال حتى يحول عليه الحول' supports this. The additional condition that the wealth be free from debt is uniquely Hanafi; debts that fully encumber the wealth prevent zakat. Examples include personal loans, unpaid dowry, kharaj, and decreed maintenance. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that the cause of zakat (nisab and growth) is present regardless of debt. The Hanafi response: zakat is due on surplus wealth; debt renders the wealth effectively non-existent. This view is supported by the practice of Caliph Uthman and other Companions, amounting to a tacit consensus. Hanafis analogize the debtor's ownership to that of a mukatab (deficient ownership). If the remaining wealth after debt repayment reaches nisab, zakat is obligatory on the surplus.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth set by Shariah for zakat to become obligatory.
حول (hawl): The passage of one lunar year on the wealth.
دين (dayn): A debt owed by the zakat payer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person has 200 dirhams of silver but also owes 200 dirhams in debt?
A) Zakat is obligatory on the full 200 dirhams
B) Zakat is not obligatory because the debt cancels the nisab
C) Zakat is obligatory only if the debt is due immediately
D) Zakat is obligatory on 100 dirhams only

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, zakat is not due on wealth fully encumbered by debt, as zakat is a right on surplus wealth only.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
10 min
The Five Conditions for Zakat Obligation
Enumerates and proves five conditions for zakat obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions for zakat obligation according to the Hanafi school and apply the debt condition to determine zakat liability in a given scenario.

Core Idea
Zakat is only obligatory if the wealth is free from debt — the Hanafi school considers debt a preventative condition.

Zakat is not a simple tax on any wealth. The Lawgiver has laid down precise conditions that must all be met before zakat becomes due. In this passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, the author enumerates five prerequisites: being Muslim, being free, owning a minimum threshold (nisab), the passage of a full year (hawl), and the wealth being free from debt. We will unpack each condition, examine its proof, and especially analyse the debated issue of debt blocking zakat.

Guided Path
1
List the five conditions
From the text, extract the five conditions: Islam, freedom, nisab, hawl, and freedom from debt. Note that these are shurut al-wujub (prerequisites for obligation), not pillars of the act.
The conditions are mentioned in a concise list: "والإسلام، والحرية، وملك نصاب حولي فارغ عن الدين"
2
Examine the reasoning for conditions 1-2 (Islam and Freedom)
Understand why zakat is not obligatory on a disbeliever (Islam is a condition for all worship) and on a slave (lack of complete ownership). Even a mukatab slave does not have full ownership, so zakat is not due.
The text uses the hadith 'No charity except from surplus wealth' to justify the freedom condition.
3
Define nisab and hawl with their proofs
Identify the specific nisab amounts (200 dirhams silver, 20 mithqals gold, 5 camels, 30 cows). For hawl, note the hadith 'No zakat on wealth until a year passes' and the rationale that the year encompasses growth seasons.
Hawl is not required for crops and fruits; that is a specific exception.
4
Analyse the debt condition and its dispute
Read the Hanafi proof for debt blocking zakat: the practice of Caliph Uthman and consensus, analogy to a mukatab's incomplete ownership. Contrast with the Shafi'i objection that the cause (nisab) is present.
The Hanafi position is that wealth up to the debt is considered non-existent; only surplus is zakatable.
5
Apply the conditions to a practical case
Synthesize all conditions: take a scenario of a Muslim with 300 dirhams for a year but a debt of 150 dirhams. Rule that zakat is not due because the debt reduces the effective nisab. Then adjust: if debt is 50 dirhams, zakat is due on 250 dirhams if it reaches nisab.
This step uses the mufta bihi Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكاة
۱۸۹
شرائط وجوبها
والإسلام، والحرية، وملك نصاب حولي فارغ عن الدين،
الثالث
الرابع الخامس
والنفقة ونحوها حقوق العباد ؛ ولهذا تتأدى بدون النية، وكذا العشر؛ ولهذا يجب على المكاتب، وفي أرض الوقف. [ رمز الحقائق: ١١٦/١] ولأن من شرطها النية، وهي لا تتحقق منهما، ولا تعتبر نية الولي؛ لأن العبادة لا تتأدى بنية الغير؛ ولأن ملكهما ناقص ولا يملكان التصرف فكيف ينمو مالهما، وهي لا تجب إلا في المال النامي. (عيني، فتح) والإسلام أي الثالث فلا تجب على الكافر؛ لأن الإسلام شرط لصحة العبادات كلها [رمز الحقائق: ١١٦/١] والحرية [ أي الرابع فلا تجب على الرقيق؛ لعدم تحقق التمليك. (ع)] فلا تجب على العبد؛ لعدم ملكه، وقد قال عليه: "لا صدقة إلا عن ظهر غنى" ولا غنى للعبد، ولو مكاتباً؛ لأنه وإن ثبت له الملك إلا أنه ليس بكامل؛ لوجود المنافي، وهو الرق؛ ولأن المال الذي في يده دائر بينه وبين المولى، فإن أدى مال الكتابة سلم له، وإن عجز سلم للمولى، فكما لا يجب على المولى فيه شيء فكذلك لا يجب على المكاتب. (مستخلص، فتح) وملك نصاب من إضافة الصفة إلى الموصوف أي شرط وجوبها نصاب مملوك، أو من إضافة المصدر إلى مفعوله أي وملك المكلف نصابا. والنصاب ما عينه الشارع سبباً للزكاة كمائتي درهم في الفضة، وعشرين مثقالا في الذهب، وخمسة في الإبل، وثلاثين في البقرة، ولا تجب في أقل من النصاب، وقوله: "حولي" اشتراط الحول مخصوص بما عدا زكاة الزرع والثمار، وإنما اشترط حولان الحول؛ لأن النماء شرط، وهو باطن، فأدير الحكم على زمان يتحقق فيه النمو، وهو الحول؛ لاشتماله على الفصول الأربع التي لها تأثير في زيادة النفوذ بالبيع والشراء، وزيادة الأنعام بالدر والنسل، وزيادة القيمة في عروض التجارة باعتبار تفاوت الرغبات في كل فصل.
(فتح وغيره) نصاب : أي الخامس فلا تجب في أقل منه؛ لأن الشرع قدر السبب كمائي درهم مثلا. حولي: صفة للنصاب أي حال عليه الحول؛ لقوله : "لا زكاة في مال حتى يحول عليه الحول". (ع) فارغ عن الدين: أي لو كان عليه دين يحيط بماله وله مطالب من العباد إصالة أو كفالة، حالاً أو مؤجلا منع عن إيجاب الزكاة كدين استهلاك، ومهر ولو مؤجلا وعشر، وخراج ونفقة قريب وزوجة قضى بها، وكذا دين الزكاة بعد الوجوب؛ لأن له مطالباً من جهة العباد يعني الإمام في الأموال الظاهرة، ونوابه في الأموال الباطنة، والأموال الظاهرة أي المواشي، والمال على العاشر، والباطنة هي الذهب والفضة، وأموال التجارة في مواضعها وقال الشافعي لا يمنع؛ لتحقق سبب الوجوب، وهو ملك نصاب ،نام ولنا: أن الزكاة إنما تجب في المال الفاضل عن الحاجة، ومال المديون ليس كذلك، فاعتبر بقدر دينه معدوماً، وهو قول عثمان عفان منه بن وابن عباس ما، وابن عمر لهما، وكفى بهم قدوة، وكان عثمان الله يقول: "هذا شهر زكاتكم، فمن كان عليه دين فليؤد دينه حتى تخلص أمواله فيؤدى منها الزكاة وكان ذلك بمحضر من الصحابة من غير نكير، فكان إجماعاً؛ ولأن ملك المديون ناقص حيث كان للغريم أن يأخذ إذا ظفر بحبس حقه، فصار كمال المكاتب، وإن كان مالاً كثر من دينه زكى الفاضل إذا بلغ نصاباً. (مسكين، فتح)
The Book of Zakat. 189. Conditions of its obligation: Islam, freedom, ownership of a nisab (minimum threshold) that has passed a year and is free from debt. The third, fourth, fifth. And maintenance and similar are rights of servants; therefore they are performed without intention, and likewise the tithe; therefore it is obligatory on the mukatab slave and on waqf land. [Symbol of Realities: 116/1] And because intention is a condition for it, and it is not realized from them, and the intention of the guardian is not considered because worship is not performed by the intention of another; and because their ownership is incomplete and they do not have the right to dispose, so how can their wealth grow? And it is only obligatory on productive wealth. (Ayni, Fath) And Islam, i.e., the third: it is not obligatory on the disbeliever because Islam is a condition for the validity of all acts of worship. [Symbol of Realities: 116/1] And freedom, i.e., the fourth: it is not obligatory on the slave because of the lack of realization of ownership. (Ayni) It is not obligatory on the slave because he does not own; and the Prophet ﷺ said: 'No charity except from surplus wealth,' and the slave has no surplus. And even if he is a mukatab (slave contracted for freedom), because although ownership is established for him, it is not complete due to the presence of the impediment, which is slavery; and because the wealth in his hand is circulating between him and his master: if he pays the manumission money, it becomes his; if he fails, it becomes the master's. So just as nothing is obligatory on the master regarding it, likewise nothing is obligatory on the mukatab. (Mukhtasar al-Fath) And 'ownership of a nisab' can be read as adding the attribute to the described (i.e., the condition is an owned nisab) or as adding the source to its object (i.e., the obligated person owns a nisab). The nisab is what the Lawgiver designated as a cause for zakat: 200 dirhams in silver, 20 mithqals in gold, five camels, thirty cows. It is not obligatory on less than the nisab. His statement: 'one-year' — stipulating the year is specific to what is other than zakat of crops and fruits. The passing of the year is stipulated because growth is a condition and it is hidden, so the ruling is based on a period in which growth takes place, which is the year, due to its inclusion of the four seasons that affect increase: increase in wealth through buying and selling, increase in livestock through milk and offspring, and increase in value of trade goods due to variation in demand each season. (Fath and others) Nisab: i.e., the fifth: it is not obligatory on less than it because the Lawgiver determined the cause, such as 200 dirhams. One-year: an attribute of the nisab, i.e., a full year has passed over it, due to his statement: 'No zakat on wealth until a year passes over it.' (Ayni) Free from debt: i.e., if one has debt that encompasses his wealth, and he has claimants from people, whether original or as guarantor, whether immediate or deferred, it prevents the obligation of zakat — such as a consumption debt, dower (even if deferred), tithe, land tax, maintenance of a relative or a wife that has been decreed. Likewise, the debt of zakat itself after it becomes obligatory, because there is a claimant from the side of people, meaning the Imam for apparent wealth, and his deputies for hidden wealth. Apparent wealth is livestock and wealth upon the tax collector; hidden wealth is gold and silver and trade goods in their places. Al-Shafi'i said: debt does not prevent, because the cause of obligation is established: ownership of a nisab that is productive. Our evidence: that zakat is only obligatory on wealth that is surplus to need, and the debtor's wealth is not like that. Thus his wealth up to the extent of his debt is considered non-existent. This is the saying of 'Uthman ibn 'Affan, Ibn 'Abbas, and Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with them), and they suffice as role models. 'Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) used to say: 'This is your month of zakat; whoever has a debt should pay his debt so that his wealth becomes clear and then zakat is paid from it.' This was in the presence of the Companions without denial, so it was consensus. And because the ownership of the debtor is incomplete, since the creditor can take his due if he finds it, so it resembles the ownership of a mukatab. If the wealth exceeds the debt, he pays zakat on the surplus if it reaches a nisab. (Miskin, Fath)
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Book of Zakat in Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the five conditions (shurut) for the obligation of zakat. The author lists them: Islam, freedom, ownership of a nisab (minimum threshold), the passing of one full year (hawl), and the wealth being free from debt. Each condition is then elaborated with legal reasoning and proof texts.

1. Islam: Zakat is not obligatory on a disbeliever because Islam is a condition for all acts of worship; a disbeliever's acts are not accepted. This is a fundamental Hanafi principle.

2. Freedom: A slave does not own property, so zakat is not obligatory. Even a mukatab slave (who has a contract of manumission) does not have complete ownership because his wealth is contingent on paying his master; if he fails, the wealth goes to the master. Hence, zakat is not obligatory on him either, as the Prophet said: 'No charity except from surplus wealth.'

3. Ownership of a nisab: The nisab is the minimum amount set by the Lawgiver as a cause for zakat—200 dirhams for silver, 20 mithqals for gold, 5 camels, 30 cows, etc. Zakat is not obligatory on less than the nisab.

4. Passing of one year (hawl): The year is stipulated because growth (nama') is a condition for zakat, and it is hidden; the year is a period in which growth typically occurs, encompassing the four seasons that affect increases in wealth, livestock, and trade goods. This condition applies to all zakatable wealth except crops and fruits (which have their own rules). The proof is the hadith: 'No zakat on wealth until a year passes over it.'

5. Freedom from debt: If a person has debt that envelops his wealth (or reduces it below the nisab), zakat is not obligatory. This is because zakat is only obligatory on surplus wealth beyond need. The Hanafi school holds that debt prevents zakat, citing the practice of Caliph 'Uthman and consensus of Companions. Al-Shafi'i disagreed, arguing that the cause of obligation (nisab) is present. The Hanafi rebuttal: the debtor's ownership is incomplete, like that of a mukatab; the creditor has the right to seize the wealth. If the wealth exceeds the debt, zakat is paid on the surplus that reaches nisab.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth set by the Lawgiver as a threshold for zakat obligation, e.g., 200 dirhams for silver.
حول (hawl): The passing of one complete lunar year over the wealth, required for zakat on most types of wealth.
دين (dayn): Any financial liability or debt that reduces the net value of wealth, affecting zakat obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following conditions is disputed by Imam al-Shafi'i?
A) Islam
B) Freedom
C) Ownership of nisab
D) Freedom from debt

Key Takeaway
Zakat obligation depends on five conditions: Islam, freedom, nisab, hawl, and freedom from debt; debt prevents zakat entirely in Hanafi fiqh if it equals or exceeds the nisab.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
6 min
Conditions of Zakat Performance: Basic Needs, Growth, and Intention
Explains three conditions for zakat performance with legal definitions and exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for valid zakat performance according to the Hanafi school and apply them to distinguish zakatable from non-zakatable wealth.

Core Idea
Three conditions govern zakat performance: wealth free from basic needs, capable of growth, and accompanied by intention.

This lesson unpacks three essential conditions for performing zakat: the wealth must be surplus to basic needs (hajat asliyyah), it must be productive or capable of growth (nam), and the payment must be accompanied by intention (niyyah). Understanding these conditions ensures zakat is rendered correctly, distinguishing it from mere charity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
From the passage, list the three conditions for zakat performance: freedom from basic needs, productivity of nisab, and intention.
These are shurut ada' (conditions of performance) not shurut wujub (conditions of obligation).
2
Define 'basic needs' (hajat asliyyah)
Read the list of exempt items: dwelling, clothing, furniture, riding animals, service slaves, tools, books. Understand that these are exempt regardless of value.
This condition effectively replaces the 'free from debt' condition because the debtor's wealth is already tied to basic need.
3
Analyze 'productive' (nam) – actual and potential
Distinguish between real growth (breeding, trade) and notional growth (gold/silver inherently tradeable). Note that intention is not required for innate growth but required for actual growth via trade.
Mal al-dimar (lost/inaccessible wealth) has no zakat because it cannot grow.
4
Understand the role of intention (niyyah)
Intention must be present at payment or at setting aside. The recipient’s knowledge is irrelevant. Giving all wealth in charity without intention suffices if the entire wealth is given.
Niyyah distinguishes zakat from ordinary charity. It can be made at time of setting aside due to ease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرائط أدائها
وحاجته الأصلية، نام ولو تقديرا وشرط أدائها نية مقارنة للأداء أو لعزل ما وجب أو تصدق بكله.
أي شرط أدائها
الزكاة
وحاجته الأصلية: أي حاجته السكنى واللباس والركوب والاستعمال والاستخدام فلا تجب في دار السكنى إن لم تكن للتجارة، ولا فرق بينهما لو كانت للسكنى أو لم تكن بأن كانت للاستعمال لا تجب عليها الزكاة وإن كان قيمتها ،نصاباً وثياب البدن وأثاث المنزل ودواب الركوب وعبيد الخدمة وسلاح الاستعمال وآلات المحترفين وكتب العلم، وهذا القيد مغن عن قوله: "فارغ عن الدين"؛ لأن مال المديون ليس بفاضل، بل هي مستحقة لحاجته الأصلية، وهو دفع المطالبة ،والملازمة، والحبس في الدنيا والمؤاخذة في العقبى. (مسكين، فتح) نام: صفة رابعة للنصاب، أي حقيقة بالتوالد والتناسل وبالتجارات. (ع) ولو تقديراً: بأن يتمكن من الاستنماء بأن كان المال معداً للتجارة بغير نيتها كالنقدين، أو بنيتها عند حدوث الملك الاختياري، بخلاف ما لو ورثه ونواه للتجارة والحاصل أن النماء الحقيقي، والتقديري ينقسم إلى خلقي وفعلي، فالخلقي الذهب والفضة؛ لأنهما خلقا للتجارة، فلا يشترط فيهما النية والفعلي: ما يكون بإعداد العبد، وهو العمل بنية التجارة كشراء العروض والحيوانات وقبول الهبة بنية التجارة، أو كان المال معداً للإسامة كالحيوانات السائمة، فإن لم يتمكن من الاستنماء، فلا زكاة كما في مال الضمار، وهو في اللغة المال الغائب الذي لا يرجى، وفي الشرع كل مال غير مقدور الانتفاع به مع قيام أصل الملك، وكذا الآبق، والمفقود، والمغصوب إذا لم يكن عليه بينة، والمال الساقط في البحر، والمدفون في المفازة إذا نسي مكانه والذي أخذه السلطان مصادرة، والوديعة إذا نسي المودع وليس هو من معارفه والدين المجحود، إذا لم يكن بينة. (مسكين، فتح) مقارنة للأداء: أي أداء الفقير أو الوكيل ولو حكماً كما دفع بلا نية ثم نوى والمال قائم بيد الفقير، ولا يشترط علم الفقير بأنها زكاة على الأصح، حتى لو أعطى مسكيناً دراهم وسماها هبة أو قرضاً ونوى الزكاة يجزئه؛ لأن العبرة لنية الدافع، لا لعلم المدفوع إليه، وللوكيل دفع الزكاة لولده كبيراً كان أو صغيراً، ولامرأته إذا كانوا محاويج، ولا يجوز أن يمسك لنفسه شيئاً، إلا إذا قال ضعها حيث شئت، وهذا محمول على ما إذا كان الوكيل فقيراً. وقوله: "أو لعزل" أي شرط صحة أداء الزكاة النية وقت الأداء؛ لأنها عبادة، فلا تصح بدون النية وقت الأداء، كسائر العبادات أو نية مقارنة وقت العزل؛ لأن الدفع يتفرق، فيتحرج باستحضار النية عند كل دفع، فاكتفى بوجودها
حاجة العزل، دفعاً للحرج كتقديم النية في الصوم. (فتح) لعزل أي أو نية مقارنة لعزل الواجب عن الزكاة. أو تصدق بكله [ أي بكل النصاب أو بجميع ماله فيسقط عنه الزكاة؛ لأن الجزء الواجب دخل فيه. (ع)] أي لو تصدق بجميع ماله ولا ينوي الزكاة سقط فرضها؛ لأن الجزء الواجب دخل فيه، فإن قيل: النية شرط في الزكاة و لم توجد؟ قلنا: إن الواجب نية أصل العبادة لتمتاز عن العادة وقد وجدت؛ لأن الكلام فيما إذا تصدق على الفقير والصدقة ما يراد بهما رضا الله تعالى ونية الفرض إنما تشترط لتحصيل التعين وذا عند عدم التعين -
Conditions of its performance: and his basic need, productive (nam) even if notionally, and the condition of its performance is intention concurrent with the payment or with the setting aside of what is obligatory, or giving all of it in charity. That is, the condition of its performance. Zakat. And his basic need: i.e., his need for housing, clothing, riding, use, and service. So zakat is not obligatory on a dwelling house if it is not for trade; there is no difference between whether it is for dwelling or not; if it is for use, zakat is not obligatory on it even if its value reaches nisab. Likewise, clothing of the body, household furniture, riding animals, service-slaves, weapons for use, tools of professionals, and books of knowledge. This restriction renders superfluous his saying: 'free from debt', because the debtor's wealth is not surplus; rather, it is required for his basic need, which is to repel claim, prosecution, imprisonment in this world, and accountability in the next. (Miskin, Fath) Nam: the fourth attribute of the nisab, i.e., actually through procreation, breeding, and trade. (Ayni) 'Even if notionally' means he is able to make it grow, such as wealth prepared for trade without its intention, like the two precious metals (gold and silver), or with its intention at the time of discretionary acquisition. Contrary to if he inherited it and intended it for trade. The gist is that real and notional growth is divided into innate (khilqi) and actual (fi'li). Innate: gold and silver, because they are created for trade, so intention is not required. Actual: what is through the servant's preparation, which is working with intention of trade, like buying goods and animals, accepting a gift with trade intention, or wealth prepared for pasturing (sa'imah) like grazing animals. If one is not able to make it grow, there is no zakat, as in the case of mal al-dimar (lost wealth). Philologically, it is wealth that is absent and not hoped for. Legally, it is every wealth from which benefit is not possible while ownership subsists, such as: a runaway slave, a lost person, usurped property without evidence, wealth fallen into the sea, wealth buried in the desert if its place is forgotten, wealth taken by the ruler as a fine, a deposit if the depositor forgot and he is not among his acquaintances, and a denied debt without evidence. (Miskin, Fath) 'Concurrent with the payment': i.e., the payment to the poor person or the agent, even constructively, as if he paid without intention and then intended while the wealth is still in the poor person's hand. It is not a condition that the poor person knows it is zakat according to the soundest view. Even if he gave dirhams to a poor person and called it a gift or a loan and intended zakat, it suffices, because the consideration is the intention of the giver, not the knowledge of the recipient. The agent may pay zakat to his child, whether adult or minor, and to his wife if they are needy. It is not permissible for him to keep anything for himself, unless he said 'place it where you wish'; this is understood when the agent is poor. His statement: 'or for setting aside' means the condition for the validity of performing zakat is intention at the time of payment, because it is an act of worship; it is not valid without intention at the time of payment, like other acts of worship. Or intention concurrent with the time of setting aside, because payment is scattered, and it would be difficult to bring intention at every payment, so intention at the time of setting aside suffices, removing hardship, like advancing intention in fasting. (Fath) 'For setting aside': i.e., intention concurrent with setting aside the obligatory portion for zakat. 'Or giving all of it in charity': i.e., if he gives all his wealth in charity without intending zakat, the obligation falls off because the obligatory portion is included in it. If it is said: intention is a condition in zakat and it was not present? We say: the obligation is intention of the essence of worship to distinguish it from habit, and that is present; because the discussion is when he gives in charity to a poor person, and charity is intended for the pleasure of Allah, and intention of obligation is only required to achieve specification, and that is when there is no specification.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions for the performance (ada') of zakat: the wealth must be free from basic needs (hajat asliyyah), the nisab must be productive (nam) or potentially productive, and intention (niyyah) must be present.

1. Hajat asliyyah (basic needs): Items essential for living, such as a dwelling house, clothing, furniture, riding animals, service slaves, weapons, tools of trade, and books of knowledge, are not subject to zakat even if their value reaches nisab. This is because zakat is only on surplus wealth. The debtor's wealth is not surplus, so this condition effectively replaces the earlier condition of being free from debt.

2. Nam (productive): The nisab must be capable of growth, either actually (through breeding, trade) or notionally (potential to grow). This is the fourth attribute of nisab. Real growth is inherent in gold and silver (khilqi) without intention; actual growth requires human effort and intention (e.g., trade goods). If wealth cannot grow, like lost or inaccessible wealth (mal al-dimar), no zakat is due. Examples include property that is lost, usurped without evidence, or debts denied without proof.

3. Niyyah (intention): Intention is a condition for the validity of zakat payment. It can be made at the time of payment or at the time of setting aside (categorizing) the zakat amount. If one gives charity without intending zakat, but the entire wealth is given, the obligation falls due to inclusion. The intention does not need to be known to the recipient; the giver's intention suffices. An agent may pay to his own needy relatives, but if he is poor, he may not keep any for himself unless authorized.

Key Terms
حاجة أصلية (hajat asliyyah): Basic necessities of life such as housing, clothing, furniture, and tools of trade; zakat is not obligatory on these items.
نام (nam): Productive or capable of growth; the nisab must be actually or potentially productive for zakat to be due.
نية (niyyah): Intention; for zakat, it must be present at the time of payment or setting aside, distinguishing it from ordinary charity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is intention (niyyah) sufficient for zakat?
A) Only at the time of payment to the poor
B) At the time of setting aside the zakat amount or at payment
C) It is not required if the giver is generous
D) Only if the recipient is aware of the intention

Key Takeaway
Valid zakat performance requires wealth free from basic needs, a productive nisab, and intention at payment or setting aside.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Conditions for Paying Zakat: Basic Need, Growth, and Intention
Commentary on conditions for zakat payment including intention and nisab growth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for valid zakat payment and apply them to determine whether specific wealth is subject to zakat.

Core Idea
Zakat is only due on growing wealth surplus to basic needs, paid with intention.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary outlines the prerequisites for fulfilling the zakat obligation. Understanding these conditions is crucial to correctly applying zakat in various financial circumstances. We will examine the three core conditions: freedom from basic need, the growth potential of the nisab, and the requirement of intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Conditions
Read the opening sentence: 'Conditions of its payment: his basic need, growing even if hypothetically, and the condition of its payment is an intention...' These are the three pillars for valid zakat payment.
Note the word 'shara'it' indicates conditions (shurut) not pillars.
2
Understand 'Basic Need'
The commentary expands 'basic need' (haja asliyya) to include dwelling, clothing, furniture, riding animals, servants, tools, and books. Wealth used for these is exempt from zakat even if its value reaches nisab.
This condition subsumes 'free from debt' because a debtor's wealth is needed to satisfy demands.
3
Distinguish Actual vs. Hypothetical Growth
The nisab must be 'growing' (nam). Actual growth occurs through breeding or trade; hypothetical growth means the wealth is capable of increase (e.g., gold and silver are inherently growing; goods prepared for trade). If wealth is not capable of increase (e.g., mal al-dimār), no zakat is due.
Growth can be innate (khilqi) like gold/silver, or voluntary (fi'li) through intention and effort.
4
Grasp the Role of Intention (Niyya)
Intention is required to distinguish worship from habit. It must be present at the time of payment or at the time of setting aside the wajib amount. Intention is not required for the recipient to know it is zakat.
Analogy to fasting: advance intention at night suffices for the whole day, removing hardship of repeating intention.
5
Examine the Exceptional Case: Giving All Wealth in Charity
If a person gives all his wealth in charity without explicitly intending zakat, the obligation is waived because the wajib portion is included, and the general intention of charity suffices for distinction from habit.
This shows that when the entire wealth is given, specific intention for zakat is not required.

Conditions of its payment: his basic need, growing even if hypothetically, and the condition of its payment is an intention concurrent with the payment or with setting aside what is obligatory or giving all in charity. That is, condition of paying zakat. His basic need: i.e., his need for dwelling, clothing, riding, use, and service. So zakat is not obligatory for a dwelling house if it is not for trade, and there is no difference between them if it is for dwelling or not, i.e., if it is for use, zakat is not obligatory even if its value is a nisab. And clothes for the body, household furniture, riding animals, servants for service, weapons for use, tools of professionals, and books of knowledge. This condition suffices from his saying: "free from debt"; because the wealth of a debtor is not surplus, rather it is needed for his basic need, which is repelling demand, attachment, imprisonment in this world and punishment in the afterlife. (Miskin, Fath) 'Growing': a fourth attribute of the nisab, i.e., actually by breeding and increase and by trades. (A) 'And even hypothetically': that he is able to gain increase, such as wealth prepared for trade without its intention like gold and silver, or with its intention at the time of acquisition by choice, contrary to if he inherited it and intended it for trade. The result is that actual and hypothetical growth is divided into innate and voluntary: innate is gold and silver because they are created for trade, so intention is not required for them; and voluntary is what is by preparation of the servant, i.e., working with intention of trade like purchasing goods and animals and accepting a gift with intention of trade, or wealth prepared for pasturing like grazing animals. If he is not able to gain increase, then no zakat as in mal al-dimār, which in language is absent wealth that is not hoped for, and in law is every wealth not possible to benefit from while ownership remains, and likewise the runaway slave, the lost property, and the usurped property if he has no evidence, wealth fallen into the sea, buried in the desert if he forgets its place, what the ruler takes by confiscation, the deposit if the depositor forgets and he is not known to him, and the denied debt if there is no evidence. (Miskin, Fath) 'Concurrent with payment': i.e., payment to the poor or agent, even if juridically as when he pays without intention then intends while the wealth is still in the poor's hand. And it is not a condition that the poor knows it is zakat according to the most correct view, so even if he gives a poor person dirhams and calls them a gift or loan and intends zakat, it suffices because the consideration is the intention of the giver, not the knowledge of the recipient. And the agent may pay zakat to his child, whether adult or minor, and to his wife if they are needy. And he may not keep anything for himself unless he says "place it wherever you wish," and this is interpreted as when the agent is poor. And his saying: "or for setting aside" means the condition for the validity of paying zakat is intention at the time of payment because it is an act of worship, so it is not valid without intention at the time of payment like other acts of worship, or intention concurrent at the time of setting aside because payment is scattered and it would be difficult to bring intention at every payment, so presence at the time of setting aside suffices to remove difficulty like advancing intention in fasting. (Fath) 'For setting aside': i.e., or intention concurrent for setting aside the obligatory from zakat. 'Or giving all in charity' i.e., all of the nisab or all of his wealth, then zakat is waived because the obligatory part is included in it. (A) i.e., if he gives all his wealth in charity without intending zakat, the obligation falls because the obligatory part is included. If it is said: intention is a condition in zakat and it was not present? We say: the obligatory is intention of the original worship to distinguish from habit, and it was present because the discussion is when he gives charity to the poor, and charity is intended for the pleasure of Allah, and the intention of obligation is only required for specification, and that is when there is no specification.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the conditions for paying zakat. It begins by stating the conditions: the wealth must be surplus to basic needs, must be growing actually or potentially, and payment must be accompanied by intention or intention at the time of setting aside or giving all in charity. The commentary then expands on each condition. Basic needs include housing, clothing, riding animals, etc.; wealth used for these is exempt from zakat even if its value reaches nisab. The condition 'free from debt' is subsumed under basic need because a debtor's wealth is not surplus—it is needed to meet demands and avoid imprisonment. The nisab must be 'growing' (nam), either actually through reproduction or trade, or potentially by being prepared for trade or pasturing (like grazing animals). If wealth is not capable of increase, like mal al-dimār (unreachable wealth), no zakat is due. Examples of mal al-dimār are lost or stolen property without evidence, deposits forgotten, etc. The intention (niyya) must be concurrent with payment to the poor or agent; it is not required that the recipient knows it is zakat. The intention can also be made at the time of setting aside the zakat amount, to avoid difficulty of repeating intention for each payment. Finally, if one gives all his wealth in charity without specifically intending zakat, the obligation is lifted because the obligatory portion is included; the general intention of charity suffices for distinguishing from habit, though detailed intention is only needed for specifying the type of obligation.

Key Terms
نية (niyya): The mental intention that distinguishes an act of worship from a mere habit; required for zakat.
نام (nām): Growing; the fourth attribute of the nisab, meaning the wealth is capable of increase actually or potentially.
مال الضمار (māl al-ḍimār): Wealth that is not accessible despite ownership, such as lost, stolen, or denied property without evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a condition for paying zakat?
A) The wealth must be surplus to basic needs.
B) The nisab must be capable of growth.
C) The recipient must know it is zakat.
D) The payer must have intention at payment or setting aside.

Key Takeaway
Zakat is only due on wealth that is surplus to basic needs, capable of growth, and paid with intention; giving all in charity without specific intention suffices.

Zakat on Grazing Animals (Sawa'im): Definition, Nisab, and Partial Charity Dispute
Introduction to zakat on grazing animals, definition, nisab, and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sawa'im, list the conditions for zakat on them, state the nisab for camels (25 camels: bint makhad; 5 camels: sheep), and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether giving charity discharges zakat, and the rule on debt forgiveness.

Core Idea
Zakat on sawa'im is wajib at specific nisabs; partial charity does not discharge the full obligation according to the relied-upon view.

This lesson introduces the chapter on zakat of grazing animals (sawa'im). We begin by defining sawa'im and their conditions, then explore the nisab for camels and the wisdom behind the obligatory animals. The passage also addresses key intra-Hanafi differences, including whether giving some wealth in charity fulfills the zakat on that portion, and the special case of forgiving a debt owed by a poor person.

Guided Path
1
Define sawa'im and state conditions for zakat
Identify the term 'sā'imah' and the three key conditions: free grazing for most of the year, mubah pasture, and intention for dairy/brood.
Animals for transport or trade are not sawa'im for zakat purposes.
2
Identify nisab for camels
State that at 25 camels the obligatory animal is a bint makhad (female camel in second year); at 5 camels it is a sheep (any gender, one year old).
The sheep at 5 camels is a concession due to difficulty.
3
Understand the wisdom behind the nisab
Note that for camels, the young and females are preferred because camels have high value; for 5 camels, a sheep is analogous to 2.5% of wealth.
The ruling is tawqifi (based on revelation) but has rational aspects.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on charity
Imam Muhammad says if you give some wealth in charity before the year ends, zakat on that portion drops; Abu Yusuf says it does not because the obligation is on the entire wealth.
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is Abu Yusuf's.
5
Apply the debt forgiveness rule
If you forgive a debt owed to you by a poor person, the zakat on that debt is dropped regardless of intention; if only part is forgiven, only that part's zakat drops.
This is a special concession for debts to the poor.

باب صدقة السوائم أي في بيان أحكامها وهي التي تكتفي بالرعي في أكثر السنة، وتجب في خمس وعشرين إبلاً بنت مخاض، = السائمة في المرعى أي تفرض أي سائمة والواجب متعين في هذا النصاب فلا حاجة إلى التعين وصار كما إذا نوى الصوم مطلقاً في رمضان، ولو تصدق ببعض المال سقطت زكاة المؤدى عند محمد، وعند أبي يوسف لا تسقط؛ لأن الباقي محل الواجب، ولو كان له دين على فقير فأبرأه عنه سقط زكاته عنه نوى به الزكاة أو لا، ولو أبرأه عن البعض سقط زكاة ذلك البعض، وزكاة الباقي لا تسقط ولو نوى به الأداء عن الباقي رمز الحقائق: ۱۱۷/۱] (ومستخلص) باب صدقة السوائم بدأ بصدقة السوائم؛ اقتداء بكتاب رسول الله، ولأنها كانت إلى العرب، وأعز أموالهم المواشي، وأشرفها الإبل، فلهذا قدمها على البقر، وتعبيره بالصدقة؛ للاقتداء بقوله تعالى: {إِنَّمَا الصَّدَقَاتُ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ وَالْمَسَاكِينِ} (التوبة: 60) أي الزكاة، ولأنها إذا أطلقت يراد بها الزكاة، وسميت الزكاة بالصدقة؛ لدلالتها على صدق العبد في العبودية (فتح) السوائم: جمع سائمة وهي الحيوانات الراعية في المرعى. (نهر) وهي التي: هذا تعريف لمطلق السائمة، لا التي يجب فيها الزكاة؛ إذ يشترط فيها كون ذلك لقصد الدر والنسل، حتى لو أسامها للحمل والركوب لم يجب فيها شيء، ولو أسامها للتجارة كان فيها زكاة التجارة. والرعي بالفتح مصدر رعت الماشية، وبالكسر الكلأ نفسه، ولا بد من كون المرعى مباحاً حتى لو رعت غير المباح لا تكون سائمة. (فتح) في أكثر السنة هو ما فوق النصف، فلو رعت أقل السنة أو علفها نصف الحول لا تكون سائمة ولا تجب فيها الزكاة. بنت مخاض وهي التي استكملت سنة ودخلت في الثانية، سميت بها؛ لأن أمها صارت ذات مخاض بأخرى، والمخاض وجع الولادة. (رمز الحقائق: ۱۱۸/۱)] إنما قيد بها؛ لأن الشرع جعل الواجب في نصاب الإبل الصغار دون الكبار بدليل عدم جواز الأضحية بها؛ إذ لا تجوز الأضحية إلا بالثني فصاعداً، وكان ذلك تيسيراً لأرباب المواشي، وجعل الواجب أيضاً من الإناث حتى لا يجوز فيها سوى الإناث، ولا تجوز الذكور إلا بطريق القيمة؛ لأن الأنوثة تعد فضلا في الإبل، فصار الواجب وسطاً، وقد جاءت السنة بتعيين الوسط، ولم تعين الأنوثة في البقر والغنم؛ لأن الأنوثة فيها لا تعد فضلاً. وقوله: "في كل خمس من الإبل شاة" إنما وجبت الشاة في الخمس من الإبل؛ لأنها إذا بلغت خمساً كان مالاً كثيراً لا يمكن إخلاؤه عن الواجب للإسراف ولا إيجاب واحدة من الإبل للإحجاف، فتجب شاة ذكراً كان أو أنثى تم لها سنة وطعنت في الثانية فصاعداً، ولا يجوز ما دون ذلك. فإن قيل: الأصل في الزكاة أن يجب في كل نوع منه، فكيف وجبت الشاة في الإبل؟ قلنا: بالنص على خلاف القياس؛ ولأن الواحد من خمس خمس، والواجب ربع العشر، وفي إيجاب الشقص ضرر عيب الشركة، فأوجبنا الشاة؛ لأنها تقرب العشر للإبل الخمس؛ لأنها كانت تقوم بخمسة دراهم وبنت مخاض بأربعين، فإيجاب الشاة في خمس من الإبل كإيجاب الخمس في المائتين من الدراهم وقال في النهر الراجح أنه توقيفي لا أنه معقول المعنى. (فتح)
Chapter of Zakat of Grazing Animals. (i.e., regarding its rulings) And they are those that suffice with grazing for most of the year. And zakat becomes obligatory in twenty-five camels: a bint makhad. = the grazing animals in the pasture. i.e., it is obligatory. i.e., grazing animal. And the obligatory is specified in this nisab so there is no need for specification, and it becomes as if he intended fasting absolutely in Ramadan. And if he gives some of his wealth in charity, the zakat of what is paid drops according to Muhammad, but according to Abu Yusuf it does not drop because the remainder is the place of the obligation. And if he had a debt on a poor person and he absolves him from it, his zakat on that debt drops whether he intended zakat or not. And if he absolves him from part, the zakat of that part drops, and the zakat of the remainder does not drop even if he intended by it payment for the remainder. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 117/1) (and Mustakhlas) Chapter of Zakat of Grazing Animals. He began with zakat of grazing animals; following the Book of Allah’s Messenger, and because they were the property of the Arabs, and their most valuable wealth was livestock, and the noblest of them was camels, so he gave it precedence over cattle. And his expression 'sadaqah' is to follow His statement: {Indeed, the charities are for the poor and the needy} (al-Tawbah: 60), i.e., zakat, and because when it is used absolutely, zakat is meant, and zakat is called sadaqah because it indicates the truthfulness of the servant in servitude. (Fath) 'al-Sawa'im' is plural of sa'imah, which are animals grazing in the pasture. (Nahr) 'And they are those': this is a definition of absolute grazing animals, not those on which zakat is obligatory, because it is conditioned that this is for the purpose of milk and offspring, so if he pastures them for transport or riding, nothing is obligatory, and if he pastures them for trade, then the zakat of trade applies. And 'al-ra'y' with fatha is the source verb of 'the cattle grazed', and with kasra it is the herbage itself. And it is necessary that the pasture be mubah (free), so if they graze on non-mubah, they are not sa'imah. (Fath) 'For most of the year' means more than half. So if they graze less than half the year or are fed for half the year, they are not sa'imah and no zakat is obligatory on them. 'Bint makhad': she is the one that has completed one year and entered the second; so called because her mother has become pregnant with another, and 'makhad' is the pain of childbirth. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 118/1) It is only restricted by this because the Law made the obligatory in the nisab of camels from the young, not the old, as evidenced by the impermissibility of sacrificing them, for sacrifice is not permissible except with thani and above, and that was to ease the livestock owners. And the Law also made the obligatory from females, so only females are allowed, and males are not allowed except by value, because femaleness is considered a virtue in camels, so the obligatory became moderate, and the Sunnah specified the moderate. And femaleness is not specified in cattle and sheep because femaleness in them is not considered a virtue. And his saying: 'For every five camels, a sheep.' The sheep became obligatory in five camels because when they reach five, it is significant wealth that cannot be left without an obligation due to extravagance, nor obligating one camel due to hardship, so a sheep is obligatory, male or female, that has completed one year and entered the second and above, and what is below that is not permissible. If it is said: The principle in zakat is that it becomes obligatory from the same type, so how did a sheep become obligatory in camels? We say: by textual evidence contrary to analogy; and because one camel from five is a fifth, and the obligatory is a quarter of a tenth, and in obligating a share there is harm due to the defect of co-ownership, so we obligated a sheep because it approximates the tenth of five camels, because they would be valued at five dirhams and a bint makhad at forty, so obligating a sheep in five camels is like obligating five dirhams in two hundred dirhams. And it is said in al-Nahr that the preponderant view is that it is tauqifi (based on revelation) and not rationally understood. (Fath)
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on zakat of grazing animals (sawa'im). It first defines sawa'im as animals that depend on open grazing for most of the year; they must be intended for dairy and breeding, not for transport or riding, and the pasture must be free (mubah). Zakat becomes obligatory at the nisab of 25 camels, specifically a bint makhad (a female camel in its second year). The text then discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute: if one gives some of his wealth in charity, does that fulfill zakat? According to Imam Muhammad, the zakat on the amount given is discharged; according to Abu Yusuf, it is not discharged because the obligation is on the entire wealth. The passage also covers the ruling on forgiving a debt owed by a poor person: the zakat on that debt is dropped regardless of intention, but if only part is forgiven, only that part's zakat drops. The commentary explains why camels are mentioned first (following the Prophet's practice and Arab custom), why the term 'sadaqah' is used, and the definition of bint makhad. For the first nisab (5 camels), a sheep is due, and the text addresses the objection that zakat should be from the same type, responding that it is based on revealed text (tawqifi) and not pure analogy. The ratio is explained: a sheep approximates the value of one-fifth of a camel, analogous to the standard rate of 2.5%.

Key Terms
سائمة (sā'imah): Grazing animals that rely on free pasture for most of the year, intended for dairy and offspring.
بنت مخاض (bint makhāḍ): A female camel that has completed one year and entered the second year.
صدقة (ṣadaqah): In this context, synonym for zakat (obligatory charity).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the obligatory animal for zakat on 25 camels that are sawa'im?
A) A sheep
B) A bint makhad
C) A bint labun
D) A hiqqa

Key Takeaway
Zakat on sawa'im is wajib with specific nisabs and conditions; partial charity does not discharge the full obligation per the relied-upon view, and forgiving a debt owed by a poor person drops zakat on that debt.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Zakat on Grazing Camels: Nisabs and the Shafi'i Dispute
Rulings on zakat for camels as grazing livestock

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi nisabs for camels and evaluate the dispute with the Shafi'i school regarding the calculation beyond 120 camels.

Core Idea
For camels beyond 120, Hanafi law imposes one sheep per 5 camels, not the 40/50 rotation of the Shafi'is.

Zakat on grazing camels is a wajib obligation with specific nisabs defined by the Sunnah. The Hanafi school follows a detailed schedule up to 120 camels and then a different rule for excess, which leads to a significant disagreement with the Shafi'i school. This lesson unpacks the rulings, the proof texts, and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
Define sā'imah and its conditions
Identify what qualifies as sā'imah: livestock that graze on permissible pasture for more than half the year, kept for milk and offspring. This determines whether zakat is wajib.
If camels are grazed for trade, they fall under zakāt al-tijārah.
2
State the nisabs up to 120
List the specific animals due for each nisab: 5-24 camels: sheep; 25-35: bint makhād; 36-45: bint labūn; 46-60: hiqqa; 61-75: jadha'a; 76-90: two bint labūn; 91-120: two hiqqas.
The waqs (exempt interval) exists only up to 24 camels; after that every nisab triggers zakat.
3
Explain the rule beyond 120
For every 5 camels over 120, one sheep is due. This is based on the letter of 'Amr ibn Hazm.
The Hanafi combine this with the 40/50 rule for those exact numbers, but not as a rotation.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
The Shafi'i school uses a rotation of 40 (bint labūn) and 50 (hiqqa) for increments beyond 120. The Hanafi response is that both hadiths can be applied, and their hadith is authentic and supported by the practice of Ibn 'Abbas and 'Ali.
The thamarah al-khilaf: on 125, Hanafi: 2 hiqqas + 1 sheep; Shafi'i: 3 bint labūn.
5
Apply the calculation to a practical case
Given a specific number of camels, compute the zakat using the Hanafi method.
Example: 130 camels → 2 hiqqas (for 91-120) + 2 sheep (for the excess 10 camels counted as 2 × 5).

 السائمة في المرعى أي تفرض أي سائمة والواجب متعين في هذا النصاب فلا حاجة إلى التعين وصار كما إذا نوى الصوم مطلقاً في رمضان، ولو تصدق ببعض المال سقطت زكاة المؤدى عند محمد، وعند أبي يوسف لا تسقط؛ لأن الباقي محل الواجب، ولو كان له دين على فقير فأبرأه عنه سقط زكاته عنه نوى به الزكاة أو لا، ولو أبرأه عن البعض سقط زكاة ذلك البعض، وزكاة الباقي لا تسقط ولو نوى به الأداء عن الباقي رمز الحقائق: ۱۱۷/۱] (ومستخلص) باب صدقة السوائم بدأ بصدقة السوائم؛ اقتداء بكتاب رسول الله، ولأنها كانت إلى العرب، وأعز أموالهم المواشي، وأشرفها الإبل، فلهذا قدمها على البقر، وتعبيره بالصدقة؛ للاقتداء بقوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّمَا الصَّدَقَاتُ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ وَالْمَسَاكِينِ﴾ (التوبة: ٦٠) أي الزكاة، ولأنها إذا أطلقت يراد بها الزكاة، وسميت الزكاة بالصدقة؛ لدلالتها على صدق العبد في العبودية (فتح) السوائم: جمع سائمة وهي الحيوانات الراعية في المرعى. (نهر) وهي التي: هذا تعريف لمطلق السائمة، لا التي يجب فيها الزكاة؛ إذ يشترط فيها كون ذلك لقصد الدر والنسل، حتى لو أسامها للحمل والركوب لم يجب فيها شيء، ولو أسامها للتجارة كان فيها زكاة التجارة. والرعي بالفتح مصدر رعت الماشية، وبالكسر الكلأ نفسه، ولا بد من كون المرعى مباحاً حتى لو رعت غير المباح لا تكون سائمة.
