No Zakat on Horses, Mules, and Donkeys
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on zakat for horses, mules, and donkeys, and explain the intra-madhhab dispute with Imam Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
Horses, mules, and donkeys are exempt from zakat — the hadith explicitly negates any obligation.

This lesson examines the ruling on zakat for horses, mules, and donkeys. While these animals are livestock, the relied-upon Hanafi position is that no zakat is due on them, based on authentic hadith. We will explore the evidence and the intra-madhhab disagreement with Imam Abu Hanifa, who held a different view on mixed-gender grazing horses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what exactly is being ruled upon (horses, mules, donkeys) and the hukm level (no obligation).
The ruling is an exemption from zakat for these animals when they are sa'imah (grazing).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary proof cited in the text: the hadith 'ليس على المسلم في فرسه وغلامه صدقة' (Bukhari, Muslim).
A second hadith from Ali is also mentioned, waiving sadaqah on horses, donkeys, and working oxen.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the hadith proves the ruling: the explicit negation of sadaqah on the horse indicates no zakat obligation.
The hadith is general; the Sahibayn use it as a categorical exemption.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the opposing view: Abu Hanifa (with Zufar) held that mixed-gender grazing horses are zakatable based on another hadith and qiyas.
Abu Hanifa's proof: 'في كل فرس سائمة دينار أو عشرة دراهم' and analogy with other livestock.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Determine why the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad is chosen for fatwa: the authentic hadith overrides the other, and the text explicitly says 'wa huwa al-mukhtar lil fatwa'.
Fatwa today follows the Sahibayn: no zakat on horses, mules, or donkeys.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا شيء في الخيل: مطلقا سواء كانت ذكوراً أو إناثاً في السوائم مخلوطا أو لا، والمراد بالخيل: السائمة؛ إذ الباب معقود لها، وهو مشتق من الخيلاء، هو اسم جمع للعراب والبرازين لا واحد له كالغنم والإبل، وعدم الزكاة فيه قولهما وهو المختار للفتوى؛ لقوله : ليس" على المسلم في فرسه وغلامه صدقة"، متفق عليه، وقوله علي: عفوت لكم عن صدقة الجبهة والكسعة والنخة والجبهة الخيل والكسعة: الحمير، والنخة: البقر العوامل، وبه أخذ المصنف، وعند أبي حنيفة: إذا كانت الخيل سائمة واختلط ذكورها وإناثها فصاحبها بالخيار إن شاء أعطى من كل فرس ديناراً، وإن شاء قومها وأعطى من كل مائتي درهم خمسة دراهم وهو قول زفر، وإن كانت ذكوراً منفرداً لا زكاة فيها عند الإمام، وكذا إذا كانت إناثاً منفردات لا زكاة فيها، وفي رواية عنه: أنها تجب في الإناث؛ لإمكان التناسل بالفحل المستعار، بخلاف الذكور ، وله قوله عليه: "في كل فرس سائمة دينار أو عشرة دراهم، وتأويل ما روياه: فرس الغازي وعبيد الخدمة. (مسكين، مستخلص) والبغال والحمير: من حيث السوم إجماعاً؛ لقوله عليه "لم ينزل علي فيهما شيء"، وأما من حيث التجارة ففيهما الزكاة والبغال بالكسر جمع بغل وهو ما يتولد بين الحمار والفرس والحمير بالفتح جمع حمار وهو العير، والحملان بضم الحاء، وقيل: بكسرها جمع حمل بفتحتين، والفصلان بضم الفاء جمع فصيل، ولد الناقة قبل أن يصير ابن مخاض أي في السنة الأولى، والعجاجيل جمع عجول بكسر العين وتشديد الجيم، وقيل: جمع عجل بالكسر، وتكلموا في صورة المسألة فإنها مشكلة؛ لأن الزكاة لا تجب بدون مضي الحول، وبعد الحول لم تبق صغار، فقيل: صورة المسألة أن الصغار كانت لها أمهات فمضت ستة أشهر فولدت أولاداً، ثم ماتت الأمهات وبقيت الأولاد قدر النصاب وتم الحول عليها وهي صغار هل تجب الزكاة فيها أو لا ؟ فقال أبو يوسف، إنا لو أوجبنا فيها ما يجب في المسان كما قال زفر أحجفنا بأرباب الأموال، ولو أوجبنا فيها شاة أضررنا بالفقراء، فأوجبنا واحدة منها استدلالا بالمهازيل فإن نقصان الوصف كما أثر في تخفيف الواجب لا في إسقاطه فكذلك إسقاط السن، والصحيح قول أبي حنيفة أن لا شيء فيها؛ لأن النص أوجب للزكاة أسنانا مرتبة فلا مدخل للقياس في ذلك
And nothing is due on horses: absolutely, whether male or female, grazing, mixed or not. The meaning of 'khayl' is grazing horses; the chapter is dedicated to them. The absence of zakat is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and it is chosen for fatwa due to the hadith...
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute concerning zakat on horses, mules, and donkeys. The matn states 'nothing is due on horses', and the commentary clarifies that the relied-upon position (qaulahuma) is that no zakat is due on grazing horses, based on the authentic hadith: 'The Muslim is not obligated to give sadaqah on his horse or his slave.' Another hadith from 'Ali states that the Prophet waived sadaqah on horses, donkeys, and working oxen. However, there is an ikhtilaf with Abu Hanifa: if horses are grazing and males and females are mixed, the owner may choose to give one dinar per horse or evaluate them and give 2.5% of the value; if males alone or females alone, no zakat according to Imam Abu Hanifa (except a riwaya that females are zakatable). The commentary also discusses the offspring of horses, mules, and donkeys: no zakat on the animals themselves, but if traded, zakat applies. A difficult case arises when young animals are born and mothers die before the year completes; Abu Yusuf said one young animal is due by analogy with emaciated animals, but Abu Hanifa said nothing is due because the texts specify specific ages, leaving no room for qiyas.

Key Terms
الخيل (al-khayl): A collective noun for horses, whether Arab or non-Arab breeds; no singular from the same root.
السوائم (al-sawa'im): Grazing livestock; the chapter is dedicated to them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling on zakat for a person who has 10 grazing horses (with both males and females)?
A) Zakat is due: one dinar per horse
B) Zakat is due: 2.5% of value
C) No zakat is due
D) Zakat is due only if males and females are separate

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that no zakat is due on horses, mules, or donkeys, based on the authentic hadith from the Prophet.

Ruling on taking a jadha' in zakat of sheep
Intra-Hanafi dispute on jadha' in zakat of sheep

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi relied-upon position on taking a jadha' in zakat of sheep, and explain the intra-madhhab disagreement by citing the proofs and rebuttals.

Core Idea
In Hanafi zakat, only a thani (two-year-old) or older is accepted; a jadha' is not sufficient, despite a disagreement from the Sahibayn.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a jadha' (young male animal) can be taken as zakat for sheep and goats. The relied-upon position, based on Zahir al-Riwaya, prohibits it, but a narration from Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn allows it. We will analyze their proofs and the reasoning that leads to the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
The act is giving zakat on sheep and goats. The dispute is about the minimum acceptable age of the animal: must it be a thani (≥1 year for sheep) or can a jadha' be given?
2
State the two positions
The Zahir al-Riwaya position (mufta bihi) holds that only a thani or older is acceptable. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and one narration from Abu Hanifa hold that a jadha' may be taken.
The Sahibayn are the primary students of Abu Hanifa.
3
Compare the proofs
The Zahir al-Riwaya relies on the hadith of 'Ali: 'Nothing is taken in zakat except the thani and above' and the principle that the wajib is the wasat (middle). The Sahibayn cite the hadith 'Our due is only the jadha' and the thani' and analogize from udhiyah.
The rebuttal: the Sahibayn's hadith is interpreted as referring to camels, and udhiyah is a narrower ruling.
4
Evaluate the tarjih and note the practical consequence
The Zahir al-Riwaya is given precedence because its dalil is stronger and the principle of wasat supports it. The practical consequence: if a jadha' is given, it is not accepted; the owner must provide a thani.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا الجذع: أي لا يؤخذ الجذع مطلقا سواء كان زكاة الضأن أو المعز، والجذع من الضأن ما أتى عليه أكثر ومن البقر ما تم له سنة، ومن الإبل ما تم له أربع سنين، ونقلوا عن الأزهري: أن الجذع من المعز ما تم له سنة، والضأن ما له ألية، وروي عن أبي حنيفة وهو قولهما: أنه يؤخذ الجذع؛ لقوله عليه: "إنما حقنا الجذع والثني"؛ ولأنه يتأدى به الأضحية فكذا الزكاة مع أن باب الأضحية أضيق من باب الزكاة ألا ترى أن التبيع والتبيعة لا يجوز أحدهما في الأضحية ويجوز في الزكاة، ووجه ظاهر الرواية حديث علي الله موقوفا ومرفوعا: "لا يؤخذ في الزكاة إلا الثني فصاعداً"؛ ولأن الواجب هو الوسط والجذع من الصغار، وجواز الأضحية عرف نصا وهو قوله علي: "نعمت الأضحية الجذع من الضأن"، والمراد بما روياه: "إنما حقنا" إلخ الجذع من الإبل. (فتح، مستخلص)
Not the jadha': meaning the jadha' is not taken at all, whether it be zakat of sheep or goats. The jadha' of sheep is one that is over [a certain age]; of cattle, one that has completed a year; of camels, one that has completed four years. They transmitted from al-Azhari: that the jadha' of goats is one that has completed a year, and sheep that has a fat tail. It is narrated from Abu Hanifa and it is their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) statement: that the jadha' is taken, due to his (peace be upon him) statement: 'Our due is only the jadha' and the thani'; and because it is used to fulfill the udhiyah sacrifice, so similarly zakat, even though the chapter of udhiyah is narrower than the chapter of zakat—do you not see that the tabi' and the tabi'ah are not permissible in udhiyah but are permissible in zakat. The aspect of the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwaya) is the hadith of 'Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, as a mauquf and marfu' report: 'Nothing is taken in zakat except the thani and above'; and because the obligatory is the middle, and the jadha' is from the young. And the permissibility in udhiyah is known by text, which is the statement of 'Ali: 'Excellent is the udhiyah of the jadha' of sheep.' And what they narrated ('Our due is only...') is interpreted as referring to the jadha' of camels. (Fath, Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a jadha' (young male animal) can be taken in zakat of sheep and goats. The text first defines the jadha' for different animals: for sheep, one that is more than a certain age (usually 6-12 months); for cattle, one year old; for camels, four years old. Then it reports a narration from Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that the jadha' may be taken, citing a hadith 'Our due is only the jadha' and the thani' and arguing by analogy from udhiyah sacrifice. However, the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwaya) is that only a thani (two-year-old or older) is taken, based on a hadith from 'Ali and the principle that the wajib is the middling animal, while the jadha' is considered young. The text clarifies that the hadith cited by the Sahibayn is interpreted as referring to camels, not sheep. Thus, the correct Hanafi fatwa is that a jadha' is not accepted in zakat of sheep and goats.

Key Terms
الجذع (al-jadha'): A young male animal that has not reached the thani stage; ages vary by species.
الثني (al-thani): An animal that has entered its second year (or equivalent for camels/cattle).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, which animal is taken in zakat of sheep?
A) A jadha' of any kind
B) A thani or older
C) A lamb under one year
D) Any sheep regardless of age

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi zakat, the obligatory animal is the thani; a jadha' is not accepted despite an intra-madhhab disagreement.

Zakat on Grazing Horses: The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat of grazing horses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bihi position on zakat of grazing horses and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, including the proofs and tarjih.

Core Idea
No zakat on horses is the fatwa, but Abu Hanifa differed for mixed herds.

Zakat on livestock is a key obligation, but its application to horses has been a point of discussion within the Hanafi school. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the relied-upon view of no zakat on grazing horses, while also detailing the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and his student Zufar. Understanding this dispute and its resolution is essential for knowing the operative fatwa and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the relied-upon ruling
Read the opening statement: 'ولا شيء في الخيل' (nothing is due on horses). Note that this is the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and is declared 'al-mukhtar li al-fatwa' (chosen for fatwa).
The author affirms this as the operative position.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
The text cites two proofs: the hadith 'No sadaqah on a Muslim's horse or slave' and the statement of 'Ali remitting zakat on certain animals. Analyze how these proofs support the no-zakat ruling.
3
Study Abu Hanifa's contrary view
Abu Hanifa obligated zakat on mixed herds of male and female grazing horses, giving the owner a choice: pay one dinar per horse or value them and pay 2.5%. Also note the narration making zakat wajib on mares alone.
Zufar followed Abu Hanifa.
4
Understand the Hanafi response to Abu Hanifa's proof
The Sahibayn interpret the hadith about 'every grazing horse a dinar' as referring specifically to the horse of a warrior or a working slave, not general grazing horses.
This is the tarjih (preference) mechanism.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi and its implications
The text concludes with 'bihi akhadha al-musannif' (al-Musannif adopted it). Thus, the fatwa is that no zakat is due on grazing horses, regardless of gender or mixing. This is the ruling to apply in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا شيء في الخيل: مطلقاً سواء كانت ذكوراً أو إناثاً في السوائم مخلوطا أو لا، والمراد بالخيل: السائمة؛ إذ الباب معقود لها، وهو مشتق من الخيلاء، هو اسم جمع للعراب والبرازين لا واحد له كالغنم والإبل، وعدم الزكاة فيه قولهما وهو المختار للفتوى؛ لقوله : ليس" على المسلم في فرسه وغلامه صدقة"، متفق عليه، وقوله علي: عفوت لكم عن صدقة الجبهة والكسعة والنخة والجبهة الخيل والكسعة: الحمير، والنخة: البقر العوامل، وبه أخذ المصنف، وعند أبي حنيفة: إذا كانت الخيل سائمة واختلط ذكورها وإناثها فصاحبها بالخيار إن شاء أعطى من كل فرس ديناراً، وإن شاء قومها وأعطى من كل مائتي درهم خمسة دراهم وهو قول زفر، وإن كانت ذكوراً منفرداً لا زكاة فيها عند الإمام، وكذا إذا كانت إناثاً منفردات لا زكاة فيها، وفي رواية عنه: أنها تجب في الإناث؛ لإمكان التناسل بالفحل المستعار، بخلاف الذكور ، وله قوله عليه: "في كل فرس سائمة دينار أو عشرة دراهم، وتأويل ما روياه: فرس الغازي وعبيد الخدمة. (مسكين، مستخلص) والبغال والحمير: من حيث السوم إجماعاً؛ لقوله عليه "لم ينزل علي فيهما شيء"، وأما من حيث التجارة ففيهما الزكاة والبغال بالكسر جمع بغل وهو ما يتولد بين الحمار والفرس والحمير بالفتح جمع حمار وهو العير
And nothing [is due] in horses: absolutely, whether they be males or females, whether [grazing and] mixed [with males and females] or not. The meaning of 'horses' here is the grazing ones, as the chapter is devoted to them. The word 'khayl' is derived from 'khayla''; it is a collective noun for pure Arabian horses and others, having no singular, like 'ghanam' and 'ibil'. The absence of zakat on them is the statement of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and it is the chosen for fatwa, due to his (peace be upon him) statement: 'There is no sadaqah for a Muslim on his horse and his slave'—agreed upon. And the statement of 'Ali: 'I have remitted for you the sadaqah on the jabhah, the kasa'ah, and the nakhah'—jabhah are horses, kasa'ah are donkeys, nakhah are working cows. And al-Musannif adopted this. According to Abu Hanifa: if horses are grazing and its males and females are mixed, the owner has a choice: if he wishes, he gives from every horse a dinar, or if he wishes, he evaluates them and gives from every two hundred dirhams five dirhams—this is the statement of Zufar. And if they are males alone, there is no zakat on them according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). Similarly, if they are females alone, there is no zakat on them. In one narration from him: that it is obligatory on females due to the possibility of reproduction using a borrowed stallion, unlike males. And he (Peace be upon him) has the statement: 'On every grazing horse a dinar or ten dirhams.' And the interpretation of what they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) narrated is: the horse of the warrior and slaves of service. (Miskin, Mustakhlas) As for mules and donkeys: from the aspect of grazing, there is consensus; due to his statement: 'Nothing has been revealed to me concerning them.' As for the aspect of trade, there is zakat on them. Al-bighal (mules) is plural of baghl, which is the offspring of a donkey and a horse; al-hamir (donkeys) is plural of himar, which is the donkey.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling of zakat on grazing horses, mules, and donkeys. It begins by stating the relied-upon Hanafi position (Sahibayn) that there is no zakat on horses at all, citing the hadith 'There is no sadaqah on a Muslim's horse or slave' and a statement of 'Ali. The text then presents Abu Hanifa's view: if there is a mixed herd of male and female horses, the owner may choose to pay one dinar per horse or evaluate and pay 2.5% (one-fortieth). For unmixed males or single sex, no zakat. One narration from Abu Hanifa obligates zakat on mares due to potential breeding. The text then states that the fatwa is with the Sahibayn (no zakat). For mules and donkeys, there is consensus on no zakat for grazing, but zakat is due if they are trade goods. The passage ends with linguistic definitions of the animals.

Key Terms
السوائم (al-sawa'im): Grazing livestock that are sent out to pasture for most of the year.
الخيل (al-khayl): Horses; a collective noun with no singular, derived from khayla' (pride).
الجبهة (al-jabhah): Horses (in the hadith of 'Ali); literally 'forehead'
الكسعة (al-kasa'ah): Donkeys (in the hadith of 'Ali)
النخة (al-nakhah): Working cows (in the hadith of 'Ali)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi fatwa regarding zakat on grazing horses?
A) Zakat is always due
B) No zakat is due
C) Zakat is due only if mixed males and females
D) Zakat is due only on mares

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that no zakat is due on grazing horses, despite a legitimate difference from Imam Abu Hanifa.

Zakat on Mules and Donkeys: Consensus and Trade Exception
Consensus ruling on mules and donkeys with trade exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on zakat for grazing mules and donkeys and identify the condition under which zakat becomes due.

Core Idea
No zakat on grazing mules and donkeys by consensus, but zakat due if they are trade goods.

While horses generated an intra-school dispute, mules and donkeys have a clear consensus on no zakat when grazing. The passage also clarifies that if they are bought and sold as merchandise, zakat applies. This lesson covers that consensus and the distinction between livestock and trade goods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the consensus ruling
The text says 'والبغال والحمير: من حيث السوم إجماعاً' (mules and donkeys: regarding grazing, there is consensus). This means no zakat is due on them as livestock.
Consensus here likely means within the Hanafi school and possibly beyond.
2
Examine the proof
The Prophet said: 'لم ينزل علي فيهما شيء' (Nothing has been revealed to me concerning them). This indicates no obligation.
3
Note the exception for trade
The text adds: 'وأما من حيث التجارة ففيهما الزكاة' (As for the aspect of trade, there is zakat on them).
This applies the general principle that trade goods trigger zakat.
4
Understand the linguistic definitions
The passage defines 'bighal' (mules) as offspring of a donkey and a horse, and 'hamir' (donkeys) as the ass.
These definitions clarify which animals are included.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا شيء في الخيل: مطلقاً سواء كانت ذكوراً أو إناثاً في السوائم مخلوطا أو لا، والمراد بالخيل: السائمة؛ إذ الباب معقود لها، وهو مشتق من الخيلاء، هو اسم جمع للعراب والبرازين لا واحد له كالغنم والإبل، وعدم الزكاة فيه قولهما وهو المختار للفتوى؛ لقوله : ليس" على المسلم في فرسه وغلامه صدقة"، متفق عليه، وقوله علي: عفوت لكم عن صدقة الجبهة والكسعة والنخة والجبهة الخيل والكسعة: الحمير، والنخة: البقر العوامل، وبه أخذ المصنف، وعند أبي حنيفة: إذا كانت الخيل سائمة واختلط ذكورها وإناثها فصاحبها بالخيار إن شاء أعطى من كل فرس ديناراً، وإن شاء قومها وأعطى من كل مائتي درهم خمسة دراهم وهو قول زفر، وإن كانت ذكوراً منفرداً لا زكاة فيها عند الإمام، وكذا إذا كانت إناثاً منفردات لا زكاة فيها، وفي رواية عنه: أنها تجب في الإناث؛ لإمكان التناسل بالفحل المستعار، بخلاف الذكور ، وله قوله عليه: "في كل فرس سائمة دينار أو عشرة دراهم، وتأويل ما روياه: فرس الغازي وعبيد الخدمة. (مسكين، مستخلص) والبغال والحمير: من حيث السوم إجماعاً؛ لقوله عليه "لم ينزل علي فيهما شيء"، وأما من حيث التجارة ففيهما الزكاة والبغال بالكسر جمع بغل وهو ما يتولد بين الحمار والفرس والحمير بالفتح جمع حمار وهو العير
And nothing [is due] in horses: absolutely, whether they be males or females, whether [grazing and] mixed [with males and females] or not. The meaning of 'horses' here is the grazing ones, as the chapter is devoted to them. The word 'khayl' is derived from 'khayla''; it is a collective noun for pure Arabian horses and others, having no singular, like 'ghanam' and 'ibil'. The absence of zakat on them is the statement of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and it is the chosen for fatwa, due to his (peace be upon him) statement: 'There is no sadaqah for a Muslim on his horse and his slave'—agreed upon. And the statement of 'Ali: 'I have remitted for you the sadaqah on the jabhah, the kasa'ah, and the nakhah'—jabhah are horses, kasa'ah are donkeys, nakhah are working cows. And al-Musannif adopted this. According to Abu Hanifa: if horses are grazing and its males and females are mixed, the owner has a choice: if he wishes, he gives from every horse a dinar, or if he wishes, he evaluates them and gives from every two hundred dirhams five dirhams—this is the statement of Zufar. And if they are males alone, there is no zakat on them according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). Similarly, if they are females alone, there is no zakat on them. In one narration from him: that it is obligatory on females due to the possibility of reproduction using a borrowed stallion, unlike males. And he (Peace be upon him) has the statement: 'On every grazing horse a dinar or ten dirhams.' And the interpretation of what they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) narrated is: the horse of the warrior and slaves of service. (Miskin, Mustakhlas) As for mules and donkeys: from the aspect of grazing, there is consensus; due to his statement: 'Nothing has been revealed to me concerning them.' As for the aspect of trade, there is zakat on them. Al-bighal (mules) is plural of baghl, which is the offspring of a donkey and a horse; al-hamir (donkeys) is plural of himar, which is the donkey.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling of zakat on grazing horses, mules, and donkeys. It begins by stating the relied-upon Hanafi position (Sahibayn) that there is no zakat on horses at all, citing the hadith 'There is no sadaqah on a Muslim's horse or slave' and a statement of 'Ali. The text then presents Abu Hanifa's view: if there is a mixed herd of male and female horses, the owner may choose to pay one dinar per horse or evaluate and pay 2.5% (one-fortieth). For unmixed males or single sex, no zakat. One narration from Abu Hanifa obligates zakat on mares due to potential breeding. The text then states that the fatwa is with the Sahibayn (no zakat). For mules and donkeys, there is consensus on no zakat for grazing, but zakat is due if they are trade goods. The passage ends with linguistic definitions of the animals.

Key Terms
البغال (al-bighal): Mules; plural of baghl, offspring of a male donkey and a female horse.
الحمير (al-hamir): Donkeys; plural of himar.

Key Takeaway
Mules and donkeys have no zakat as livestock by consensus, but zakat is required if they are trade goods.

Zakat on Young Livestock: The Dispute and Final Hanafi View
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat of young animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on zakat for young livestock and explain why the final view holds that no zakat is due.

Core Idea
Textually prescribed ages in zakat preclude qiyas; young animals lacking those ages incur no zakat even after a year.

This passage addresses a tricky case: young animals that survive a year but are not of the prescribed age for zakat. Abu Hanifa's final view, adopted by the school, is that no zakat is due because the text specifies ages. The passage also shows how Abu Yusuf's questioning led to Abu Hanifa's refined ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
Young animals (himlan, fisal, 'ajajil) whose mothers died, a full year passes while they are still young. Is zakat due?
The key issue: the animals lack the prescribed age (sinn) even after a full year.
2
Identify the conflicting positions
Zufar and initially Abu Hanifa: full zakat on adults. Abu Yusuf: one young animal. Abu Hanifa's final (and Muhammad): nothing.
Abu Hanifa changed his view twice.
3
Examine the proofs
Abu Yusuf analogized to emaciated animals (mahazil): deficiency reduces but doesn't drop. Abu Hanifa relied on nass (prescribed ages): no room for qiyas.
Analogy (qiyas) vs textual specification (nass).
4
Follow the evolution through the story
Abu Yusuf visited Abu Hanifa and discussed the case. Initially Abu Hanifa said one sheep, then one lamb, then nothing. This shows careful ijtihad.
Abu Hanifa's final view is the mufta bihi.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that no zakat is due on such young animals, per Abu Hanifa's final view and Muhammad.
This is the ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحملان بضم الحاء وقيل بكسرها جمع حمل بفتحتين والفصلان بضم الفاء جمع فصيل ولد الناقة قبل أن يصير ابن مخاض أي في السنة الأولى والعجاجيل جمع عجول بكسر العين وتشديد الجيم وقيل جمع عجل بالكسر وتكلموا في صورة المسألة فإنها مشكلة; لأن الزكاة لا تجب بدون مضي الحول وبعد الحول لم تبق صغار فقيل صورة المسألة أن الصغار كانت لها أمهات فمضت ستة أشهر فولدت أولاداً ثم ماتت الأمهات وبقيت الأولاد قدر النصاب وتم الحول عليها وهي صغار هل تجب الزكاة فيها أو لا ؟ فقال أبو يوسف إنا لو أوجبنا فيها ما يجب في المسان كما قال زفر أحجفنا بأرباب الأموال ولو أوجبنا فيها شاة أضررنا بالفقراء فأوجبنا واحدة منها استدلالا بالمهازيل فإن نقصان الوصف كما أثر في تخفيف الواجب لا في إسقاطه فكذلك إسقاط السن والصحيح قول أبي حنيفة أن لا شيء فيها; لأن النص أوجب للزكاة أسنانا مرتبة فلا مدخل للقياس في ذلك وهذه الأسنان مفقود في الصغار وهذا آخر أقوال أبي حنيفة وهو قول محمد وكان يقول أولا يجب فيها ما يجب في الكبار وهو قول زفر ومالك ثم رجع وقال يجب فيها واحدة منها وهو قول أبي يوسف والشافعي وروي عن أبي يوسف أنه قال دخلت على أبي حنيفة فقلت ما تقول في من ملك أربعين حملا فقال فيها شاة سنة فقلت ربما تأتي قيمة الشاة على أكثرها أو جميعها فتأمل ساعة ثم قال لا ولكن تؤخذ واحدة منها فقلت ويؤخذ الحمل في الزكاة فتأمل ساعة ثم قال لا إذن لا يجب فيها شيء فعد هذا مناقبه حيث أخذ من بكل قول من أقاويله مجتهد ولم يضع منها شيء. (فتح) والحملان جمع حمل وهو ولد الضأن في السنة الأولى (ط) والفصلان جمع فصيل وهو ولد الناقة قبل أن يتم الحول . (ط)
Al-himlan (with damma on ha', and some say with kasra) is plural of hamal (with two fatha), al-fisal (with damma on fa') is plural of fasil, the young of a she-camel before it becomes a ibn makhad, i.e., in the first year. Al-'ajajil is plural of 'ajul (with kasra on 'ayn and shadda on jim), and some say plural of 'ijl (with kasra). They discussed the scenario of the issue, for it is problematic: because zakat is not obligatory without the passing of the year, and after the year, they are no longer young. So it is said: the scenario is that the young had mothers, and six months passed, then they gave birth to offspring, then the mothers died, and the offspring remained, reaching the nisab, and the year completed over them while they were still young. Is zakat obligatory on them or not? Abu Yusuf said: If we obligate on them what is obligatory on the adult animals, as Zufar said, we would be unjust to the owners; and if we obligate one sheep on them, we would harm the poor. So we obligate one of them (i.e., one young animal) by analogy with the emaciated animals, for the deficiency in description (size) affects the lightening of the obligation but not its dropping, so likewise the dropping of age (i.e., young age). The correct statement is that of Abu Hanifa: nothing is due on them, because the text (nass) has obligated specific ages for zakat, and there is no room for analogy in this. And these specific ages are absent in the young. This was Abu Hanifa's final statement and it is the statement of Muhammad. He (Abu Hanifa) used to say initially: what is obligatory on adults is obligatory on them—this is the statement of Zufar and Malik. Then he retracted and said: one of them is obligatory—this is the statement of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i. It is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he said: I entered upon Abu Hanifa and said: What do you say about one who owns forty hamal (young sheep)? He said: There is one sheep on them (in zakat) for a year. I said: Perhaps the value of the sheep comes to most or all of them. So he pondered for an hour, then said: No, rather one of them is taken. I said: And is the hamal taken in zakat? He pondered for an hour, then said: No, then nothing is due on them. So count this among his merits, that he took from every statement of his ijtihad and did not discard any of them. (Fath) Al-himlan is plural of hamal, which is the young of sheep in the first year (T). Al-fisal is plural of fasil, which is the young of a she-camel before completing a year. (T)
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage addresses a complex scenario: young livestock (lambs, calves, foals) are born, their mothers die, and a full year passes while the young are still young—is zakat due? The text presents definitions of the terms: himlan (young sheep), fisal (young camel), 'ajajil (young cattle). The problem is that zakat requires passage of a full year and the animal to be at the prescribed age (sinn). The scenario posits that the young had mothers who died; the offspring have been alive for a full year but are still young (not yet reached the required age). Abu Yusuf argues for taking one young animal as zakat, by analogy with emaciated (mahazil) animals: deficiency in size reduces the quantity but not the obligation. Zufar and initially Abu Hanifa thought full zakat on adults is due. Later, Abu Hanifa adopted the view that nothing is due because zakat is textually tied to specific ages (sinn) and the young lack those ages. Muhammad agreed. The story with Abu Yusuf shows Abu Hanifa's gradual refinement. The final relied-upon position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that no zakat is due on such young animals. The text records this as a merit of Abu Hanifa's ijtihad.

Key Terms
الحملان (al-himlan): Young male lambs in their first year.
المسألة (al-mas'alah): The hypothetical scenario under dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One sheep
B) One young lamb
C) Nothing
D) Ten sheep

Key Takeaway
Textually prescribed ages in zakat preclude qiyas; young animals lacking those ages incur no zakat even after a year.

Zakat on Working and Fodder Animals: Exemption and Proofs
Ruling with proof: no zakat on working or fodder-fed animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for working and fodder-fed animals, identify the primary textual proofs, and explain the underlying rationale (illa) for the exemption.

Core Idea
No zakat on working or fodder-fed animals because they lack the growth (nama') required for zakat.

Zakat is obligatory on certain types of wealth, but not all animals are subject to it. The Hanafi school makes a key distinction between animals that graze freely (sa'imah) and those used for work or fed by the owner. This passage explains the ruling and the reasons behind it, supported by specific texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories and ruling
Read the definitions of 'awamil (working animals) and 'alufah (fodder-fed animals). Note the clear ruling: no zakat is due on either category.
The ruling is absolute; it does not depend on nisab or other conditions.
2
Locate the primary proofs
The text cites a hadith 'There is no sadaqah on working animals' and a statement from 'Ali. Identify these as the direct evidence (dalil naqli) for the exemption.
The hadith is specific to 'awamil; 'alufah is exempted by analogy or by extension through the rationale.
3
Understand the underlying rationale
The sabab (cause) for zakat is growing wealth (mal nam). The evidence of growth is either free grazing (for dairy/offspring) or preparation for trade. 'Awamil and 'alufah lack this growth because they incur maintenance costs instead.
This is a qiyas: the general rule requires growth; these categories lack it, so they are exempt.
4
Recognize the opposing school's argument
Imam Malik uses the general Quranic verse (9:103) to argue that all wealth is subject to zakat. Note the Hanafi response: the general command is specified (takhsis) by the hadith and the rationale.
This shows the Hanafi method of restricting general texts with specific evidence.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi position is considered mufta bihi. The proof is strong (specific hadith) and the rationale (lack of growth) is sound. There is no intra-Hanafi dispute.
The ruling is relied upon in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعوامل أي ولا في العوامل أي المعدات للعمل والحمل والغزو كالحراثة وسقي الماء عمل عليها أم لم يعمل. (فتح، مستخلص والعلوفة وهي التي يعلفها صاحبها نصف الحول أو أكثر. (ط)] بفتح العين ما يعلف من الغنم وغيرها الواحد والجمع سواء وقال مالك تجب الزكاة فيها للعمومات كقوله تعالى: ﴿خُذْ مِنْ أَمْوَالِهِمْ صَدَقَةً﴾ [التوبة:103] ولنا قوله عليه: "ليس في العوامل صدقة" وقال علي: "ليس في المثيرة صدقة" ولأن السبب هو المال النامي ودليل النماء الإسامة للدر والنسل أو الإعداد للتجارة ولم يوجد في العوامل وتكثر المؤونة في العلوفة فلم يوجد النماء معنى. (فتح، مستخلص)
And the 'awamil (working animals): meaning nothing [is due] on working animals, i.e., those prepared for work, carrying, and warfare, such as plowing and drawing water, whether they actually worked or not. (Fath, Mustakhlas) And the 'alufah (fodder animals): they are those that their owner feeds (with fodder) for half a year or more. (T) With fatha on 'ayn, what is fed to sheep and other animals, singular and plural are the same. Malik said: Zakat is obligatory on them due to generalities like His statement: 'Take from their wealth sadaqah' [9:103]. Our proof is his statement (peace be upon him): 'There is no sadaqah on working animals,' and 'Ali's statement: 'There is no sadaqah on plowing animals.' And because the cause (sabab) is growing wealth, and the evidence of growth is grazing for milk and offspring or preparation for trade, and this is not found in 'awamil. And the maintenance is heavy in 'alufah, so growth is not found in meaning. (Fath, Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that no zakat is due on working animals (al-'awamil) and fodder-fed animals (al-'alufah). Working animals are those used for plowing, carrying loads, or warfare, regardless of whether they actually worked. Fodder animals are those fed by the owner for half the year or more, which prevents them from being truly grazing (sa'imah). The text refutes the view of Imam Malik, who argued for zakat based on the general command of zakat in the Quran. The Hanafi proofs include a specific hadith 'There is no sadaqah on working animals' and a statement of 'Ali. Additionally, the underlying rationale (illa) for zakat is growth (nama'), which is evidenced by grazing (for dairy and offspring) or trade. Working animals do not have such growth; rather, they incur costs. Fodder animals similarly lack true growth because the owner bears the cost of feeding. Thus, both categories are exempt.

Key Terms
العوامل (al-'awamil): Animals used for work, such as plowing, carrying, or warfare.
العلوفة (al-'alufah): Animals that are fed fodder by the owner for a significant portion of the year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are working animals (al-'awamil) exempt from zakat according to Hanafis?
A) They are not considered wealth.
B) They do not have growth (nama') as shown by grazing.
C) They are always below nisab.
D) Because of a consensus of all scholars.

Key Takeaway
Working and fodder-fed animals are exempt from zakat because they lack the growth that is the essential cause of zakat.

Zakat on Surplus (al-'Afw) Between Nisabs
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakatability of surplus between nisabs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi ruling on al-'afw and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between the Sheikhayn and Muhammad/Zufar.

Core Idea
The surplus between two zakat nisabs is exempt from zakat according to the Sheikhayn, based on explicit hadith.

What happens to the extra animals between the first and second nisab? Are they exempt, or do they also incur zakat? Within the Hanafi school, this question sparked an early dispute between the founding imams. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq lays out the two positions and their practical consequence. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply nisab thresholds correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of the ruling
Determine what 'al-'afw' means here: the surplus amount of livestock above a nisab but below the next nisab.
e.g., between 5 and 9 camels, the 4 camels above 5 are 'afw.
2
State the two positions
Sheikhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): no zakat on al-'afw. Muhammad and Zufar: zakat is due proportionally on both nisab and surplus.
3
Analyze the dalil of the Sheikhayn
Hadith: 'On five camels, a sheep; nothing on the increase until there are ten.' This explicit text (nass) exempts the surplus.
The hadith is a clear proof (qat'i al-dalala) for the Sheikhayn.
4
Examine the counter-argument
Muhammad and Zufar argue that zakat is gratitude for all wealth, and surplus is also wealth. The Sheikhayn respond that the explicit text overrides this general reasoning.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Use the example: 80 sheep, 40 perish. Sheikhayn: 1 sheep due (original nisab intact). Muhammad/Zufar: half a sheep due (half the wealth remains).
The mufta bihi is the Sheikhayn's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العفو: [ أي ولا في العفو وهو ما بين النصابين. (ط)] أي الفاضل عن النصاب، وهذا عند الشيخين، وقال محمد وزفر: الزكاة في النصاب والعفو جميعاً، وثمرة الخلاف تظهر فيمن كان له ثمانون من الغنم، فهلك أربعون تجب فيها شاة عندهما، وعند محمد وزفر تجب نصف قيمة شاة؛ لأن الزكاة إنما وجبت شكرا لنعمة المال، والكل في هذا المعنى سواء، بل معنى التمول في العفو أظهر، ولهما قوله عليه: "في خمس من الإبل شاة، ولا شيء في الزيادة حتى تكون عشرة، وهذا نص على عدم الوجوب في الزيادة. (فتح، مستخلص)
Al-'afw (the surplus): [Meaning nothing (is due) on al-'afw, which is what is between the two nisabs. (T)] i.e., the excess above the nisab. And this is according to the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Muhammad and Zufar said: Zakat is on the nisab and the surplus together. The fruit of the difference appears in one who had eighty sheep, then forty perished: according to the two, a sheep is due (on the original nisab); according to Muhammad and Zufar, half the value of a sheep is due. Because zakat is only obligated as gratitude for the blessing of wealth, and all (wealth) is equal in this meaning; rather, the meaning of being wealth is more apparent in the surplus. And for the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is his (peace be upon him) statement: 'On five camels, a sheep; and nothing on the increase until there are ten.' And this is a clear text on the non-obligation on the increase. (Fath, Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on 'al-'afw'—the amount of livestock between two nisabs (for example, between 5 and 9 camels). The Sheikhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that no zakat is due on the surplus; only the nisab itself triggers zakat, and the surplus is exempt until the next nisab. Muhammad and Zufar hold that zakat is due on both the nisab and the surplus proportionally. The practical difference is illustrated: someone owns 80 sheep (the nisab for sheep is 40: 40-120 gives 1 sheep). If 40 sheep die before the end of the year, according to the Sheikhayn, since the nisab (40) remains, one sheep is due. According to Muhammad and Zufar, since half the sheep died, only half the zakat (half a sheep) is due. The Sheikhayn rely on the hadith: 'On five camels, a sheep; nothing on the increase until there are ten,' which explicitly exempts the surplus. The opposing view argues that zakat is gratitude for all wealth, including surplus. The relied-upon position is that of the Sheikhayn (no zakat on al-'afw).

Key Terms
العفو (al-'afw): The surplus amount of livestock between two nisabs (e.g., between 5 and 9 camels).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone owns 70 sheep (nisab: 40-120 gives 1 sheep), how many sheep as zakat according to the Sheikhayn?
A) One sheep
B) 0.5 sheep
C) 1.75 sheep
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The surplus (al-'afw) between two zakat nisabs is exempt from zakat according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

When Livestock Perishes After Zakat Obligation: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-school dispute on zakat liability when livestock perishes after obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on zakat when the nisab perishes after obligation and distinguish it from the Shafi'i view, applying the principle of yusr (ease) and dawam al-qudra (continued ability).

Core Idea
For easy obligations like zakat, continued ability is a condition; for fixed obligations like fitrana, it is not.

When zakat becomes obligatory on livestock and then the animals die before payment, does the obligation drop? The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ sharply. The answer hinges on a deeper usul distinction: some obligations require continued ability, others are fixed once ability is present. This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq explains the Hanafi ruling and its principle, contrasting with the Shafi'i analogy to sadaqat al-fitr. By understanding the reasoning, you will grasp how the Hanafi school uses the attribute of yusr to shape zakat rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: for apparent wealth (like grazing livestock), if the nisab perishes after obligation but before payment, zakat drops, provided the owner was not negligent (i.e., the imam did not request it).
Note the qualification: if the imam asked and the owner refused, he becomes liable.
2
Identify the opponent's view
Al-Shafi'i holds that zakat does not drop if the owner had the ability to pay (tamakkun min al-ada') at the time of obligation, even if the property perishes later.
Shafi'i bases this on analogy with sadaqat al-fitr.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i dalil: zakat is a financial right that resembles sadaqat al-fitr; once the right is established and the owner has the ability to pay, destruction of the property does not extinguish the obligation.
The key is tamakkun: ability to pay at the time the obligation became due.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal distinguishes between obligations of 'ease' (yusr) and obligations of 'possibility' (mumkin). Zakat on livestock is 'easy'—its collection is delegated to the imam, so the owner is not negligent until asked. Continued ability is a condition. In contrast, sadaqat al-fitr is a 'possible' obligation—once one has the means, the obligation is fixed and does not require continued ability.
The Hanafi principle: a right that becomes obligatory with a certain attribute (like ease) remains only as long as that attribute persists.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a person owned 40 sheep for a full lunar year and they died before he paid zakat, the Hanafi ruling is that no zakat is due (assuming no negligence). The Shafi'i ruling is that he must still pay.
This difference can have significant financial implications.

Source Text

والهالك بعد الوجوب [وفي هلاك البعض يسقط بقدره. (ط)] بالجر عطف على ما قبله أي لا شيء في الهالك بعد وجوب الزكاة، وقيد به; لأنه قبل الوجوب لا شيء في الهالك اتفاقاً، وكذلك في هلاك البعض يسقط بقدره، وقال الشافعي: لا يسقط إذا هلك بعد التمكن من الأداء، معناه إذا هلكت الأموال الباطنة بعد الوجوب وبعد التمكن من الأداء لا تسقط الزكاة; لأنها حق مال فلا تسقط بهلاك المال كصدقة الفطر; لأن الطلب بالأداء متوجه عليه في الحال، فيكون بالتأخير مفرطاً، بخلاف الأموال الظاهرة وهي السائمة; لأن الأخذ فيها إلى الإمام فلا يكون تفريطاً ما لم يطلب حتى لو طلب ومنعه ضمن والأصل عندنا أن الواجب متى كان بصفة اليسر، ودوام القدرة شرط لدوام الواجب; لأن الحق متى وجب بصفة لا يبقى إلا بتلك الصفة، وأما الواجب بقدرة الممكنة كصدقة الفطر فلا يشترط دوام القدرة لدوام الواجب، فلهذا لا تجب الزكاة إذا هلك النصاب، فتجب صدقة الفطر. (فتح)
And the destruction after obligation [And in destruction of part, it drops proportionally. (T)] in the genitive case, coordinators on what preceded: meaning nothing is due on what perishes after the obligation of zakat. It is qualified because before obligation there is nothing on the perished by agreement. Similarly, in destruction of part, it drops proportionally. Al-Shafi'i said: it does not drop if destruction occurs after the ability to perform (al-tamakkun min al-ada'), meaning if the hidden properties (amwal batina) perish after obligation and after ability to perform, the zakat does not drop because it is a financial right that does not drop by destruction of the property, like sadaqat al-fitr. Because the demand for payment is directed to him immediately, so delay makes him negligent. This contrasts with apparent properties (amwal zahira) which are the grazing livestock, because taking them is up to the imam, so there is no negligence as long as he is not asked; if he is asked and refuses, he becomes liable. The principle according to us is: when the obligatory (wajib) has the attribute of ease (yusr), continued ability (dawam al-qudra) is a condition for the continuity of the obligation. Because a right, when it becomes obligatory with a certain attribute, does not remain except with that attribute. As for the obligatory that is within one's capacity at the time (like sadaqat al-fitr), continuity of ability is not a condition for continuity of the obligation. For this reason, zakat is not obligatory if the nisab perishes, while sadaqat al-fitr remains obligatory (even after destruction of wealth). (Fath)
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario where livestock (or other zakatable wealth) perishes after zakat becomes obligatory but before payment. The Hanafi position distinguishes between two types of wealth: apparent (zahir, like grazing livestock) and hidden (batin, like cash and trade goods). For apparent wealth, if it perishes after obligation, zakat drops because the owner had no negligence (the imam is responsible for collection). If the owner was asked and refused, he becomes liable. For hidden wealth, if it perishes after the owner had the ability to pay (tamakkun min al-ada'), zakat does not drop, because the owner is negligent by delaying. The Shafi'i school differs: they hold that zakat does not drop for any wealth once the owner had ability to pay, analogy with fitrana. The Hanafi response explains the principle: for obligations that are 'easy' (yatirah) and conditioned on continued ability (like zakat on livestock), the obligation drops when the condition fails. For obligations that are 'possible' (mumkinah) like fitrana, once the condition is met, the obligation is fixed and does not drop. The text concludes that zakat drops if nisab perishes, but fitrana does not.

Key Terms
التمكن من الأداء (al-tamakkun min al-ada'): The owner's ability to pay the zakat at the time it became due (e.g., having the means).
يسر (yusr): Ease; the attribute of zakat obligations that makes continued ability a condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why does zakat on apparent wealth (livestock) drop if the animals die before payment?
A) Because the owner's ability to pay was not yet demanded by the imam.
B) Because zakat is never obligatory until the imam collects it.
C) Because the year was not completed.
D) Because the livestock was not of the required type.

Key Takeaway
For the Hanafi school, zakat on apparent wealth drops upon destruction before payment if the owner was not negligent, due to the principle that obligations requiring ease (yusr) are conditional on continued ability.

Zakah Exemptions: Work Animals, Fodder-Fed, Surplus, and Loss
Rulings on livestock zakah exemptions with proofs and disagreements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on zakah for young livestock, work animals, fodder-fed animals, surplus between nisabs, and wealth that perishes after obligation, and explain the proofs and disagreements.

Core Idea
Zakah is not due on work animals, fodder-fed livestock, surplus, or lost apparent wealth before demand.

Zakah on livestock is a key obligation, but the Hanafi school recognizes several exemptions based on the nature of the animals and the timing of loss. This lesson examines five categories where zakah may be reduced or waived, along with the proofs and scholarly disagreements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five exempt categories
The passage covers young livestock (when required age is missing), work animals, fodder-fed animals, surplus between nisabs, and animals that perish after obligation. List them and their rulings.
Each has a distinct rationale.
2
Analyze the proof for each exemption
For work animals and surplus, specific hadith are cited. For fodder-fed and loss, analogical reasoning is used. Identify the dalil for each.
Hadith: 'لا شيء في العوامل' and 'في خمس من الإبل شاة ولا شيء في الزيادة'
3
Note the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab disagreements
The text records differences among Hanafi imams (e.g., Muhammad and Zufar on surplus) and with Maliki and Shafi'i schools. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf.
e.g., Muhammad and Zufar require zakah on surplus, contrary to the two shaykhs.
4
Apply the rulings to a scenario
Given a case with mixed categories (e.g., 80 sheep, 40 fodder-fed, 40 grazing; 20 perish), determine zakah due using the mufta bihi.
Use the working position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

(فتح)
Chapter of Zakah on Grazing Livestock: Zakah of sheep, and lambs, and weaned camel calves, and young cows, and work animals, and fodder-fed animals, and surplus, and that which perishes after obligation. And if an age [requirement] is obligatory and it is not found, one pays a higher [age] and takes the surplus, or a lower [age]. [Commentary: He pays the required age animal from his livestock to the collector, and these ages are missing in the young. This is the final position of Abu Hanifa, and it is the view of Muhammad. He initially held that what is obligatory for adults is obligatory for them, which is the view of Zufar and Malik. Then he retracted and said: one (animal) among them is obligatory, which is the view of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i. It is narrated from Abu Yusuf: I entered upon Abu Hanifa and said: what do you say about one who owns forty lambs? He said: a one-year-old sheep is due. I said: perhaps the value of the sheep reaches most or all of them. He pondered a moment then said: no, but one of them is taken. I said: and is the lamb taken in zakah? He pondered then said: no. Then nothing is obligatory. This is counted among his merits: he took from each of his views as a mujtahid and did not discard anything. (Fath) 'Himlan' is plural of 'hamal' which is the offspring of sheep in the first year. 'Fislan' is plural of 'fasil' which is the offspring of the she-camel before completing one year. (T) 'Al-awamil': nor on work animals, i.e., animals prepared for work, carrying, and warfare, such as plowing and watering, whether they are worked or not. (Fath, Mustakhlas) 'Al-ulufah': that which its owner feeds for half the year or more. (T) Malik said: zakah is obligatory due to general proofs like His saying: "Take from their wealth a charity" (9:103). Our proof is his statement عليه: "There is no zakah on work animals," and Ali said: "There is no zakah on plowing animals." Also the cause is growing wealth, and the evidence of growth is being kept for milk and offspring or preparation for trade, which is not found in work animals. In fodder-fed animals, maintenance is abundant, so growth is not found in meaning. (Fath, Mustakhlas) 'Al-afw': i.e., nor on surplus which is what is between two nisabs. This is according to the Two Shaykhs. Muhammad and Zufar said: zakah is due on the nisab and the surplus together. The fruit of the difference appears in one who has eighty sheep, and forty perish: according to them, one sheep is obligatory; according to Muhammad and Zufar, half the value of a sheep is obligatory. Their proof is his statement عليه: "For five camels, one sheep, and nothing for the increase until it becomes ten." This is a text indicating non-obligation of the increase. (Fath, Mustakhlas) 'And that which perishes after obligation': i.e., nothing on that which perishes after the obligation of zakah. This restriction is because before obligation, nothing is due upon perishing by consensus. Similarly, upon perishing of some, it falls proportionally. Al-Shafi'i said: it does not fall if it perishes after being able to pay. Meaning: if the hidden wealth perishes after obligation and after ability to pay, zakah does not fall because it is a right of wealth that does not fall by perishing of wealth, like zakah al-fitr. The demand for payment is directed at him immediately, so delay is negligence. Unlike apparent wealth (grazing livestock), because collection is done by the imam, so there is no negligence until he demands. If he demands and he prevents it, he becomes liable. Our principle: the obligatory, when it is of a type of ease, continuous ability is a condition for the continuity of the obligation. As for that which is obligatory based on possible ability like zakah al-fitr, continuous ability is not a condition. Therefore, zakah is not obligatory if the nisab perishes, while zakah al-fitr is obligatory. (Fath)
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq deals with rulings on zakah for grazing livestock. It covers several distinct issues: young animals, work animals, fodder-fed animals, surplus between nisabs, and animals that perish after the obligation of zakah arises. The commentator expands on the matn with positions of different Hanafi imams and other schools. For young animals (lambs, kids, calves), Abu Hanifa's final position (also held by Muhammad al-Shaybani) is that if the required age is not found, one pays a higher age animal and takes the surplus, or a lower age animal. Initially, he held that the same duty applies as for adults, but he retracted. For work animals, the Hanafi position is no zakah, based on hadith "There is no zakah on work animals" and the analogy that growth is lacking. For fodder-fed animals (those fed by owner for at least half the year), no zakah due to absence of growth in meaning. For surplus (al-afw), i.e., the amount between two nisabs, the working position (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is no zakah, citing the hadith about five camels and nothing for the increase. For perishing after obligation, Hanafis distinguish between hidden wealth (like cash) and apparent wealth (grazing livestock). If the nisab perishes after capability to pay, zakah falls for grazing livestock (since the imam collects) but not for hidden wealth (since owner is negligent). The principle: continuous ability is required for obligations based on ease, but not for obligations like fitr that are based on possible ability.

Key Terms
السوائم (al-sawā’im): Grazing livestock that are let loose to pasture for most of the year without being fed by the owner.
العوامل (al-‘awāmil): Work animals used for plowing, carrying water, or other labor, whether actually worked or not.
العفو (al-‘afw): The surplus amount between two nisabs (e.g., after 5 camels, the extra camels up to 9 are ‘afw and no zakah due).
الهالك بعد الوجوب (al-hālik ba‘d al-wujūb): Wealth that perishes after the obligation of zakah has become due (e.g., after nisab held for a year).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school exempts work animals, fodder-fed livestock, surplus between nisabs, and apparent wealth that perishes before demand from zakah, based on specific hadith and the principle of continuous ability.

Fulfilling Zakah: Value, Age Adjustment, Middle Quality, and Adding Mustafad
Rules for fulfilling zakah when required age missing, paying value, assessing quality, and adding new acquisitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain and apply the Hanafi rulings on fulfilling zakah when the exact age animal is unavailable, including paying value, adjusting surplus/deficit, taking middle quality, and adding newly acquired property of the same type to the nisab.

Core Idea
Zakah's purpose is to meet need; thus value and other ages suffice, and mustafad of same type is added to the existing year.

This lesson covers practical scenarios in zakah payment. The Hanafi school provides flexibility: if the exact age is missing, you can pay a higher or lower age with adjustment, or pay cash value. The collector must take middle quality. Additionally, any new property of the same type acquired during the year is added to your nisab and zakah is due at your existing year's end. We'll explore the evidence and differences with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
State the basic obligation and the problem
Identify the default zakah obligation for livestock (e.g., 40 sheep require one sheep of specific age). Then recognize that the exact age may not always be available.
2
Explain the Hanafi solution for age mismatch
If the required age is missing, the owner may give a higher age animal and take the surplus value from the collector, or give a lower age and pay the deficiency. Both are permitted.
This is based on the principle of flexibility to ensure the obligation is fulfilled.
3
Explain the ruling on paying value
The owner may pay the cash value of the obligatory animal instead of the animal itself. This is allowed in zakah, 'ushr, expiations, fitr, and vows, but not in udhiyah, hadiy, or manumission.
The proof is that the purpose of zakah is to fill the need of the poor, which is rational; thus any wealth suffices. The textual specification indicates quantity, not type.
4
Explain the ruling on taking middle quality
The collector must take animals of average quality, avoiding the best and the worst. This is based on the hadith: 'Beware of the finest of their wealth.'
If the owner refuses to pay, the collector does not forcibly take; instead, the owner is imprisoned to pay himself.
5
Explain the ruling on adding mustafad
If a person already has a nisab and acquires additional property of the same type during the year (e.g., offspring, profit, inheritance, gift), it is added to the existing nisab. Zakah is paid on the total at the end of the original haul.
The hadith '...whatever occurs after that, no zakat until the next new year' supports that newly acquired property is not zakah until the year end, but by consensus offspring and profits are added. Shafi'i disagrees on profits.

Source Text

وردّ الفضل، أو دفع القيمة، ويؤخذ الوسط، ويُضمّ مستفاد من جنس نصاب في الزكاة من جنس ما يجب أي ما هو مستفاد ورد الفضل إلى الساعي، فإن وجبت بنت لبون دفع بنت مخاض وأعطى فضل قيمة بنت لبون إليه. (مسكين) أو دفع القيمة: [ أي قيمة ما وجب عليه، وقال الشافعي: لا يجوز أداء غير المنصوص، وهذه الأحكام في البقر والإبل سواء. (مسكين)] أي في الزكاة والعشر والكفارات وصدقة الفطر والنذر بخلاف الضحايا والهدايا والعتق، وتعتبر القيمة يوم الوجوب عنده، وعندهما يوم الأداء، وفي السوائم تعتبر يوم الأداء إجماعاً. وقال الشافعي: لا يجوز أداء غير المنصوص في هذه الأشياء كلها؛ لقوله عليها في أربعين شاة شاة وفي ست وثلاثين من الإبل بنت لبون إلى غير ذلك من النصوص، فلا يجوز إبطال النص بالتعليل؛ ولأنها قربة تتعلق بمحل فلا تتأدى بغيره كالهدايا والضحايا ولنا أن المقصود سد خلة الفقراء في الزكاة والعشر وغيرهما، وذلك يحصل بأي مال كان، والتقييد بالشاة ونحوها لبيان القدر لا للتعيين بخلاف الهدايا والضحايا؛ لأن القربة فيهما بالإراقة وهي غير معقولة فلا يتقوم وهذا معقول فيتقوم، وكذا الإعتاق فإن معنى القربة فيه إتلاف الملك ونفي الرق، وهو لا يتقوم أيضاً، واشتراط عدم وجود السن بجواز دفع الأعلى والأدنى، ودفع القيمة وقع اتفاقاً حتى لو دفع أحد هذه الأشياء مع وجود السن الواجب جاز عندنا خلافاً للشافعي، والخيار في ذلك لرب المال، ويجبر الساعي على القبول إلا إذا دفع أعلى منها وطلب الفضل؛ لأنه شراء للزيادة ولا إجبار فيه على الساعي. (عيني، فتح) ويؤخذ الوسط: لقوله عليه: "إياكم وكرائم أموالهم"، رواه الجماعة، وقوله علي: "لا تأخذ من خزرات أموال الناس" أي كرائمها، وخذ من حواشي "أموالهم أي من أوساطها، والحاصل أنه لا يأخذ الساعي خيار المال ولا رذالته نظرا لجانب الفقير، ورب المال إذا امتنع عن أداء الزكاة فلا يأخذها كرهاً؛ لأنها زكاة فلا تتأدى بدون اختياره، لكن يجبر بالحبس ليؤدي بنفسه، وعند الشافعي يأخذها كرهاً. تتمة: مات من عليه الزكاة لا تؤخذ من تركته إلا أن يوضي فحينئذ تعتبر من الثلث عندنا، وعند الشافعي: تؤخذ من تركته. (عيني، فتح) ويضم مستفاد: أي من كان له نصاب فاستفاد في أثناء الحول ما هو من جنسه ضم إليه مطلقاً، سواء كان ولدا أو ربحا وإن استفيد بسبب غير مقصود كالإرث والهبة، وإن لم يكن من جنسه لا يضم اتفاقاً، وقال الشافعي: إن كان المستفاد ولدا يضم إلى ما عنده من جنسه قولا واحداً، وإن كان ربحا فله قولان في ضمه إلى النصاب، وإن وجد ذهبا أو فضة من المعدن وأدى خمسه وعنده نصاب من جنسه فله قولان وحاصل مسألة المتن أن المستفاد في أثناء الحول من جنس النصاب يضم إليه ولا ينفرد له حول آخر بل يزكى للكل بحول النصاب السابق. وقال الشافعي: لا يزكى المستفاد بحول النصاب بل بحول آخر، وعند مالك وأحمد يضم في غير المواشي، ولنا قوله عليه: "إن من السنة شهراً تؤدون فيه زكاة أموالكم، فما حدث بعد ذلك فلا زكاة فيه حتى يجيء رأس الشهر"، رواه الترمذي، وهذا يقتضي أن تجب الزكاة في الحادث عند مجيء رأس السنة، وأما الأولاد والأرباح فتضم بالإجماع إلا في قول الشافعي في الأرباح. (مسكين)
And returning the surplus, or paying the value, and the middle is taken, and added is newly acquired property of the same type as the nisab in zakah, of the type that is obligatory, i.e., what is newly acquired. And returning the surplus to the collector: if a bint labun is obligatory, he pays bint makhad and gives the surplus value of bint labun to him (the collector). (Miskin) Or paying the value: i.e., the value of what is obligatory upon him. Al-Shafi'i said: it is not permitted to pay other than what is specified. These rulings apply to cattle and camels alike. (Miskin) i.e., in zakah, 'ushr, expiations, sadaqat al-fitr, and nazr, unlike udhiyah, hadiy, and manumission. The value is considered on the day of obligation according to him (Abu Hanifa), and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on the day of payment. For grazing livestock, it is considered on the day of payment by consensus. Al-Shafi'i said: it is not permitted to pay other than what is specified in all these matters; because of his statement عليه: "In forty sheep, one sheep; in thirty-six camels, bint labun" etc. So the text cannot be nullified by analogy. And because it is an act of worship attached to a specific item, so it is not fulfilled by another, like udhiyah and hadiy. Our proof: the purpose is to fill the need of the poor in zakah, 'ushr, etc., which can be achieved by any wealth. The restriction to sheep etc. is to indicate the quantity, not the specific type, unlike udhiyah and hadiy because the act of worship there is through slaughter, which is not rational, so it is not measured by value. This (zakah) is rational, so it is measured by value. Similarly, manumission: its act of worship is destroying ownership and negating slavery, which is also not measured by value. The condition of the absence of the required age permits paying higher or lower, and paying value occurs by agreement. Even if one pays these with the required age present, it is permissible according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. The choice is with the owner of the wealth, and the collector is forced to accept, except if he pays a higher age and demands the surplus, because that is buying the increase, and the collector is not forced. (Ayni, Fath) And the middle is taken: due to his statement عليه: "Beware of the finest of their wealth," reported by the group, and Ali's statement: "Do not take the best of people's wealth," i.e., its finest, rather take from the edges of their wealth, i.e., its averages. So the collector takes neither the best nor the worst, considering the poor. And if the owner of wealth refuses to pay zakah, it is not taken forcibly, because zakah is not fulfilled without his choice, but he is imprisoned to pay himself. According to al-Shafi'i, it is taken forcibly. Addendum: If one who owes zakah dies, it is not taken from his estate unless he bequeaths it; then it is considered from one-third according to us. According to al-Shafi'i, it is taken from his estate. (Ayni, Fath) And added is newly acquired: i.e., whoever has a nisab and acquires during the year something of the same type, it is added to it absolutely, whether it is offspring or profit, even if acquired through an unintended means like inheritance or gift. If it is not of the same type, it is not added by agreement. Al-Shafi'i said: if the acquired is offspring, it is added to his existing stock of the same type unanimously; if it is profit, he has two views on adding it to the nisab. And if he finds gold or silver from a mine and pays its khums and has a nisab of the same type, he has two views. The summary of the matn's issue: newly acquired property during the year of the same type as the nisab is added to it and does not have its own separate year; rather, the entire amount is given zakat according to the earlier nisab's year. Al-Shafi'i said: the newly acquired is not zakah with the nisab's year, but with another year. According to Malik and Ahmad, it is added for non-livestock. Our proof is his statement عليه: "The sunna is a month in which you pay zakat on your wealth; whatever occurs after that, no zakat is due until the next new year," reported by Tirmidhi. This implies that zakat is due on newly acquired property at the turn of the year. As for offspring and profits, they are added by consensus, except for the view of al-Shafi'i on profits. (Miskin)
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on zakah for grazing livestock, addressing how to fulfill the obligation when the exact required age is unavailable, paying value instead of the specific animal, taking the middle quality, and adding newly acquired property of the same type to the existing nisab. The commentator expands on each point. For paying higher or lower age with surplus or deficiency adjustment, the Hanafi position is that if the required age is missing, the owner may pay a higher age animal and take the surplus value from the collector, or pay a lower age and give additional value. Paying the cash value of the obligatory animal is also allowed in Hanafi, based on the purpose of zakah (fulfilling the need of the poor), unlike udhiyah and manumission where the act is not rational. The value is calculated on the day of payment for grazing livestock by consensus (within Hanafi). The middle quality is taken, neither the best nor the worst, as per hadith. If the owner refuses, he is imprisoned to pay himself, not forcibly taken (contra Shafi'i). If the owner dies, the zakah is not taken from the estate unless bequeathed, then from one-third (Hanafi). Shafi'i takes it from estate. For newly acquired property (mustafad) of the same type during the year, it is added to the existing nisab and zakah is paid at the end of the existing year. Hadith: 'Whatever occurs after that, no zakat until the next new year' supports that newly acquired is not zakah until the year end, but by consensus offspring and profits are added. Shafi'i disagrees on profits.

Key Terms
المستفاد (al-mustafād): Property acquired during the year after the nisab was already held, such as offspring, profit, inheritance, or gift.
دفع القيمة (daf‘ al-qīmah): Paying the monetary value of the obligatory zakah animal instead of the animal itself.
الوسط (al-wasaṭ): The middle quality; the collector must avoid taking the best or the worst, taking average-quality animals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person who owes zakah dies without having paid it, what happens?
A) The zakah is taken from his estate, like a debt.
B) The zakah is not taken from his estate unless he bequeathed it; then from one-third.
C) The zakah is waived because death ends obligations.
D) The zakah is paid from the estate only if the heir agrees.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes the purpose of zakah, allowing flexibility in payment method and addition of new property to the current year's nisab.

Zakat Paid to Rebels and Advancing Zakat
Commentary expanding two zakat rulings with rational reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on zakat taken by rebels and state the conditions under which advance payment of zakat is valid.

Core Idea
Zakat taken by rebels suffices because the Imam failed protection; advancing zakat is valid from a single nisab.

The Hanafi school provides practical rulings for situations where the state is unable to collect zakat, such as when rebels take control. This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq clarifies that zakat forcibly taken by rebels does not need to be re-paid, based on the principle that collection is tied to protection. Additionally, the text addresses the common question of paying zakat in advance, affirming its validity under specific conditions. Let's examine these two important rulings with their underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Scan the passage and note that it discusses two distinct issues: (1) zakat collected by rebels, and (2) paying zakat in advance (ta'jil). Each ruling has its own conditions and legal effect.
2
Analyze the rebels ruling
Read the statement: if rebels take kharaj, ushr, or zakat, it is not taken again. Note the reason: 'because the Imam did not protect them, and collection is based on protection.' Then find the intra-madhhab difference about intention (niyyah). Understand the condition for the ruling to apply.
The key term is himaayah (protection). The Imam's right to collect zakat is contingent on his ability to protect the people.
3
Analyze the ta'jil ruling
Look at the phrase: 'if the owner of a nisab advances zakat for years or for multiples of nisab, it is valid.' Identify the condition: the advance must be from a single nisab (i.e., one who owns a full nisab may pay zakat for future years or for multiple nisabs in advance). Consider the inter-madhhab difference: Malikis do not allow ta'jil at all, and Shafi'is only allow for one year ahead.
The condition 'from one nisab' means the person must currently be a sahib al-nisab; the advance is valid even if the nisab fluctuates later.
4
Apply the himaayah principle
The passage includes a supplement (tamah) about a harbi who becomes Muslim in enemy territory. Apply the same principle: since the Imam cannot protect him, zakat is not compulsory, but he is advised to pay if he knows of its obligation. This illustrates the consistent logic of the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صدقة السوائم
صدقة الغنم
إليه، ولو أخذ الخراج والعشر والزكاة بغاة لم يؤخذ أخرى، ولو عجل ذو النصاب نصاب لسنين أو لنصب صح.
مرة أخرى قدم الزكاة على الحول
زكاة سنين معدودة عجل من نصاب واحد التقديم فيها
إليه: أي إلى النصاب الذي استفيد منه في أثناء الحول ولو بهبة أو إرث. (ط،ع) بغاة: جمع باغ، وهم الذين خرجوا عن طاعة الإمام وتغلبوا على بلدة رمز الحقائق: ۱۲۲/۱] لم يؤخذ أخرى [ أي مرة أخرى مطلقاً سواء نوى التصدق أو لم ينو، وقيل: إذا نوى بالدفع التصدق عليهم سقط عنه وإلا لا. (مسكين] لأن الإمام لم يحمهم والجباية بالحماية، بخلاف ما إذا مر بهم هو فعشروه حيث يؤخذ منه ثانياً إذا مر على أهل العدل؛ لأن التقصير من جهته حيث مر عليهم لا من الإمام، والذمي فيه كالمسلم، ثم إذا لم يؤخذ منهم ثانيا يفتون بأن يعيدوها فيما بينهم وبين الله تعالى، وقيل في الخراج لا، وقيل: إذا نوى بالدفع الصدقة عليهم أجزأته؛ لأنهم لو حوسبوا بما عليهم من التبعات يكونون فقراء، وعلى هذا ما يؤخذ من الرجل في جبايات الظلمة والمصادرات إذا نوى بالدفع التصدق عليهم جاز عما نوى رمز الحقائق: ۱۲۲/۱] تتمة: أسلم الحربي في دار الحرب وأقام فيها سنين، ثم خرج إلينا لا يأخذ الإمام منه الزكاة لعدم الحماية، ونفتيه بأدائها إن كان عالما بوجوبها وإلا فلا؛ لأن الخطاب لم يبلغه وهو شرط الوجوب زكى المال الحلال بالمال الحرام اختلف في الإجزاء نوى الزكاة في ما يدفع إلى صبيان أقاربه أو لمن يهدى إليه الباكورة أو من يبشره بقدوم صديقه أو المعلم في المكتب إذا لم يستأجره يجوز. (فتح)
Chapter of Zakat on Livestock. Zakat of sheep. To it: if the kharaj, ushr, and zakat are taken by rebels, it is not taken again. And if the owner of nisab advances zakat for years or for multiples of nisab, it is valid. When the zakat is given before the completion of the year, for a counted number of years, from one nisab, the advance payment in it. To it: meaning to the nisab that was acquired during the year, even by gift or inheritance. (T, A) Rebels: plural of rebel, those who have left obedience to the Imam and have overcome a town. [Symbol of al-Haqa'iq 122/1] It is not taken again: meaning not taken a second time absolutely, whether he intended charity or not. And it is said: if he intended charity by paying them, it is counted for him; otherwise not. (Miskin) Because the Imam has not protected them, and collection is based on protection, unlike the case when he passes by them and they collect ushr from him, where it is taken from him a second time if he passes by the people of justice, because the shortcoming is from his side by passing them, not from the Imam. And the dhimmi is like the Muslim in this. Then, if it is not taken from them a second time, they give fatwa that they should repeat it between themselves and Allah. And it is said regarding kharaj, no. And it is said: if he intended charity by the payment, it suffices, because if they were held accountable for the obligations on them, they would be poor. Similarly, what is taken from a man by the taxes of oppressors and confiscations, if he intends charity by the payment, it is permissible for what he intended. [Symbol of al-Haqa'iq 122/1] Supplement: A harbi became Muslim in dar al-harb and stayed there for years, then came out to us. The Imam does not take zakat from him due to lack of protection. And we give fatwa that he should pay it if he was aware of its obligation, otherwise not, because the address did not reach him, and that is a condition of obligation. He gave zakat of lawful wealth with unlawful wealth; there is disagreement on its validity. He intended zakat in what he gives to the young children of his relatives, or to one to whom he gives the first fruits, or to one who gives him glad tidings of the arrival of a friend, or to the teacher in the school if he did not hire him — it is permissible. (Fath)
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of zakat on livestock, focusing on two key rulings. First, if rebels (bughat) — those who rebel against the Imam and take over a territory — collect kharaj, ushr, or zakat, the payer is not required to pay again. The reason is that the Imam failed to provide protection (himaaya), and collection is tied to protection. However, there is an intra-Hanafi difference: if the payer intended to give charity to the rebels, it suffices; otherwise, he must repeat the payment. Second, the passage addresses advancing zakat (ta'jil al-zakat): if a person who owns a full nisab pays zakat for multiple years or for multiple nisabs in advance, it is valid. The reason is that the original nisab is the basis, and the additional payment is subsidiary. This is opposed to Malik who disallows advance payment entirely, and Shafi'i who disallows advancing for multiple years. The passage also includes a supplement (tammah) about a harbi who becomes Muslim in enemy territory: since the Imam does not collect zakat from him due to lack of protection, he is advised to pay if he was aware of the obligation. Additional rulings cover mixing lawful and unlawful wealth for zakat, and the permissibility of giving zakat to specific recipients like young relatives or the teacher in a school if not hired.

Key Terms
بغاة (bughāt): Rebels who have rebelled against the Imam and taken control of a territory
تعجيل (ta'jīl): Paying zakat before its obligation becomes due, i.e., before the completion of the year for a nisab
حماية (himāyah): Protection provided by the Imam to the people, which is the basis for his right to collect zakat

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if rebels take zakat from a Muslim, does he need to pay zakat again to the legitimate Imam?
A) Yes, because rebels are not legitimate.
B) No, because the rebels took it by force.
C) No, if he intended charity when paying.
D) Yes, unless he paid voluntarily.

Key Takeaway
Zakat taken by rebels suffices if the payer intended charity, and advancing zakat is valid from a single nisab for multiple years or multiples of nisab.
