Zakat on Jewelry: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on zakat of jewelry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school obligates zakat on jewelry and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using dalil.

Core Idea
Zakat on jewelry is wajib because gold and silver are zakatable by substance, not use.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute: whether women's jewelry is subject to zakat. The Hanafi school holds that any gold or silver reaching nisab, regardless of form, triggers zakat. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, citing a hadith and reasoning based on usage. The Hanafi response marshals stronger hadith and Quranic generality. This lesson will guide you through the proofs and the resolution.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What exactly does the Hanafi school rule regarding zakat on gold and silver jewelry? Identify the hukm level and conditions.
The ruling applies to both men's and women's jewelry, including vessels and ingots.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Which school disagrees? What is their position and on what grounds?
Imam al-Shafi'i exempts permissible jewelry based on a hadith and analogy to clothes.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i dalil: the hadith of Jabir and the reasoning of 'no growth'.
The hadith is claimed to be weak by Hanafi authorities.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school refute the Shafi'i evidence? What alternative proofs do they present?
They cite hadith of the woman and Aisha, and the generality of Quran 9:34.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference between the two positions in a real-world scenario?
Hanafi: annual zakat on jewelry; Shafi'i: no zakat unless excessive or for trade.

كتاب الزكاة
باب زكاة المال
يجب في مائتي درهم وعشرين ديناراً ربع العشر ولو تبراً أو حلياً أو آنية، ثم في كل خمس بحسابه
وهي نصاب الفضة
وهو نصاب الذهب
(فتح)
باب زكاة المال : [ أي في بيان أحكامها، وأراد بالمال غير السوائم؛ لأن حكمها ذكر فيما مضى. (ع)] المال اسم لما يتمول ويدخر واللام فيه للمعهود في قوله عليه: "هاتوا ربع عشر أموالكم فخرجت السوائم؛ لأن زكاتها غير مقدرة به، وقدمها على خمس الركاز والعشر؛ لأنهما كالمستفاد وقدم النقدين على العروض؛ لأنهما أصلان لسائر الأموال في معرفة القيم، وقدم الفضة على الذهب اقتداء بكتب رسول الله . مائتي درهم إلخ: لما أخرجه الشيخان: "ليس في ما دون خمس أواق صدقة"، والأوقية كانت في أيامهم أربعين درهماً، فخمس أواق يساوي مائتي درهم وقوله عليها: "ليس في أقل من عشرين ديناراً صدقة" وهو نصاب الذهب، وقوله : ربع العشر"؛ لقوله علي : " في الرقة ربع العشر، وفي عشرين دينارا نصف دينار". (عيني) ربع العشر أي الجزء الواحد من أربعين، ففي مائتي درهم خمس دراهم، وفي عشرين ديناراً نص نصف دينار. (ع) ولو تبرا وهو القطعة المأخوذة من المعدن غير مضروب من ا الذهب أو الفضة. (ط،ع) أو حليا إلخ وكذا حلي الخيل وحلية السيف والمصحف والمنطقة واللجام والسرج والأواني، وقال الشافعي: لا تجب الزكاة في حلي النساء، وخاتم الفضة للرجال؛ لما روى جابر الله أنه عليه قال: "ليس في الحلي زكاة"؛ ولأنه مبتذل في مباح وليس بنام فأشبه بثياب البذلة ولنا أن امرأة أتت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وفي يد ابنتها مسكتان [؟] ، فقال عليها: "أتعطين زكاة هذا؟ قالت: "لا"، قال: "أيسرك أن يسورك بسوارين من نار، ورأى عليها في يدي عائشة لها فتخات فقال لها: "أتودين زكاتهن؟" فقالت: "لا"، قال: "حسبك من النار"، وعموم قوله تعالى: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يَكْبِرُونَ الذَّهَبَ وَالْفِضَّةَ﴾ (التوبة:٣٤) يتناول الحلي فلا يجوز إخراجه بالرأي، وما رواه من حديث جابر قال البيهقي: لا أصل له وقوله مبتذل في مباح وليس بنام" لا ينفعه؛ لأن عين الذهب والفضة لا يشترط فيهما حقيقة النماء، ولا تسقط زكاتهما بالاستعمال كما إن كان حلي المرأة أكثر من المعتاد تجب فيه الزكاة إجماعاً، والحاصل أن في نصاب الفضة والذهب ربع العشر ولو كانت مثقالاً تبراً أو حلياً؛ لأن النبي عليلها كتب إلى معاذ الله: خذ من كل مائتي درهم خمسة دراهم، ومن كل عشرين نصف مثقال. (فتح، مستخلص آنية من أواني البيت كالإبريق وغيره. (ع)
The Book of Zakat. Chapter on Zakat of Wealth. It is obligatory on two hundred dirhams and twenty dinars one-quarter of a tenth, even if it is ingots, jewelry, or vessels. Then for every five, according to that calculation. This is the nisab of silver. This is the nisab of gold. (Fath) Chapter on Zakat of Wealth: [It means in explanation of its rulings, and he intended by 'wealth' other than grazing livestock; because its ruling was mentioned previously. (A) Wealth is a name for that which is possessed and stored, and the definite article here refers to what is customary in his statement: "Pay one-quarter of a tenth of your wealth" so livestock are excluded; because their zakat is not specified in this way. He presented it before the fifth of treasure-trove and the tenth; because they are like acquired wealth. He presented the two precious metals before goods; because they are the two origins for other wealth in determining values. He presented silver before gold, following the letters of the Messenger of God. Two hundred dirhams etc.: Because both Sheikhs reported: "There is no charity on less than five ounces", and the ounce in their days was forty dirhams, so five ounces equals two hundred dirhams. And his statement: "There is no charity on less than twenty dinars" which is the nisab of gold. And his statement: one-quarter of a tenth; because of his statement upon him: "On silver one-quarter of a tenth, and on twenty dinars half a dinar". (Ayni) One-quarter of a tenth means one part of forty. So on two hundred dirhams, five dirhams; on twenty dinars, half a dinar. (A) Even if it is an ingot, which is a piece taken from the mine, unstruck, of gold or silver. (T, A) Or jewelry etc., and likewise jewelry of horses, adornment of sword, mushaf, belt, bridle, saddle, and vessels. Al-Shafi'i said: Zakat is not obligatory on women's jewelry and a silver ring for men; because of the hadith of Jabir that he said: "There is no zakat on jewelry"; and because it is used for permissible purposes and is not growing, so it resembles worn clothes. Our proof: A woman came to the Prophet and on her daughter's hand were two anklets [?], and he said: "Do you pay zakat on this?" She said: "No." He said: "Would it please you that God should put two bracelets of fire on you?" And he saw on the hands of Aisha some rings and said to her: "Do you pay their zakat?" She said: "No." He said: "That is sufficient for you from the Fire." And the generality of His statement: "And those who hoard gold and silver" (9:34) includes jewelry, so it cannot be dismissed by opinion. As for what he narrated from the hadith of Jabir, al-Bayhaqi said: It has no basis. And his statement 'it is used for permissible purposes and is not growing' does not benefit him; because the substance of gold and silver does not require actual growth, and its zakat is not dropped by use. And if a woman's jewelry exceeds the customary amount, zakat is due on it by consensus. The conclusion: On the nisab of silver and gold, one-quarter of a tenth, even if it is an ingot or jewelry; because the Prophet wrote to Mu'adh: Take from every two hundred dirhams five dirhams, and from every twenty half a mithqal. (Fath, Mustakhlis: Vessels are household utensils like the pitcher etc.)
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the obligation of zakat on jewelry. The passage begins by stating the basic ruling: zakat is obligatory on silver when it reaches 200 dirhams and on gold when it reaches 20 dinars, at the rate of one-quarter of a tenth (2.5%). This applies regardless of whether the wealth is in the form of ingots (tibr), jewelry (hily), or vessels (āniyah). The commentary (Fath) explains that the nisab for silver is based on the hadith from Bukhari and Muslim: 'There is no charity on less than five ounces' (each ounce being 40 dirhams, totaling 200 dirhams). For gold, the hadith states: 'There is no charity on less than twenty dinars.' The rate of one-quarter of a tenth is derived from the Prophet's instruction to take half a dinar from twenty dinars and five dirhams from two hundred dirhams. The text then addresses the view of al-Shafi'i, who exempts women's jewelry and men's silver rings from zakat, relying on a hadith of Jabir and the argument that jewelry is for use and not for growth. The Hanafi response presents counter-evidences: the Prophet's questioning of a woman with anklets and of Aisha with rings, threatening them with fire if they do not pay zakat. The generality of Quran 9:34 (condemning hoarders) is also invoked. The hadith of Jabir is declared weak by al-Bayhaqi. The Hanafi position is that the substance of gold and silver itself is subject to zakat, irrespective of use or form. If jewelry exceeds the customary amount, zakat is due by consensus. The passage concludes that the same ruling applies to ingots and vessels, citing the letter of the Prophet to Mu'adh. This is a classic Hanafi position: zakat is tied to the substance of gold and silver, not to its intended use or growth potential.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): The minimum threshold of wealth that triggers zakat obligation: 200 dirhams of silver or 20 dinars of gold.
ربع العشر (rub' al-'ushr): One-quarter of a tenth, i.e., 2.5% or 1/40 of the nisab.
حلي (hily): Jewelry made of gold or silver, worn by men or women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No, because it is for personal use.
B) Yes, because the substance is gold or silver.
C) Only if it is excessive.
D) Only if she intends to sell it.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, zakat on jewelry is wajib because the obligation attaches to the substance of gold and silver, not to their form or intended use.

Zakat on Surplus Wealth: The One-Fifth Condition
Ruling with proof and dispute on zakat for surplus wealth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi condition of one-fifth for zakat on surplus wealth and evaluate the opposing arguments from the Sahibayn and Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Surplus wealth is exempt from zakat until it reaches one-fifth of the nisab.

This passage tackles a classic dispute over whether zakat is due on every extra dirham above the nisab or only when the increase reaches a significant threshold. The Hanafi position, relying on specific hadiths, sets the condition at one-fifth. We will walk through the proofs and the opposing reasoning to understand the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that Abu Hanifa holds no zakat on surplus unless it reaches one-fifth of the nisab—40 dirhams for silver or 4 dinars for gold.
This is the 'afw' (exempted) amount.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Note that Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that zakat is due on any surplus, regardless of its size.
They argue from general zakat texts.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine their dalil: generality of Quranic and hadith commands on zakat on gold and silver, and the idea that zakat is gratitude for wealth beyond the nisab.
The nisab is a threshold, not a recurring exemption.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis counter with specific hadiths (Mu'adh and Amr ibn Hazm) and the principle of hardship removal. These texts qualify the general commands.
Specific texts (khass) restrict the general (amm) per Hanafi usul.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Work through a concrete example: 200 dirhams + 10 dirhams. Hanafi: zakat on 200 only. Opponents: zakat on 210.
The difference is 0.25 dirhams on the 10 dirhams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فى كل خمس بحسابه بضم الخاء أي في كل خمس نصاب، وهو أربعون درهما من الورق وأربعة دنانير من الذهب. (ع)] أي بحساب كل النصاب، يعني - كما أنه يجب في كل النصاب من ا الفضة والذهب ربع عشره يجب في الزائد عليه ربع العشر أيضاً بشرط أن يكون الزائد خمس النصاب، ولا يجب شيء إذا كان الزائد أقل من خمسة =  باب زكاة المال الأوزان المعتبرة والمعتبر وزنهما أداء ووجوباً، وفي الدراهم وزن سبعة، وهو أن يكون العشرة في بلوغ النصاب الذهب والفضة لا قيمتهما أي المعتبر فيها منا وزن سبعة مثاقيل وغالب الورق ورق لا عكسه أي من الدراهم خمس أي ذلك الاعتبار، مثلاً: نصاب الفضة مائتان، فلو زاد على هذا المقدار درهم أو درهمان إلى تسعة وثلاثين درهماً لا تجب في الزيادة عنده شيء، وإذا زاد أربعون درهماً وهو النصاب يجب فيه درهم لهذه الزائدة، وكذا نصاب الذهب عشرون مثقالاً، فلو زاد عليه مثقال أو مثقالان أو ثلاثة لا يجب فيه شيء، فإذا زاد أربعة مثاقيل وهو خمس النصاب يجب في هذه الأربعة . ربع العشر، وهو قيراطان؛ لأن المثقال عشرون قيراطاً، وأربعة مثاقيل يساوي ثمانين قيراطاً، ورابع عشره قيراطان وهكذا ما بين الخمس إلى الخمس عفو عنده في الفضة والذهب؛ لقوله عليها في حديث معاذ الله: "لا تأخذ من الكسور شيئاً"، وقوله في حديث عمرو ابن حزم" ليس في ما دون الأربعين صدقة"؛ ولأن الحرج مدفوع شرعاً، وفي إيجاب الكسر ،الحرج، وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد والشافعي: يجب في ربع عشره، ولو كان الزائد درهماً أو مثقالاً أو غير ذلك لإطلاق النصوص؛ ولأن الزكاة وجبت شكرا لنعمة المال واشتراط النصاب في الابتداء لتحقق الغنى، فلا معنى لاشتراطه بالخمس وغيره بعد ذلك. (محشي)
In every five according to its calculation – with a damm on the kha' – meaning in every fifth of the nisab, which is forty dirhams of silver and four dinars of gold. (A) That is according to the calculation of the entire nisab, meaning just as on the entire nisab of silver and gold one-quarter of a tenth is obligatory, on the surplus also one-quarter of a tenth is obligatory, on condition that the surplus is one-fifth of the nisab. Nothing is obligatory if the surplus is less than five [dirhams/dinars]. [PAGE_203] Chapter on Zakat of Wealth: Standard weights. The weight of both is considered in payment and obligation. In dirhams, the weight of seven is considered: that ten dirhams should be... In reaching the nisab, gold and silver (not their value) are considered. That which is considered in them... from us is the weight of seven mithqals. Mostly the silver is silver, not the opposite. That is from the dirhams, five is that consideration. For example: the nisab of silver is two hundred. If an increase of one or two dirhams up to thirty-nine dirhams is added, nothing is obligatory on the increase according to him. But if forty dirhams are added (which is the nisab), one dirham is obligatory for this increase. Likewise, the nisab of gold is twenty mithqals. If an increase of one, two, or three mithqals is added, nothing is obligatory. If four mithqals are added (which is one-fifth of the nisab), one-quarter of a tenth is obligatory on these four, which is two qirats; because the mithqal is twenty qirats, and four mithqals equal eighty qirats, and one-quarter of a tenth of that is two qirats. Similarly, what is between one-fifth and one-fifth is exempt according to him in silver and gold, because of the Prophet's statement in the hadith of Mu'adh: "Do not take anything from fractions," and his statement in the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm: "There is no charity on less than forty." And because hardship is legally removed, and imposing zakat on fractions causes hardship. Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i said: Zakat is obligatory on one-quarter of a tenth, even if the increase is a dirham or a mithqal or otherwise, because of the generality of the texts; and because zakat became obligatory as gratitude for the blessing of wealth, and the condition of nisab at the beginning is to confirm sufficiency, so there is no meaning to conditioning it on one-fifth or otherwise after that. (Mahshi)
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is an intra- and inter-madhhab dispute about zakat on surplus wealth above the nisab. The Hanafi position (attributed to Abu Hanifa here) holds that no zakat is due on an increase (ziyādah) unless it reaches one-fifth of the nisab – i.e., 40 dirhams for silver or 4 dinars (mithqals) for gold. This is based on two hadiths: the Prophet's instruction to Mu'adh 'Do not take anything from fractions' and the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm 'There is no charity on less than forty'. The rationale is that imposing zakat on small fractions would cause hardship, which Islamic law seeks to avoid. The opposing view is held by the two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) as well as Imam al-Shafi'i: they argue that zakat is due on any amount above the nisab, at the rate of 2.5%, because the general texts command zakat on all gold and silver without qualification. They reason that the nisab condition establishes sufficiency; once that is met, any additional wealth should be subject to zakat as a form of gratitude. The commentary (Mahshi) states that the Hanafi view is the one relied upon (mufta bihi). This dispute has practical consequences: under the Hanafi view, if one has 200 dirhams plus 10 dirhams, no zakat on the 10; under the Sahibayn/Shafi'i view, zakat would be due on 210 dirhams.

Key Terms
الكسور (al-kusur): Fractions; amounts less than a complete nisab-fifth (40 dirhams or 4 dinars).
عفو (afw): The surplus amount between one-fifth increments that is exempt from zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if someone has 200 dirhams and then earns 15 more dirhams, how much zakat is due on the total?
A) Zakat on 215 dirhams at 2.5%
B) Zakat on the original 200 dirhams only
C) No zakat at all until the excess reaches 40 dirhams
D) Zakat on the 15 dirhams only

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa exempts surplus below one-fifth of the nisab to ease hardship, while others require zakat on any excess.

Standard Weights for Zakat: Weight vs. Value
Ruling on standard weights of dirhams and dinars for zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi standard weight for dirhams and apply the rule that zakat nisab and payment are based on weight, including the excise rule for increments of less than one-fifth of the nisab.

Core Idea
Zakat is based on weight, not value; partial increments are exempt until a full fifth of nisab is accumulated.

This lesson establishes the legal standard for dirhams and dinars in zakat calculations. The Hanafi school insists on weight as the primary criterion for both reaching the nisab and fulfilling the payment. Additionally, a unique excise rule exempts fractional increases until they form a complete one-fifth block of the nisab. Understanding this standard and the incremental rule is essential for correctly calculating zakat on precious metals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the standard weights
Recognize that the Hanafi standard dirham weighs 0.7 mithqal (10 dirhams = 7 mithqals) and the mithqal (dinar) weighs 20 qirats (100 barley grains). This was historically derived at the time of Caliph Umar.
The legal dirham is 14 qirats (70 grains).
2
Apply the weight standard to nisab
The nisab for silver is 200 dirhams by weight; for gold, 20 mithqals. Value alone does not trigger obligation unless weight reaches the nisab.
A gold vessel weighing 15 mithqals, even if valuable, incurs no zakat.
3
Apply the excise rule for increments
For wealth above nisab, zakat is due only on complete blocks of one-fifth of the nisab (40 dirhams silver, 4 mithqals gold). Fractions between these blocks are exempt (عف).
E.g., for gold, from 21–23 mithqals: no extra zakat; at 24 mithqals, zakat on the additional 4 mithqals.
4
Apply the weight standard to payment
When paying zakat, the weight of the paid metal must equal the weight of the obligation. Paying less weight, even if of higher value, is invalid.
Paying 4 good dirhams worth 5 poor dirhams for a 5-dirham obligation is invalid due to weight deficiency.
5
Distinguish the intra-Hanafi dispute
Note that Muhammad al-Shaybani prefers what is more beneficial for the poor (value-based), and Zufar considers value alone. However, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: weight governs absolutely.
The two shaykhs' view is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

(محشي) والمعتبر إلخ: يعني أن المعتبر أن يكون المؤدى في الوزن قدر الواجب عند الشيخين، وعند محمد: الأنفع للفقراء، ولا اعتبار للقيمة مثلاً: لو أدى أربعة جيدة قيمتها خمسة ردية عن خمسة لا يجوز؛ لنقصان الوزن، ويعتبر الوزن أيضاً في وجوب الزكاة بالاتفاق، مثلاً: لو كان له إناء ذهب وزنه عشرة مثاقيل، وقيمته مائتا درهم لا تجب الزكاة بالاتفاق؛ لعدم تكامل النصاب في الوزن، وعند زفر تعتبر القيمة، فلو كان له إبريق فضة وزنه مائتان، وقيمته ثلاث مائة، فأدى خمسة جاز عند الشيخين خلافاً لمحمد وزفر، فعندهما أن ينبغي يؤدي سبعة دراهم ونصفاً؛ لأنه أنفع للفقراء باعتبار القيمة. (محشي)
وفي الدراهم إلخ: أصله أن الدراهم كانت على ثلاثة أصناف: صنف منها كل عشرة منه عشرة مثاقيل، وصنف منها كل عشرة منه ستة مثاقيل، وصنف منها كل عشرة منه خمسة ،مثاقيل وكان الناس يتصرفون فيها إلى أن استخلف عمر الفاروق فأراد أن يستوفي الخراج فطالبهم بالأكثر والتمسوا منه التخفيف فجمع محاسبي زمانه ليتوسطوا بين ما رامه ورامته الرعية فاستخرجوا له وزن السبعة بأن جمعوا من كل صنف عشرة دراهم فصار الكل أحدا وعشرين مثقالا، ثم أخذوا ثلث ذلك وكان سبعة مثاقيل، والمثقال – هو الدينار – عشرون قيراطاً، والدرهم أربعة عشرة قيراطاً، والقيراط خمس شعيرات غير مقشورة، فيكون الدرهم الشرعي سبعين شعيرة والمثقال مائة شعيرة. (مسكين) وزن سبعة في الزكاة والنصاب وتقدير الديات والمهر.
مثاقيل: كما أن المعتبر في المثقال أن يكون كل سبعة منه وزن عشرة دراهم ورق أي إذا كانت الغلبة للفضة في الدراهم المضروبة فهي كالدراهم من الفضة الخالصة. (ط) لا عكسه يعني إن كانت الغلبة للغش أي للنحاس والصفر لا يكون ورقا بل في حكم العروض. (ط)] أي لا يكون عكسه ورقاً، بل يكون عروضاً فينظر فإن نواه للتجارة يعتبر قيمته مطلقا، وإن لم ينوه للتجارة ينظر فإن كانت فضته تتخلص تعتبر، فتجب فيها الزكاة إن بلغت نصاباً وحدها أو =
And their weight is considered in payment and obligation. In dirhams, the weight of seven is considered: that the ten [dirhams] should be... In reaching the nisab, gold and silver (not their value) are considered. That which is considered in them... from us is the weight of seven mithqals. Mostly the silver is silver, not the opposite. That is from the dirhams, five is that consideration. For example: the nisab of silver is two hundred. If an increase of one or two dirhams up to thirty-nine dirhams is added, nothing is obligatory on the increase according to him. But if forty dirhams are added (which is the nisab), one dirham is obligatory for this increase. Likewise, the nisab of gold is twenty mithqals. If an increase of one, two, or three mithqals is added, nothing is obligatory. If four mithqals are added (which is one-fifth of the nisab), one-quarter of a tenth is obligatory on these four, which is two qirats; because the mithqal is twenty qirats, and four mithqals equal eighty qirats, and one-quarter of a tenth of that is two qirats. Similarly, what is between one-fifth and one-fifth is exempt according to him in silver and gold, because of the Prophet's statement in the hadith of Mu'adh: "Do not take anything from fractions," and his statement in the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm: "There is no charity on less than forty." And because hardship is legally removed, and imposing zakat on fractions causes hardship. Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i said: Zakat is obligatory on one-quarter of a tenth, even if the increase is a dirham or a mithqal or otherwise, because of the generality of the texts; and because zakat became obligatory as gratitude for the blessing of wealth, and the condition of nisab at the beginning is to confirm sufficiency, so there is no meaning to conditioning it on one-fifth or otherwise after that. (Mahshi) 'And the weight is considered' etc.: It means that what is considered is that what is paid should be equal in weight to what is obligatory according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). According to Muhammad: whatever is more beneficial for the poor. Value is not considered. For example, if someone pays four good dirhams whose value is five poor dirhams for five [obligatory], it is not permissible due to the deficiency in weight. Weight is also considered in the obligation of zakat by agreement. For example, if he has a gold vessel weighing ten mithqals and its value is two hundred dirhams, zakat is not obligatory by agreement, because the nisab is not completed in weight. According to Zufar, value is considered. If he has a silver pitcher weighing two hundred [dirhams] and its value is three hundred, and he pays five [dirhams], it is permissible according to the two shaykhs, contrary to Muhammad and Zufar. According to them, he should pay seven and a half dirhams, because it is more beneficial for the poor in consideration of value. (Mahshi) 'And in dirhams' etc.: Its origin is that dirhams were of three types: a type where ten of them were ten mithqals, a type where ten of them were six mithqals, and a type where ten of them were five mithqals. People dealt with them until Umar al-Faruq became caliph. He wanted to collect the kharaj, so he demanded the maximum, and they asked him for a reduction. He gathered the accountants of his time to mediate between his desire and the desire of the subjects. They derived the weight of seven by collecting ten dirhams from each type, so the total was twenty-one mithqals. Then they took one-third of that, which was seven mithqals. The mithqal (which is the dinar) is twenty qirats, the dirham is fourteen qirats, and the qirat is five hulled barley grains. Thus, the legal dirham is seventy grains, and the mithqal is one hundred grains. (Miskin) The weight of seven is [used] in zakat, nisab, and estimation of diyat and mahr. Mithqals: Just as the mithqal is considered such that every seven of them weigh ten dirhams. That is, if the silver predominates in the minted dirhams, they are like pure silver dirhams. (T) Not the opposite: meaning if the predominance is of alloy (i.e., copper or brass), it is not silver but rather in the ruling of trade goods. (T) That is, its opposite is not silver; rather it is a commodity. So it is considered: if he intended it for trade, his value is considered absolutely; if he did not intend it for trade, it is considered that if its silver can be purified, it is considered, and zakat becomes obligatory on it if it reaches a nisab by itself or =
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage deals with the standard weights of dirhams and dinars for the purpose of zakat calculation. It establishes that zakat is based on weight, not market value, both in determining whether the nisab is reached and in the actual payment of zakat. The Hanafi school holds that the weight of the dirham (silver coin) is standardized at seven tenths of a mithqal (i.e., 10 dirhams = 7 mithqals). This standard was historically derived during the caliphate of Umar by taking an average of three types of dirhams in circulation. The legal dirham is defined as 14 qirats (each qirat = 5 hulled barley grains), totaling 70 barley grains; the mithqal (dinar) is 20 qirats = 100 barley grains. The commentary mentions an ikhtilaf among Hanafi imams: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs), zakat must be paid in weight equal to the obligation; if one pays good dirhams whose weight is less than required, it is invalid even if their value is higher. However, according to Muhammad al-Shaybani, the more beneficial option for the poor should be chosen (i.e., pay by value). Zufar goes further, considering value alone in determining obligation. The majority Hanafi position (the two shaykhs) is that weight is determinative for both obligation and payment. The passage also clarifies that if a coin has a predominance of alloy (ghish), it is not treated as silver but as a trade commodity; if intended for trade, its entire value is considered for zakat; otherwise, only the silver content if it can be purified.

Key Terms
وزن سبعة (wazn sab'ah): The standard weight: 10 dirhams = 7 mithqals, i.e., 1 dirham = 0.7 mithqal.
الغالب (al-ghālib): The predominant metal in a coin; if silver predominates, it is silver; if alloy, it is a commodity.
العفو (al-'afw): Exemption: fractions of wealth between one-fifth blocks of nisab are exempt from zakat.
خمس النصاب (khums al-nisāb): One-fifth of the nisab: 40 dirhams for silver, 4 mithqals for gold. The threshold at which zakat becomes due on increases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (two shaykhs), if a person owes 5 dirhams in zakat but pays 4 dirhams that are worth 5 dirhams of lower quality, is the zakat valid?
A) Yes, because the value is equal.
B) No, because the weight is deficient.
C) Yes, if the recipient agrees.
D) Only if the payer is poor.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, zakat on silver and gold is determined by weight, not value; the nisab is 200 dirhams/20 mithqals, and increments are only zakatable when they form complete one-fifth blocks of the nisab.

Zakat on Fractional Increases: The 'Afw Threshold
Establishes no zakat on increases less than one-fifth nisab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on fractional increases above nisab, apply the one-fifth threshold to gold and silver, and evaluate the opposing evidence from Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
No zakat on fractional increases below one-fifth of nisab — 'afw is the rule.

This passage addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute: when does an increase above the zakat nisab become subject to zakat? Abu Hanifa holds that small fractions are exempt ('afw) until they reach a complete one-fifth (khums) of the nisab. His two foremost students and al-Shafi'i disagree, arguing that any increase, however small, incurs zakat. The ruling directly affects how Muslims calculate zakat on savings that grow incrementally.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what Abu Hanifa rules regarding fractional increases above nisab for both silver and gold. Note the specific thresholds: 40 dirhams for silver and 4 mithqals for gold.
These thresholds represent one-fifth (khums) of the respective nisab.
2
Identify the opposing view
Determine the position of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and al-Shafi'i. They require zakat on any increase, even a single dirham or mithqal.
This is a rare intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf where the two Sahibayn differ from Abu Hanifa.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
Analyze the two hadiths cited: the command not to take from fractions and the rule 'no sadaqah on less than forty.' Understand how these prove exemption for fractional amounts.
The hadith on sheep (40) is analogized to fractional wealth.
4
Analyse the opposing proof
Examine the opponents' reasoning: general zakat texts, nisab as a one-time condition, and gratitude as the basis for zakat. Understand why they reject a second threshold.
They argue that once wealth reaches nisab, all further increases are immediately subject to zakat.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Apply the khums rule to a concrete example: a person with 210 dirhams of silver. According to Abu Hanifa, only 5 dirhams zakat (on the first 200) is due; the extra 10 is exempt. The opponents would require 5.25 dirhams.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf — the real-world difference in zakat payable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مثلاً: نصاب الفضة مائتان، فلو زاد على هذا المقدار درهم أو درهمان إلى تسعة وثلاثين درهماً لا تجب في الزيادة عنده شيء، وإذا زاد أربعون درهماً وهو النصاب يجب فيه درهم لهذه الزائدة، وكذا نصاب الذهب عشرون مثقالاً، فلو زاد عليه مثقال أو مثقالان أو ثلاثة لا يجب فيه شيء، فإذا زاد أربعة مثاقيل وهو خمس النصاب يجب في هذه الأربعة ربع العشر، وهو قيراطان؛ لأن المثقال عشرون قيراطاً، وأربعة مثاقيل يساوي ثمانين قيراطاً، الزائد أيضاً . وربع عشره قيراطان وهكذا ما بين الخمس إلى الخمس عفو عنده في الفضة والذهب؛ لقوله عليه السلام في حديث معاذ: "لا تأخذ من الكسور شيئاً"، وقوله في حديث عمرو ابن حزم: "ليس في ما دون الأربعين صدقة"؛ ولأن الحرج مدفوع شرعاً، وفي إيجاب الكسر الحرج، وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد والشافعي: يجب في ربع عشره، ولو كان الزائد درهماً أو مثقالاً أو غير ذلك لإطلاق النصوص؛ ولأن الزكاة وجبت شكرا لنعمة المال واشتراط النصاب في الابتداء لتحقق الغنى، فلا معنى لاشتراطه بالخمس وغيره بعد ذلك.
For example: the nisab of silver is two hundred (dirhams). If there is an increase of one or two dirhams up to thirty-nine dirhams, nothing is due on the increase according to him (Abu Hanifa). When it increases by forty dirhams—which is the (full) nisab—one dirham is due for this increase. Likewise, the nisab of gold is twenty mithqals. If there is an increase of one, two, or three mithqals, nothing is due. When it increases by four mithqals—which is one-fifth of the nisab—one-quarter of a tenth is due on these four, which is two qirats, because the mithqal is twenty qirats, and four mithqals equal eighty qirats, and one-quarter of a tenth of that is two qirats. Thus, between one-fifth and the next fifth is exempt (afw) according to him regarding silver and gold, due to his (the Prophet's) statement in the hadith of Mu'adh: 'Do not take anything from fractions,' and his statement in the hadith of 'Amr ibn Hazm: 'There is no sadaqah on less than forty (sheep).' Also, hardship is legally removed, and imposing (zakat on) fractions entails hardship. Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i said: Zakat is due on one-quarter of a tenth (i.e., on any increase, even a dirham or mithqal or otherwise), due to the generality of the texts; because zakat is obligatory as gratitude for the blessing of wealth, and the condition of nisab applies only at the start to establish sufficiency; there is no meaning to requiring one-fifth increments thereafter.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the majority (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and al-Shafi'i) regarding zakat on fractional increases above the nisab. Abu Hanifa holds that zakat is not due on any increase until it reaches a complete additional one-fifth (khums) of the nisab. For silver (nisab 200 dirhams), increases from 1 to 39 dirhams are exempt; only when the increase reaches 40 dirhams (one-fifth of 200) does zakat become due on that amount. Similarly for gold (nisab 20 mithqals), increases up to 3 mithqals are exempt; at 4 mithqals (one-fifth of 20) zakat is due. The basis for this is two hadiths: one instructing not to take from fractions, and another stating no sadaqah on less than forty (sheep)—this analogy is extended to fractional wealth. Additionally, requiring zakat on small increments would cause hardship. The opposing view argues that any increase, however small, incurs zakat because the primary texts are general, and the nisab condition is only for initiating the obligation, not for subsequent increases. Abu Hanifa's position is considered mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
العفو (al-'afw): The portion of wealth between one-fifth increments of nisab that is exempt from zakat.
الخمس (al-khums): One-fifth of the nisab; the threshold at which zakat becomes due on increases (e.g., 40 dirhams for silver, 4 mithqals for gold).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a person has 220 dirhams of silver, how much zakat is due on the extra 20 dirhams?
A) 0 dirhams (exempt)
B) 0.5 dirham
C) 1 dirham
D) It depends on the market value

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, fractional increases above the nisab are exempt from zakat until they accumulate to one-fifth of the nisab, based on prophetic hadith and the principle of avoiding hardship.

Zakah on Trade Goods: Nisab, Valuation, and Ikhtilaf
Detailed ruling on zakah for trade goods with proofs and disagreements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for zakah on trade goods, explain the three Hanafi valuation methods, and apply the rule of inclusion (damm) of gold and silver to determine zakah liability.

Core Idea
Trade goods are subject to zakah when their value reaches nisab at both ends of the year; valuation method and metal inclusion affect liability.

This lesson unpacks the detailed Hanafi ruling on zakah for trade goods (ʿurūḍ al-tijārah). You will learn the nisab requirement, the condition of intention, and the critical differences among the three senior Hanafi imams on how to value goods and whether to add gold and silver together. Understanding these points is essential for accurately calculating zakah on business inventory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine that zakah on trade goods (ʿurūḍ al-tijārah) is wajib according to the Hanafi school. Note that this is derived from the generality of the hadith about dirhams.
2
State the nisab condition
The nisab (200 dirhams silver or 20 mithqals gold) must be present at both the beginning and end of the lunar year. Deficiency during the year does not harm. Intention of trade (niyyat al-tijārah) is also required.
The double-end condition distinguishes zakah on trade goods from other types of wealth.
3
Determine the valuation method
Understand the three Hanafi positions: Abu Hanifa values at the metal most beneficial for the poor (usually silver), Abu Yusuf at the purchase currency (if cash), and Muhammad at the prevalent currency of the locality. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
4
Apply the rule of inclusion (damm) of gold and silver
Gold and silver are added together to complete nisab. Abu Hanifa adds by value; the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) add by parts (e.g., half nisab of one plus half of the other). The mufta bihi is the two companions' method in later fatwa.
The practical outcome differs depending on which method is used, as shown in the numerical examples.
5
Evaluate practical outcomes
Work through examples: (1) 10 dinars and 50 dirhams – Abu Hanifa sees complete nisab by value, the two companions do not. (2) 150 dirhams and 5 dinars of low value – the two companions see nisab by parts, Abu Hanifa does not. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf.

من
في طرفيه أي أول الحول وآخره، سواء كان نصاب السوائم أو الذهب أو الفضة أو مال التجارة. (مسكين) الثمنين: أي الذهب والفضة فلو لم تكن العروض للتجارة وعنده مال لا يبلغ نصابا لا يضم العروض لتكميل النصاب فلا زكاة عليه مسكين والذهب إلى الفضة قيمة بأن كان له عشرة مثاقيل من الذهب ومائة درهم الفضة أحدهما إلى الآخر ليتم النصاب، وقال الشافعي لا يضم والمعتبر كمال النصاب في كل منهما؛ : يضم لأنهما جنسان، وبه قال أحمد ولنا أنهما في الثمنية سيآن فلا يعتبر الاختلاف في الصورة، ثم الضم من حيث القيمة عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما يضم بالأجزاء، حتى لو كان أحدهما ثلث نصاب لا بد أن يكون الآخر ثلثي نصاب، وعلى هذا سائر الأجزاء كالنصف والربع وغيرهما، وثمرته تظهر فيما إذا كان له عشرة دنانير وخمسون درهماً وقيمة الدنانير لجودتها مائة وخمسون درهماً أو قيمة خمسين درهماً عشرة دنانير تجب الزكاة عنده لتكامل النصاب في الصورتين بالقيمة خلافاً لهما؛ لأن عشرة دنانير نصف النصاب، وخمسون درهما ربعه، فالنصف والربع لا يتمان النصاب، وإذا كانت مائة وخمسين درهماً وخمسة دنانير وقيمتها أقل من خمسين درهماً، فعلى قولهما تحب؟ لتكامل النصاب بالأجزاء، ولا تجب عند أبي حنيفة لنقصان النصاب. (عيني وغيره)
Chapter of Zakah on Wealth. Nisab of trade goods. And regarding trade goods that have reached the nisab of silver or gold, and deficiency of nisab during the year does not harm. It is two hundred dirhams and twenty mithqals in zakatable wealth. If it is complete at both ends, and the value of trade goods is added to the two [precious metals], and gold is added to silver by value. That is, the nisab at the beginning and end of the year. That which is for trade, i.e., gold and silver. That is, it is added. By addition to others, and if nothing is realized from it, then nothing is due, so the consideration remains for the trade goods, and intention of trade is required. And on this detail is adulterated gold. He did not mention it, relying on the mention of silver. Then predominance is that it exceeds half; if they are equal, it is said: zakat is obligatory as a precaution, and it is said: it is not obligatory, and it is said: one and a half dirhams are obligatory. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/124] And 'In 'urud' etc. is conjunct to his statement: 'In two hundred dirhams', meaning one-quarter of a tenth is also obligatory in trade goods. And al-'urud (with damm on 'ayn) is the plural of 'ard (with fatha), which is merchandise other than gold and silver. (al-'Ayni) 'Balaghat nisab wariq' etc.: It is a condition in zakat of trade goods that their value reaches the nisab of silver or gold, and the most beneficial for the poor is considered according to Abu Hanifa, in that he values it at what reaches a nisab. For example, if valued in silver it reaches two hundred dirhams, and if valued in gold it reaches nineteen mithqals, then he values it in silver. From Abu Yusuf: he values it at what he purchased with, if the price was in currency, otherwise by the prevalent currency. From Muhammad: he values it by the prevalent currency in all cases, so he values it in the city he is in, and if in a desert he values it in the city he is traveling to, and he values it in minted dirhams and dinars. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/124) And the obligation of zakat on trade goods is due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'From every two hundred dirhams, five dirhams are due.' So by its generality it includes trade goods and others. (al-'Ayni and others) 'La yadurr' [i.e., does not prevent the obligation of zakat]. And al-Shafi'i said: Completion of nisab for grazing livestock from the beginning of the year to its end is a condition, and in trade wealth completion is considered at its end. Al-'Ayni said: Completion of nisab is a condition for the commencement of the year, and its completion is a condition for obligation at its end. In between, it is not the time of commencement nor the time of obligation, so it does not prevent the obligation of zakat. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/124] 'Min' 'Fi tarafayhi' means beginning and end of the year, whether it is nisab of grazing livestock or gold or silver or trade wealth. (Miskin) 'Ath-thamanayn': i.e., gold and silver. So if the trade goods are not for trade and he has wealth that does not reach a nisab, the trade goods are not added to complete the nisab, so no zakat is due on him. (Miskin) 'Wa al-dhahab ila al-fiddah qimah' meaning if he has ten mithqals of gold and one hundred dirhams of silver, one is added to the other to complete the nisab. Al-Shafi'i said: they are not added, and completion of nisab in each is considered; because they are two different types, and Ahmad said the same. Our evidence: they are equal in being currency, so the difference in form is not considered. Then, addition in terms of value according to Abu Hanifa, but according to them (the two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) addition is by parts, such that if one is one-third nisab, the other must be two-thirds nisab, and likewise for other parts like half and quarter etc. Its practical outcome appears in the case where he has ten dinars and fifty dirhams, and the value of the dinars due to their quality is one hundred and fifty dirhams, or the value of fifty dirhams is ten dinars: zakat is obligatory according to him (Abu Hanifa) because the nisab is completed in both cases by value, contrary to them; because ten dinars is half the nisab, and fifty dirhams is a quarter, so half and quarter do not complete the nisab. And if he has one hundred and fifty dirhams and five dinars whose value is less than fifty dirhams, then according to them it is obligatory because the nisab is completed by parts, but it is not obligatory according to Abu Hanifa due to deficiency of nisab. (al-'Ayni and others)
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion on the ruling of zakah on trade goods (urud al-tijarah). It begins by stating the nisab: trade goods are subject to zakah if their value reaches the nisab of silver (200 dirhams) or gold (20 mithqals). The condition is that the nisab must be complete at the beginning and end of the lunar year; deficiency during the year does not harm. The value of the trade goods is added to gold and silver held, and gold is added to silver by value. The intention of trade (niyyat al-tijarah) is essential. The passage then discusses various intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa considers the most beneficial valuation for the poor (i.e., whichever of gold or silver gives a lower nisab threshold so more items are taxable), while Abu Yusuf values based on the purchase price currency, and Muhammad always uses the prevalent currency of the locality. The proof for zakah on trade goods is the Hadith: 'From every two hundred dirhams, five dirhams are due,' which by its generality covers all wealth including trade goods. There is a disagreement with al-Shafi'i who requires the nisab to be complete throughout the year for livestock, but accepts end-of-year completion for trade goods. The Hanafi position is that nisab completion at both ends is sufficient. A key issue is the inclusion (damm) of gold and silver to complete nisab. Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differ on the method: Abu Hanifa adds them by value, while the two companions add them by parts (e.g., half of one plus half of the other). The practical outcome is illustrated with numerical examples showing when zakah becomes wajib or not under each opinion. The mufta bihi position is not explicitly stated in this passage, but typically the Hanafi school follows Abu Hanifa's view on valuation (the most beneficial for the poor) and the two companions' view on addition by parts is also considered, with the choice depending on context.

Key Terms
العروض (al-ʿurūḍ): Plural of ʿarḍ, meaning merchandise or goods other than gold and silver coins (naqdayn).
النصاب (al-niṣāb): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers the obligation of zakah; for silver 200 dirhams, for gold 20 mithqals.
الضم (al-ḍamm): Inclusion: combining different types of wealth (e.g., gold and silver) to complete the nisab for zakah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the condition regarding the nisab of trade goods during the year?
A) Must be complete every day.
B) Must be complete at the start and end of the year.
C) Must be complete at the middle of the year.
D) It is not required if the goods are for trade.

Key Takeaway
Zakah on trade goods is wajib when their value reaches nisab at both year-end points, and the method of valuation and inclusion of metals can affect the obligation.

The 'Ashir: Role, Conditions, and Testimony Rules
Explanation of the 'ashir and rules of testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the role and conditions of the 'ashir (zakah collector) and apply the Hanafi rules of testimony when a trader claims an excuse.

Core Idea
The 'ashir must be a free, Muslim, non-Hashimi protector; his testimony is accepted under oath, but a certificate of discharge may not be required.

Zakat in the Hanafi school is not only an individual obligation but also a state-administered system. The Imam appoints an official, known as the 'ashir, to collect zakat from traders passing on roads. This lesson examines the 'ashir's qualifications, his duties, and the rules of testimony when traders offer excuses. We will also see an internal Hanafi difference on whether a written certificate is necessary.

Guided Path
1
Define the 'ashir and distinguish from the sa'i
Identify who the 'ashir is and how he differs from the sa'i who collects livestock zakat from tribes.
Both are types of musaddiq (collector).
2
List the conditions for the 'ashir
From the text, extract the required qualifications: free, Muslim, not Hashimi, capable of protection, etc.
The condition 'not a mawla of a Hashimi' is also mentioned.
3
Understand the trader's claims and the oath
When a trader claims an excuse (e.g., year not completed, debt, paid elsewhere) and swears, he is believed if he produces a certificate.
This is the default ruling.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on the certificate (bara'ah)
The text notes that in al-Jami' al-Saghir and according to Abu Yusuf, the certificate is not required; the 'ashir's word suffices. Identify the mufta bihi.
The dispute is on procedural requirement, not on the underlying trust.

باب العاشر: ألحقه بالزكاة؛ لأن بعض ما يأخذه زكاة وليس متمحضاً فلهذا أخره، وقدمه على الركاز؛ لما فيه من معنى العبادة مأخوذ "من" عشرت القوم أعشرهم عشراً" بالضم فيهما إذا أخذت عشر أموالهم، والمراد بالعشر: ما يأخذه العاشر عشراً كان أو ربعه أو نصفه، فإنه صار علم جنس عليه، وعلم الجنس ما وضع بإزاء الماهية بقيد حضورها في الذهن. نصبه الإمام على الطريق فخرج الساعي فإنه الذي يسعى في القبائل ليأخذ صدقات المواشي من أماكنها. (ط) ليأخذ الصدقات: فيه تغليب لما يؤخذ من المسلمين لكونه عبادة على ما يؤخذ من غيرهم، أي يأخذ الزكوات ويحمي التجار، وهذا فائدة نصبه، ومن ثم شرط فيه أن يكون حراً مسلماً غير هاشمي؛ لأنه لا حماية لعبد ولا كافر، وأما الهاشمي فلأن المأخوذ فيه شبهة الزكاة وأن يكون قادرا على الحماية ومنها ظهور المال وحضور المالك، وأن لا يكون مولى هاشمي وهذه شروط العاشر وهل تشترط هذه الشروط كلها في الساعي الذي يسعى في القبائل ليأخذ صدقة المواشي؟ والمصدق على وزن اسم فاعل من التفعيل اسم جنس للعاشر والساعي، والمصدق بتشديد الصاد والدال هو رب المال وما ورد من ذم العاشر محمول على من يظلم كما في زماننا وكما أنه يأخذ العاشر صدقات الأموال الظاهرة يأخذ صدقات الأموال الباطنة التي تكون مع التجار؛ لأنها تصير ظاهرة بالخروج إلى الفيافي لاحتياجها حينئذ إلى الحماية والأخذ يحمله على الحماية. (فتح)
التجار: المارين بأموالهم الظاهرة والباطنة عليه، ويحميهم من اللصوص وقطاع الطريق، ويشترط أن يكون العاشر حرا مسلما. (ط،ع) فمن قال إلخ: اعلم أن شرط ولاية الأخذ وجوب الزكاة، فكل ما وجوده مسقط فالحكم كذلك إذا ادعاه، فلو قال: لم يتم الحول أنكر الوجوب، وكذا لو قال: لم أنو التجارة أو قال: ليس هذا المال لي بل هو وديعة أو بضاعة أو مضاربة أو أنا أجير فيه أو علي دين العباد أو قال: ليس في هذا المال صدقة وإن لم يبين
السبب، وإطلاق الدين يعم غير المحيط، وقوله: "إلى عاشر آخر"؛ لأنه ادعى وضع الأمانة موضعها. (فتح) الحول أي على المال الذي في يده. (ط) أو أديت: أي لو قال: أديت زكاتي إلى عاشر آخر أو قال: أنا أديت للفقراء بنفسي ما وجب عليّ. :
التحليف للتصديق وهو القياس [تبيين الحقائق: ٨٤/٢]
Chapter of the 'Ashir: i.e., explaining its rulings. Chapter of the 'Ashir. He is the one appointed by the Imam to take charities (sadaqat) from traders. So whoever says: 'The year has not completed,' or 'I have a debt,' or 'I have paid (zakat) to another 'ashir,' and swears, he is believed. The 'Ashir. [Commentary: 'muhit biha li' seems garbled]. The chapter of the 'Ashir: He attached it to zakah because part of what he takes is zakah, and it is not purely that, so he delayed it. He placed it before [the chapter on] rikaz because it has an element of worship. Derived from 'ashartu al-qawm a'shiruhum 'ashran' (with damm in both) when you take a tenth of their wealth. By 'ushr is meant what the 'ashir takes, whether a tenth, a quarter, or a half, for it has become a generic term. And a generic term is what stands for the essence with the restriction of its presence in the mind. (Fath) His appointment by the Imam on the road; thus the sa'i is excluded, for he is the one who goes to the tribes to take sadaqat of livestock from their places. (T) 'To take charities': here is a predominance of what is taken from Muslims because it is worship over what is taken from non-Muslims. He takes zakats and protects traders, and this is the benefit of his appointment. Hence it is required that he be free, Muslim, not Hashimi, because a slave or non-Muslim cannot provide protection. As for the Hashimi, because what is taken has a resemblance to zakat. And he must be capable of protection, including that the wealth be apparent and the owner present, and that he not be a mawla of a Hashimi. These are the conditions of the 'ashir. Are all these conditions required in the sa'i who goes to the tribes to take sadaqat of livestock? And al-musaddiq (on the measure of ism fa'il from taf'il) is a generic term for the 'ashir and sa'i. Al-musaddiq (with shaddah on sad and dal) is the owner of the wealth. What has been mentioned about condemning the 'ashir is to be understood as the one who oppresses, as in our time. And just as the 'ashir takes sadaqat of apparent wealth, he also takes sadaqat of hidden wealth that is with traders, because it becomes apparent by going out to the deserts due to its need for protection then, and taking it obligates him to protect. (Fath) 'Traders': those passing by with their apparent and hidden wealth, and he protects them from thieves and highway robbers. It is required that the 'ashir be free and Muslim. (T, A) 'So whoever says' etc.: Know that the condition for his authority to take is the obligation of zakah. So everything whose existence nullifies [obligation] is similarly [ruled] if he claims it. So if he says: 'The year has not completed,' he denies the obligation. Similarly if he says: 'I did not intend trade,' or 'This wealth is not mine, but rather it is a deposit or merchandise or mudarabah or I am an employee over it, or I have a debt due to people,' or he says: 'There is no sadaqah in this wealth,' even if he does not specify the reason. And the absolute term 'debt' includes even non-encircling debt. His statement: 'to another 'ashir' because he claims he placed the trust in its proper place. (Fath) 'The year': i.e., on the wealth in his hand. (T) 'Or I have paid': i.e., if he says: 'I paid my zakat to another 'ashir,' or he says: 'I paid myself what was obligatory upon me to the poor.' (T, A) 'Another 'ashir' and in that year there was indeed another 'ashir, otherwise he is not believed. 'He is believed': pertains to all, and it is in the accusative as a state or conjunct to 'qala'. This is if he produces a certificate of discharge (bara'ah), i.e., a document of release. If he does not produce it, he is not believed. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, producing it is not required, and that is the correct position. From Abu Yusuf: it is not required. Swearing for credibility is the analogy [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 2/84].
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the chapter of the 'Ashir, the official appointed by the Imam to collect zakat from traders. It defines the 'ashir as the collector on roads, distinguishing him from the sa'i who collects zakat on livestock from tribes. The 'ashir's role includes both taking zakat and protecting traders; hence conditions are set: he must be free, Muslim, non-Hashimi (to avoid any semblance of taking zakat for his own benefit), and capable of protection. The passage then discusses the procedure when a trader claims a excuse (like the year not having elapsed, having a debt, or having paid to another 'ashir). If the trader swears, he is believed, provided he presents a certificate of discharge (bara'ah). There is a difference: according to the clearer view in al-Jami' al-Saghir, producing the certificate is not required, and Abu Yusuf agrees. The default is that the 'ashir's statement is accepted under oath, analogously to other trustees. The passage emphasizes that the 'ashir is not a mere tax collector but part of the zakat system; condemnations of 'ashirs refer only to oppressive ones.

Key Terms
العاشر (al-ʿāshir): The official appointed by the Imam to collect zakah from traders passing on roads.
الساعي (al-sāʿī): The collector who goes to the tribes to take zakat of livestock from their places.
البراءة (al-barāʾah): A certificate of discharge issued by the 'ashir confirming that zakat has been paid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is NOT a condition for the 'ashir?
A) He must be free
B) He must be a Hashimi
C) He must be Muslim
D) He must be capable of protection

Key Takeaway
The 'ashir is a trusted official whose testimony rules balance the need for collection with the trader's rights; the stronger Hanafi view accepts the oath without a certificate.

Definition and Conditions of the 'Ashshir (Road Zakat Collector)
Definition and conditions of the 'ashshir with commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of the 'ashshir and identify the conditions required for his appointment per the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The 'ashshir must be free, Muslim, non-Hashimi, and able to protect merchants.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq introduces the 'ashshir, a collector appointed by the Imam to gather zakat from merchants on the road. Understanding who qualifies for this role is crucial for proper zakat administration. The text distinguishes him from the sa'i and sets clear conditions based on Islamic legal principles.

Guided Path
1
Definition and Etymology
Identify the linguistic origin of 'ashshir (from 'ashr = ten) and its technical meaning: the Imam's appointee to collect zakat from merchants on the road. Note that the fraction taken is not always a tenth.
The term became a proper noun for the collector regardless of the actual percentage.
2
Distinguish 'Ashshir from Sa'i
Compare the 'ashshir (road for merchants) with the sa'i (goes to tribes for livestock zakat). Both are collectors but differ in location and type of wealth.
The sa'i is not required to be on a road.
3
List the Appointment Conditions
From the text: the 'ashshir must be free (hurr), Muslim, non-Hashimi (not from Banu Hashim), and capable of protection (including ability to see wealth and presence of owner).
The condition 'non-Hashimi' is because the collected goods resemble zakat, which is prohibited for Hashimis.
4
Rationale for Each Condition
A slave or non-Muslim cannot provide protection; a Hashimi cannot take what is similar to zakat. Capability implies physical ability and resources to guard the merchants.
The text also notes that the condemnation of 'ashshir in hadith applies only to unjust collectors.
5
Scope of the 'Ashshir's Duty
The 'ashshir collects both apparent wealth (livestock, crops) and hidden wealth (merchant goods) when it goes out to deserts, because then it needs protection.
This expands the 'ashshir's role beyond roadside collection.

(فتح)
نصبه الإمام على الطريق فخرج الساعي فإنه الذي يسعى في القبائل ليأخذ صدقات المواشي من أماكنها. (ط) ليأخذ الصدقات: فيه تغليب لما يؤخذ من المسلمين لكونه عبادة على ما يؤخذ من غيرهم، أي يأخذ الزكوات ويحمي التجار، وهذا فائدة نصبه، ومن ثم شرط فيه أن يكون حراً مسلماً غير هاشمي؛ لأنه لا حماية لعبد ولا كافر، وأما الهاشمي فلأن المأخوذ فيه شبهة الزكاة وأن يكون قادرا على الحماية ومنها ظهور المال وحضور المالك، وأن لا يكون مولى هاشمي وهذه شروط العاشر وهل تشترط هذه الشروط كلها في الساعي الذي يسعى في القبائل ليأخذ صدقة المواشي؟ والمصدق على وزن اسم فاعل من التفعيل اسم جنس للعاشر والساعي، والمصدق بتشديد الصاد والدال هو رب المال وما ورد من ذم العاشر محمول على من يظلم كما في زماننا وكما أنه يأخذ العاشر صدقات الأموال الظاهرة يأخذ صدقات الأموال الباطنة التي تكون مع التجار؛ لأنها تصير ظاهرة بالخروج إلى الفيافي لاحتياجها حينئذ إلى الحماية والأخذ يحمله على الحماية. (فتح)
التجار: المارين بأموالهم الظاهرة والباطنة عليه، ويحميهم من اللصوص وقطاع الطريق، ويشترط أن يكون العاشر حرا مسلما. (ط،ع)
Chapter of the Collector: i.e., explaining its rulings. Chapter of the Collector. He is the one appointed by the Imam to take the alms from the merchants. Whoever says: 'The year has not completed', or 'I have a debt', or 'I paid to another collector', and swears, is believed. The collector: surrounding me or reducing the nisab. Chapter of the Collector: He attached it to zakat because some of what he takes is zakat and it is not purely that, so he delayed it, and he placed it before rikaz because there is a meaning of worship in it. It is derived from 'I tithed the people, I tithe them, a tithe' with damma in both, when you take a tenth of their wealth. What is meant by 'tithe' is what the collector takes, whether a tenth, a quarter, or half, as it has become a proper noun for that. And a proper noun is what is placed for a concept with the condition of its presence in the mind. (Fath) 'His appointment by the Imam on the road': so excludes the sa'i who goes to the tribes to take the zakat of livestock from their places. (T) 'To take the alms': there is a preponderance of what is taken from Muslims as it is an act of worship over what is taken from others, i.e., he takes the zakat and protects the merchants, and this is the benefit of his appointment. Hence, it is required that he be free, Muslim, non-Hashimi; because a slave or disbeliever cannot protect. As for the Hashimi, because what is taken has a resemblance to zakat. And that he be capable of protection, including the appearance of wealth and the presence of the owner, and that he not be a client of a Hashimi. These are the conditions of the collector. Are all these conditions required in the sa'i who goes to the tribes to take zakat of livestock? And 'musaddiq' on the pattern of fa'il from taf'il is a generic noun for the collector and sa'i. And 'musaddiq' with shadda on sad and dal is the owner of the wealth. Whatever has been reported condemning the collector is applied to the one who oppresses, as in our time. And just as the collector takes the zakat of apparent wealth, he also takes the zakat of hidden wealth that is with merchants because it becomes apparent by going out to the deserts since they need protection then, and the taking obliges him to protect. (Fath) 'The merchants': those passing by with their apparent and hidden wealth, and he protects them from thieves and highway robbers. And it is required that the collector be free and Muslim. (T, A)
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is a definition and conditions ruling within the chapter on the collector ('ashshir). The author first explains why this chapter is placed after zakat but before rikaz: because the collector's function is not purely zakat (he also takes from non-Muslims) but has a resemblance to worship. The term 'ashshir is derived from taking a tenth, but here it applies regardless of the fraction. The commentary then distinguishes the 'ashshir from the sa'i: the former is stationed on roads for merchants, the latter goes to tribes for livestock. The conditions for appointment are: free, Muslim, non-Hashimi, and capable of protection. The Hashimi exclusion is because what is taken has a resemblance to zakat, which is forbidden for them. The passage also clarifies that the disparagement of 'ashshirs in hadith refers to unjust ones, not those who act lawfully. Finally, it notes that the 'ashshir protects both apparent and hidden wealth of merchants.

Key Terms
العاشر (al-‘āshshir): The collector appointed by the Imam to take zakat from merchants on the road, protecting them in exchange.
الساعي (as-sā‘ī): The agent who goes to tribes to take zakat of livestock from their places.
المصدق (al-muṣaddiq): A generic noun for both the 'āshshir and sā‘ī; also the owner of wealth (with shadda on ṣād and dāl).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) He must be a disbeliever to deal with merchants fairly.

Key Takeaway
The 'ashshir is a road zakat collector whose appointment requires freedom, Islam, non-Hashimi descent, and protective capability.

Believing the Merchant's Claims in Zakat: Excuses and Exceptions
Rulings on merchant's denials of zakat obligation and when he is believed with oath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the excuses that negate zakat obligation, identify when the merchant is believed upon oath, and distinguish the exception for livestock.

Core Idea
A merchant's claim negating zakat obligation is believed with oath, but livestock zakat cannot be privately paid.

When a merchant denies any zakat obligation, the collector must decide whether to accept his claim. The Hanafi school lays out a clear framework: if the merchant provides a valid excuse that would eliminate the obligation, his word is taken with an oath. However, certain claims, like private payment of livestock zakat, are not accepted. This lesson unpacks the excuses, the evidentiary rules, and the exception.

Guided Path
1
State the general principle
The collector's authority to collect depends on the obligation of zakat. If the merchant claims something that negates the obligation, the claim relates to the condition of authority.
This principle is the basis for accepting the merchant's word.
2
List the valid excuses
The merchant can claim: incomplete year, no trade intent, wealth is not his (deposit, mudarabah, etc.), or having a debt. These excuses deny the existence of the obligation.
The debt excuse is general and includes any debt that reduces the nisab.
3
Understand the dispute on written discharge
Some require a written discharge (al-bara'ah) for the claim to be accepted, but the correct Hanafi view (from al-Jami' al-Saghir) is that it is not required. The merchant is believed upon oath alone.
Imam Abu Yusuf agrees.
4
Identify the livestock exception
If the merchant claims he paid zakat on livestock directly to the poor, he is not believed. Reason: Livestock zakat is apparent wealth; the right of collection belongs to the state, so private payment does not discharge the obligation.
This is an exception to the general rule.
5
Analyze the qiyas
The ruling that the merchant is believed with oath is based on qiyas: since the condition of obligation is within the merchant's knowledge, his claim is accepted just like other claims about hidden matters. The oath confirms his truthfulness.
This qiyas is mentioned in Tabyin al-Haqa'iq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

'Whoever says etc.': Know that the condition for the authority to take is the obligation of zakat; so everything whose existence drops [the obligation], so the ruling is likewise when he claims it. For instance, if he says: 'The year has not completed', he denies the obligation; similarly if he says: 'I did not intend trade' or 'This wealth is not mine, rather it is a deposit, or merchandise, or mudarabah, or I am a hired hand in it, or I have a debt owed to people', or says: 'There is no alms in this wealth' even if he does not explain the reason. Commentary
This passage is a ruling on when a merchant's denial of zakat obligation is accepted. The general principle: if the merchant claims an excuse that would drop the obligation (like incomplete year, no trade intent, wealth is not his own, or debt), he is believed upon oath. This is because he knows his own affairs best. The text clarifies that 'debt' includes any debt that reduces the nisab, not only surrounding debt. The claim of paying to another collector is believed only if that other collector is verified for that year. The author notes a dispute: according to some, a written discharge is required; but the correct view (from al-Jami' al-Saghir) is that it is not required, and Abu Yusuf agrees. The analogy (qiyas) supports belief with oath. An exception is livestock: if the merchant claims he paid the zakat himself directly to the poor, he is not believed because livestock zakat is typically collected by the state. The final sentence notes that the dhimmi is believed in the same claims as a Muslim, but a harbi is not (though this will be detailed in the next lesson).

Key Terms
البراءة (al-barā’ah): A letter of acquittance or discharge proving payment of zakat.
السوائم (as-sawā’im): Livestock that graze freely, on which zakat is due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) When he claims he paid zakat on livestock directly to the poor.
D) When he claims he did not intend trade.

Key Takeaway
A merchant's valid excuses negating zakat are accepted upon oath, except for private payment of livestock zakat.

Rulings for Dhimmi, Harbi, and Special Cases
Rulings on 'ushr from non-Muslims and special cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the 'ushr rates for Muslims, dhimmis, and harbis, explain the reciprocity condition for harbis, and apply the Hanafi position on disputed cases like the dhimmi's claim of payment.

Core Idea
The 'ushr rate varies by status: Muslim 2.5%, dhimmi 5%, harbi 10%—but for harbi, only if they tax us similarly.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq details the 'ashshir's collection rules, distinguishing between Muslim, dhimmi, and harbi merchants. It also addresses special cases like wine and the acknowledgment of umm walad, and a dispute with al-Shafi'i over the dhimmi's claim of having paid his due. Understanding these nuances is essential for applying the rules of trade tax in an Islamic state.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rates for each category
From the passage, extract the fixed fractions: from Muslims, quarter of a tenth (2.5%); from dhimmis, double that (5%); from harbis, a full tenth (10%), but with conditions.
Note that the dhimmi rate is exactly double the Muslim rate.
2
Understand the reciprocity condition for harbi
The harbi's tenth is only taken if their state also imposes a similar tax on our merchants. If we do not know their rate, we take a tenth (based on 'Umar's instruction). If we know their rate, we match it. If they do not tax us, we take nothing. If they tax us at a rate higher than tenth, we still leave enough for the merchant to reach safety.
This principle is based on fairness and is derived from 'Umar's practice.
3
Apply the rule for unknown rates
If we do not know what rate the harbi state imposes, we take a full tenth, following the statement of 'Umar: 'If you are unable, then a tenth.'
This is a default when information is lacking.
4
Analyze the dispute with al-Shafi'i
Al-Shafi'i holds that a dhimmi who claims he paid his 'ushr to a poor Muslim is believed because he delivered the right to its due recipient. The Hanafi school responds that apparent wealth (like trade goods) must be paid to the state collector; private payment does not discharge the liability, similar to the case of jizya or a minor's debt.
The Hanafi position emphasizes public authority over private charity.
5
Note special rulings: wine and umm walad
For wine: from a dhimmi, take half a tenth of its value; from a harbi, a tenth of its value. For umm walad: if a harbi claims a slave girl is his umm walad, his acknowledgment is accepted because lineage acknowledgment is valid even from a harbi.
These rulings show the application of general principles to specific cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

His umm walad. And he took from us a quarter of a tenth, and from the dhimmi double that, and from the harbi a tenth on condition of nisab and their taking from us. And he did not repeat within a year without return. And the tenth of wine. In paying it himself [i.e., he is not believed in this claim even if he swears, rather it is taken from him again, and he is believed in the remaining situations. (T, A)] And al-Shafi'i said: He is believed because he delivered the right to its due recipient. And for us: the taking of the right for the rulers in apparent wealth cannot be invalidated, like the jizya and the debt of a minor if the debtor paid him, for the guardian can take it again. (Mukhtasar) 'The dhimmi is believed': because he is in our territory like a Muslim in transactions and their rulings, except that he is not believed in jizya if he says: 'I paid it.' (A)] Because what is taken from them is double what is taken from Muslims, so its conditions must be observed to actualize the doubling, except if he says: 'I paid it to the poor of the dhimma in the city,' then he is not believed; because what is taken is jizya, and they are not recipients of it. If he disburses it to the interests of Muslims, he has no authority to do that. (Fath) 'His umm walad': if a slave girl was with him and he says: 'This is my umm walad,' he is believed because his acknowledgment of lineage of one in his possession is valid, and being a harbi does not negate causing birth. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 125/1] 'Condition of nisab and their taking from us': this statement is of the type of laf wa nashr marattab. So his word 'condition of nisab' is related to his words 'and he took from us and from the dhimmi', and his words 'and their taking from us' relates to his words 'and from the harbi', i.e., we take a tenth from him on condition that they take a tenth from us. So if a harbi passes by with fifty dirhams or two hundred dirhams, nothing is taken from him unless they take from us the like. In Kitab al-Zakat: nothing is taken from a small amount even if they take from us the like. If he passes by with a nisab and we do not know how much they take from us, we take a tenth from him due to the statement of 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him): 'If you are unable, then a tenth.' If we know that they take from us a quarter of a tenth or half a tenth, we take the equivalent. If they do not take from us, we take nothing from them, because we are more deserving of noble traits. If they take all, we do not take all, rather we leave with him what brings him to safety. (Miskin and others) 'Nisab': i.e., on condition that his wealth reaches nisab, so nothing is taken from a small amount even if they take from us the like. (T, A) 'From us': if they do not take from us, we take nothing from him; if they take all, we do not take all, rather we leave with him what takes him to his place of safety. (T) 'And he did not repeat': i.e., the collector does not take a second tenth from the harbi. (T) 'Without return to dar al-harb': if he returns and then comes out, a second tenth is taken, because by returning the aman (safe conduct) ends, and he receives a new aman when he enters dar al-harb and then comes out. (A) 'Wine': i.e., from the dhimmi, half of a tenth of the value of wine if he passes by the collector, and from the harbi a tenth of the value. (A, T)
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage covers additional rulings on the 'ashshir's collection. First, the case of umm walad (a slave-mother of her master's child): if a harbi merchant claims a slave girl with him is his umm walad, he is believed, because acknowledgment of parentage is valid even from a harbi. Then the passage explains the amounts taken: from Muslims, a quarter of a tenth (2.5%); from dhimmis, double that (5%); from harbis, a tenth (10%). However, the harbi's tithe is conditioned on reciprocity: we only take if their rulers take from our merchants similarly. The text details how to handle unknown rates: if unknown, take a tenth based on 'Umar's instruction. If they take all our merchandise, we still leave enough for the merchant to reach safety. Next, the rule that a harbi is not tithed twice within the same year unless he returns to dar al-harb and re-enters our territory with a new aman. Finally, the ruling on wine: from dhimmis, we take half the tenth of its value; from harbis, a tenth of the value. The passage also revisits the earlier dispute with al-Shafi'i regarding payment of livestock, reinforcing the Hanafi position that apparent wealth must be paid to the state collector, and private payment does not discharge the obligation.

Key Terms
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who bears her master's child, thereby becoming free upon his death.
الجزية (al-jizyah): Poll tax levied on non-Muslim subjects in an Islamic state.
العشر (al-'ushr): The tithe, a 10% tax on trade goods from harbi, or 5% from dhimmi, or 2.5% from Muslim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The harbi's wealth reaches nisab
B) The harbi state also takes 'ushr from our merchants
C) The harbi is a Muslim
D) The harbi passes through with trade goods

Key Takeaway
The 'ushr rate depends on the merchant's status, and the harbi's rate is reciprocal; the state collector's authority is absolute for apparent wealth.
